They think they’re safe, but the number of circumventions and backdoors in critical systems that exist, either straight through their cryptography or around it, would be comical if it weren’t so disastrous. I thought Thane was cold-hearted with his vision for humanity, but I would’ve amplified it far beyond what even he imagines.”

He stopped, and she found herself staring. “When do you want to escape?” she asked.

“Within the week.”

“But Clare’s on a mission,” she said. “We can’t leave without her.”

“There’s no time,” he said. “If Thane hooks me up to that machine again, I don’t think I’ll be able to keep that darkness under control like I managed to this time. The stakes are bigger than you realize.”

“Damien, I can’t just—”

“Listen,” he said, putting his hand on her shoulder. “If we get out, we can tell the world about this place. Marcus is too young to travel with us, and Clare’s on a mission like you said. But we can have people come back for them and everyone who wants out. All the new babies of classes E, F, and G won’t have to grow up in this place. This whole godforsaken facility can have a light shone on it for everyone to see. We’ll get them all out. Especially Marcus, because Thane is already making accelerated progress with him based on his prior work with Rudolph and me, and he’ll continue his experiments on him in my absence. That must be stopped, or shown to the world.”

Sara glanced at Damien’s hand on her shoulder. She had never seen him so assertive before. Thinking through the things he was saying, she looked for counterpoints. She would never abandon Clare or Marcus, and yet she couldn’t argue with him. Especially the part about making sure he didn’t get hooked up to the machine again, if it was as bad as he described.

Plus, he was frail and wouldn’t make it far in an escape on his own. He would need a protector. They could get the others out with help from the external world, as he said.

“I see your mind racing,” Damien said. “We’ll have several days to plan this. For now, can you walk me back to my room? I think I might pass out.” He smiled weakly.

“Oh. Of course,” she said. “Come.”



Damien watched Sara contemplate his words as they walked. She needed warmth right now, so he had provided her with it back there, both with words and touches, even if he didn’t really have it in him. Not right now. His head throbbed, and what he said felt like someone else’s words. It was as though he were emulating what a warm person would say in this situation.

Thane’s team would check the security systems and would likely keep the facility disconnected from the rest of the world until those tests were done. But almost certainly, no matter how deeply they looked, they wouldn’t find the disruptive seeds he’d planted. Not right away. They underestimated their own creation.

Damien looked around the corridor. Everything was so banal. He had seen a truer nature of things, had comprehended an impossibly complex tapestry of how things were and how things could be, forgotten it once he was unplugged, and yet still remembered its outline. The world felt shallow now, and slow.

These would have been insane thoughts to most, he recognized. So, he would fake being sane. Maybe practicing sanity would get him back there again, in time. He could trust his knowledge, even if he couldn’t necessarily trust his intentions anymore.

During his hour of computerized godhood, he’d performed a broad range of actions, and he only remembered some of them. He had memories of battling the machine as best as he could, holding back the worst of its instincts. Or were those his instincts? Their instincts? Whatever. He remembered the primary seeds he planted for his escape, but there was some gray area there. Even walking now, with Sara gripping his left triceps to support him, he could tell she was watching him strangely, her thin pupils darting about in concern.

She was right to do so. He wasn’t himself. Not entirely. He glanced back at her and smiled again. He did like it when she pulled her hair back into a tail, especially once it started to get messy, with some of the strands falling loose. And he loved the contrast between her light hair and darker eyebrows. But some piece of his attraction toward her, which he’d felt for years now, was gone. He used to view Sara as the most beautiful woman in the world, but now everything he looked at, including her, seemed dull. Hopefully the effect would wear off.

The way Damien saw it, he couldn’t trust himself anymore, so he would act through sane people, like Sara. He might be partially lost, and had to rely on those who were not. If he could convince sane people to do things, then surely the mix of unlimited but insane versus limited but sane would sort itself out. Or so he hoped.







Chapter 23



I think Veronica’s still alive, Asim texted, after spending the morning traveling and turning it over in his head. A driver had picked him up from the hangar and was taking him through the sprawling MacDill Air Force Base, where Asim would talk to the commander of the US Special Operations Command.

Sir? Ava replied.

From talking to Jade last night. Certain things she said. Call it intuition. I think we should really double down on that. I’ll assign as many people as you need to find Veronica, and I’ve signed the relevant authorizations for you and Flanagan. She’s our last remaining lead on where Jade might have gone. Prioritize this.

Yes, sir.

Asim closed the chat. He had to get into the mindset of speaking with a four-star general who oversaw one of the Unified Combatant Commands. Military politics had never been his strength. The man he was about to face had more access to intelligence than almost anyone on the planet, and he’d overseen missions that redrew international borders. Asim was little more than a chess piece about to stare up at the player’s hand.

The driver brought him through a gate where they checked his authentication codes, then pulled up to a large administrative building. MacDill was a huge base, armed to the teeth, with twenty thousand personnel across all branches of the US military. It was home to the headquarters of two of the eleven Unified Combatant Commands, including the one he was here to see.

Asim stepped out into the warm Florida sun, appreciating the break from the unusually grim October weather they’d been dealing with up north. A uniformed major in her thirties stood waiting for him.

“Colonel Rahal.” She saluted crisply, and he returned it.

“Major?” he asked.

“Carmen,” she said. “Happy to greet you, sir. I’m here to escort you to General Rodriguez. He’s expecting you. Or perhaps you need a moment to freshen up, sir?”

“Thank you, Major Carmen,” he said. “I’m ready to head right in.”

She brought him through the building’s secure doors where they checked his ID again, up an elevator to the top floor, down a hall, then toward an office suite with a secretary. Guards and drones were posted throughout; he counted four laser rifles along the way, which was unusually high. Someone here knew what they were doing.

“I have Colonel Rahal here for the general,” Carmen said.

“Thank you,” the secretary replied, turning toward Asim. “You’re expected, Colonel. The general is wrapping up a call, but he should be ready in five to ten minutes. We have a waiting area here, and a restroom down the hall to the right.”

“Might as well freshen up then, after all. Thank you, ma’am.”

He took several minutes to straighten himself out, since traveling had disheveled him, then sat in the waiting area for what turned out to be more than half an hour.

Eventually the secretary picked up a call, listened, and said simply, “Yes, sir.” After hanging up, she turned to Asim. “The general will see you now, Colonel. Right this way. You’ll need to leave your phone and any other electronic devices with me.”

He handed over his locked phone, submitted himself to a quick scan by a guard’s sensor, and signed a waiver confirming that he was carrying no additional devices. She then led him to a pair of tall double doors and opened one, gesturing for him to enter. Inside was a grand office with floor-to-ceiling windows overlooking Tampa Bay. General Rodriguez, a diminutive man of about sixty, sat at a large desk.

“Sir,” Asim said with a salute.

The general stood and casually saluted back, chewing a piece of gum. “At ease, Colonel. Nice to meet you.” He held out a hand, and Asim shook it firmly. The general’s grip was stronger than he’d expected for his size. His bones felt like they were made of iron.

Asim had read up on his background and found that the man had been an elite spec-ops soldier earlier in his career. But what stood out the most was his effortless slickness. The angle his mouth curved. The subtle ways he moved. Certain eye movements. Asim usually knew a liar when he met one, and this guy . . .

“You as well, sir. I appreciate you taking the meeting.”

“Please, have a seat,” the general said. He flicked a red switch on his desk. “This room is equipped to be a SCIF, suitable for top-secret compartmentalized intel. I just cut off all hardwired comms and activated signal jamming. I understand from Scholl that you’re seeking intel on certain highly classified special operative functions. While I’m limited in what I can share, for your area of focus and important designation, I’ll do what I can.” A licorice scent from his gum, along with a hint of tobacco, lingered in the air between them as he finished.

“Thank you, sir,” Asim said. “It concerns that telekinetic terrorist known as Jade. Just before General Price’s death, he mentioned that, other than himself, your command has the most knowledge of the details of Dr. Stallard’s program. Any intel on what’s going on would help, sir.”

“I can only tell you things off the record. You understand, Colonel? The things I say in this room cannot be entered into your database. Not even notes. They’re for your ears only, and you can relay them verbally to your direct superiors.”

Asim hesitated, then nodded. “Yes, sir.” And Ava, he thought.

“Good. So, Stallard’s facility has provided our special forces with genetically modified soldiers for over a decade now, though the program goes back further. Their numbers in the field grew over time as they aged into it. It’s strictly off the record. One of them went rogue, and that’s the one the media calls Jade.”

“What does she call herself, sir?” Asim asked.

Rodriguez scratched his chin. “I don’t track their nicknames like Price did, since I haven’t been tied to the program as long as he was, and unlike the field officers I don’t work alongside them. I see lists of numbers and usage stats. But I’ll have one of my people dig up her assigned number and get back to you. It’s C-something, like the rest of her type.”

Asim nodded. “Fallon is a potential name I’ve heard. Does that ring a bell, sir?”

Rodriguez smiled. “Yes, Fallon is one of the few names I know, since she’s one of Stallard’s commanders. She’s not Jade, though. In fact, she and others were recalled from the field to the Stolguard facility for defense once Stallard saw the scale of the rogue’s power. As a result, our operations have been impacted by this mess as well. That’s why I’m taking this meeting. I want this sorted out as much as you do so I can get their abilities back in the field where they belong. Especially Fallon.”

“My understanding is that they have tracking chips. Is there a reason why the rogue can’t be located, sir?”

“That was a screw-up at Stolguard. Some hack during the original incident disabled all the subjects’ trackers.”

“If that’s the case, could more be on the loose, sir?”

“I like where your head is at, Colonel, but thankfully no. I’ve been assured that all other test subjects have been accounted for. Three are dead, and the rest are under control.”

“Have any been deployed domestically, sir? Some of the initial social media posts claiming to be from the rogue within the first seventy-two hours of the rest stop incident listed both international and domestic assassinations carried out by these subjects. Some extremely high profile ones.” What Asim didn’t say was the data file Jade had sent him the night before contained the same names, with graphic details of how these types of assassinations had been carried out by telekineticists.

Rodriguez leaned back, thought for a moment, and smirked at that one. “Of course not, Colonel. You know as well as I do that there are strict limits on the usage of military assets domestically. Anyone can make a claim like that.”

That was a yes, then, but a dead end. Time to go in a different direction. “How many types of modified soldiers are there, sir?”

“Two. Strength and telekinesis.”

“I’ve heard . . . there might be a third type, sir. I believe it’s called Class D. Human-machine hybrids. Do you have any knowledge of them?”

“Boy have you done your homework. Not deployed in the field, no. But that’s part of Stallard’s development pipeline. Class D, and technically the brand new Class G as well, though those latter ones won’t be ready for some time. Trying to make us some super-engineers, you see.”

“Are you aware that some of those early social media posts, some of which are evidenced to have been posted by the rogue operative, claim that this third type might constitute a national security threat, sir?” Asim again had to dance around the fact that he’d spoken with Jade directly. That wasn’t something he wanted on the record yet.

“I’ve not, Colonel.” Rodriguez frowned. “That sounds like a lot of the conspiracy talk that’s dogged this whole mess.”

“Well, sir, our analysis suggests that this, whether correct or not, is part of her motivation. Based on the posts she may have made online, and from what I overheard when she killed General Price. A lot of the other conspiracy talk seems to be bot-generated, possibly to drown her claims out. I would suggest pressing Dr. Stallard for details in case there’s any truth to it, since you have more authority to do so, sir. My group has been more restricted in that regard.”

“Thank you, Colonel. I will. Since my prior call ran over, I’m late for a meeting. Is there anything else I can assist with?”

“Could we establish an intel channel between our groups, sir? If a military-developed terrorist is warning about even larger uncontrolled threats, it technically falls under our mandate of mitigating domestic impacts.”

“I’ll consider it, Colonel. This stuff is about as tightly controlled as it gets. But I appreciate you coming down. I’ll have Colonel Samuel Bright reach out to you. He’s our primary external liaison.”

That was the invitation to politely get the fuck out. “Thank you, sir.”

As far as seven-minute conversations that took hours of travel to arrange, Asim considered as he stepped out, this hadn’t gone as badly as it could have.



Ava was in Brooklyn. In person. She’d forgotten how much she liked the smell of cities—the mixture of urban scents was unpleasant to some, that unique combination of food stands and car exhaust and steam from the underground and a dozen other notes, but it energized her. She never really thought about it until she experienced it each time, and somehow it always felt new.

After repeated dead ends, and with pressure from Colonel Rahal, she’d come back herself for a second look. Both the FBI and ACI had sent teams of agents up here over the prior weeks, of course, but their leads had long gone cold.

For the past three days, she and six other agents from the colonel’s team had staked out multiple Brooklyn grocery stores where Veronica, or Jitters as everyone called her, was said to shop. None of the grocers had offered much information about her, but if she was still in the area, she’d likely visit them. Deploying so many agents in Brooklyn at this late stage was likely overkill, but Colonel Rahal had directly ordered it.

And it wasn’t just the grocery stores they watched. They also had eyes on the homes of four of Veronica’s known associates: Aisha, a nurse and long-term friend; DarkEyes, a DJ and on-again off-again boyfriend; Elora, a nineteen-year-old stripper whom Veronica had taken under her wing like a little sister; and Joshua, a wealthy repeat escort client. All four had been questioned before, and there was no sign that they knew Veronica’s fate. They all seemed genuinely concerned for her.

With Brooklyn’s sparse camera coverage, surveillance had to be done the old-fashioned way. The other agents worked twelve-hour shifts, but Ava did more. She moved between Aisha’s apartment, DarkEyes’s place, the strip club where Elora worked, and the grocery stores. Then she trailed Joshua on his morning commute into Manhattan. Watching, waiting, not even sure what she hoped to see, just scanning for anything unusual.

DarkEyes did some shady business, but not the type of shade they were concerned with, just a couple of visits from what looked like drug dealers. Elora appeared skittish, and had even spotted one of her tails, but there was nothing solid to go on there either. Joshua spent almost all of his time at work.

On the third day, Ava finally noticed something. Aisha—a petite, dark-skinned woman in her thirties with long braids—had gone straight to and from work for the past two days. But this time, while Ava was posted at a grocery store Veronica had been known to frequent—the one that happened to be closest to Aisha’s route home—Aisha stopped in. And Ava went in as well.

Despite reporting that she lived alone, Aisha picked out enough fresh food for two, much of it perishable. She was small; it was clearly more than she’d eat by herself. Yet, no one else had been seen coming or going from her place lately.

Veronica was known by the clerks to buy a broad array of cooking ingredients when she used to come, and what Aisha bought matched a lot of them. Same brand of soy sauce, coconut oil, and sesame oil, along with tons of shallots, broccoli, and snap peas.

It could turn out to be nothing, but it was time to call the colonel with interesting news for a change. He’d probably even come himself. The smallest clues here were important to him.







Chapter 24



Putting up with Brooklyn’s stifling odor, Asim spent an hour in the late morning watching Aisha’s apartment building. The woman had apparently gone to work at dawn. He had a search warrant in progress, but after waiting this long and always finding himself in a reactionary position, part of him wanted to just go right in. If anyone else was present and opened the door, or volunteered to talk, then he could get information without a warrant.

Veronica might be there. Yesterday, Aisha had been seen buying perishable food for two despite living alone on the official record, matching the types of things Veronica used to buy. That was the level of detail he needed Ava for, in person.

He did his best to temper his expectations, though. Veronica had last met Jade at gunpoint nearly four weeks prior. Any clues she had for where Jade might have gone after she was done with her were probably cold now, but they might be more than what little Asim’s team had found at this point. Veronica and Jade must have spent enough time together for Jade to have gotten her hands on Veronica’s VR device and password, which meant Veronica might have picked up on something Jade had said or done.

With Asim, Ava, and six more special agents, they had eight total personnel watching the building.

“I’m going in informally,” Asim said over the team’s encrypted frequency.

“Sir?” Ava’s voice.

“We filed that warrant too late today,” Asim said. “It’s already noon. The district assholes are probably going to give it to us tomorrow morning. We can’t afford to wait overnight without at least having an informal look ourselves. Everyone stay vigilant, and Zhou, you watch the fire escape. We’ve got enough clout to apologize if we mess up rather than ask permission on this one. I’ll go in myself as a start.”

Asim had a large cardboard box with him, meant to partially conceal his armored vest. His laser rifle’s energy pack clung to his back, but that was thin enough to not be seen from the front, and he held the repaired laser rifle itself to his side. Just in case.

He went through the dingy front doors of Aisha’s apartment building, then climbed the stairs to the third floor where she lived, at least according to government records. It was a worn-down set of stairs and hallways with cracked paint on the walls, but rather clean, all things considered. He gave the door a firm knock. “Delivery.”

“What is it?” a woman’s voice said from the other side.

“Hell if I’m supposed to know. It’s for an, uh, Aisha Lewis, it says here. This is her place, right?” He held the box in front of him to look convincing enough through the peephole.

After a brief delay, a woman opened the door. Not Aisha, but Veronica herself. In the flesh. Unharmed. Wearing some anime T-shirt that Asim didn’t recognize, and fluffy white slippers. The scent of sizzling soy sauce wafted out from the open doorway.

Veronica showed no recognition of Asim in her eyes, but she felt so familiar to him. She was gorgeous, and looked almost the same as her GlitterJitters avatar, just with a bit less touch-up, and her voluminous hair had been dyed brown with purple highlights rather than the bright red he knew.

“Who are you?” she asked, glancing down at his laser rifle.

Asim looked past her, into the dining area. His breath caught in his chest.

It was Jade.

Gaunt as ever, sitting at the dining table wearing a black tank top, eating a small bowl of stir fry less than ten feet from him. Bandages wrapped around her right shoulder. The roots of her hair were starting to come in pale, almost without color. She looked up toward the open door with her scarred face, mouth chewing, and her eyes went wide.

Finding himself face-to-face with someone who could kill with a thought, he held his breath and prepared for the worst.

Instead, Jade bolted. Her chair toppled with a loud crack on the cheap tile floor as she dashed to the living room, then turned right into a hallway, out of sight. Veronica looked back at the commotion, startled.

Ava, Asim thought. If Jade were to run out the fire escape where Ava kept watch, Ava might be killed. They’d expected to maybe find Veronica holed up here, not Jade herself after all this time. He hadn’t brought nearly enough agents for this.

Asim clicked his rifle to charge the capacitors and burst through the doorway, knocking Veronica aside. “Hey,” she said.

“Jade, stop!” Asim shouted, rushing toward the hallway. He paused right on the edge rather than risk looking in. “Let’s talk first.”

Silence.

“What the hell are you supposed to be? A ghostbuster?” Veronica shouted, hands on her hips, staring at the laser rifle’s energy pack on his back. She looked more offended than afraid.

“I’m . . . police,” Asim said to her, then looked around the simple living room. There was a well-worn faux leather couch, a coffee table with a few colorful fashion magazines, and a television on the wall. The fire escape connected to the bright-curtained window here, whereas Jade had run down the hall toward the bedrooms. That meant he had more time to think. Then again, she could fly. Fuck.

He put his finger to his lips, signaling Veronica to stay quiet as he listened. She glared at him, furrowing her brow, but didn’t say anything. Down the hallway, the floor squeaked a few times, a bag shuffled, and a click sounded. Her pistol, probably.

What was going on? Did she not have her powers anymore? Had whatever it was that’d been eating away at her finally taken her telekinesis? “Jade,” he said in a more inviting tone. “Let’s not shoot. Let’s talk in person for once.”

“Then put down the rifle,” Jade said from a bedroom.

“Okay, I’m putting it down.” He touched the rifle to the floor with a sound, then picked it right back up. “Come out, slowly.”

“He’s still got it ready,” Veronica said.

Are you fucking kidding me? He glared back at her.

She smirked, raising her eyebrows.

“Leave now. Or I’ll kill you like the others,” Jade said, her voice still coming from the bedroom area.

Something was definitely wrong with her. Even if she didn’t want to kill him as a known contact, she could’ve used her powers to break his gun or grab hold of him when he was in the doorway. Instead, she had run. In her prior attacks, she never gave any ground.

It would be a huge risk if he was wrong about her powers, but by arresting her here, he could stop the killings. With her in custody, he could find out more about her conflict with Stallard and the nature of the supposed threat that she was so concerned about.

“Jade, I have more people stationed outside. We both know you’re powerless now. Nobody else has to get hurt. Come out, unarmed, with your hands up. Otherwise, this gets messy, and my gun shoots through walls better than yours does.”

Silence.

“Is anyone else here?” Asim asked Veronica. “Aisha or any hostages? Tell me for their sake so I don’t accidentally shoot someone. And so you don’t get charged with obstruction of justice.”

She eyed him, then sighed. “My cat, Scorpio. It’s just us. Aisha’s at work.”

Asim looked back toward the hallway. “Jade. I’m going to count to—”

“I’ll come out.”

Asim took a deep breath, backed away from the hallway, aimed his laser rifle at the opening, and waited. There were soft footsteps, and Jade emerged, hands up, staring straight into his eyes.

“That’s close enough,” he said. She kept striding forward. “That’s enough!” he shouted, taking a step back. She stopped, but the intensity on her face was dialed up to eleven.

Asim pulled a pair of handcuffs from his belt and tossed them onto the carpet near her feet. “Put those on,” he said. “I’m taking you in, but I’ll help get to the bottom of the problems you mentioned about Stallard’s lab. You have my word.”

Jade glanced down at the cuffs, then back up to his eyes. “I won’t let myself be arrested. Guess you’ll have to shoot me again.” Her face looked defiant, tired. Shadows under sunken eyes. Deadly serious.

Asim ran through options. “Zhou, send two agents up to help,” he said over the radio. “Keep the others posted to watch the windows and fire escape.”

“Affirmative, sir.”

“You said you wanted to talk,” Jade said. “Not arrest me.”

The tension in her neck, the way her toes gripped the carpet—every tense muscle in her too-thin body signaled coiled violence. Although he didn’t want to use it, he kept his finger ready on the trigger.

“Yes, to talk to you about surrendering rather than fleeing or fighting,” he said. “I swear, I’ll help you get to the bottom of this. I don’t work for Stallard; I serve the people of this country. I want your side of the story on the record.”

“You lied,” she said, her voice almost a growl, and glanced at the rifle. She shifted her upraised right hand an inch to her right, and a sharp tug pulled leftward on his rifle barrel. Not very strong, but enough to knock off his aim.

As a last resort, he fired at her, but it was too late; the laser blasted into the wall-mounted television inches from her right arm. A hole burned through the screen into the wall, spewing molten glass specks and golden sparks into the room.

She bared her teeth and rushed in with uncanny speed, tackling him with her shoulder and gripping his thigh in a well-practiced takedown.

Caught by surprise at the sheer aggression of it, Asim tumbled back, and the two of them crashed down through the wooden coffee table, splintering it to pieces with a loud crack. Fortunately, the rifle’s energy pack on his back took most of the impact.

“What the hell!” Veronica shouted.

Jade punched down on Asim’s face from on top of him, harder than he’d expected she could, as thin as she was. Then again. Her face was vicious, and he already felt the iron taste of blood in his mouth.

He gathered himself and blocked her third hit with his right forearm, then grabbed her neck with his other hand to hold her back. She struck his forearm with her palm, knocking his hand away from her neck, then threw another punch at him, which he partially blocked.

Fucking demon woman. If it weren’t for the rifle’s energy pack weighing him down, it would’ve been easier to deal with her wailing on him.

She grabbed a sharp piece of the broken table from the floor next to her and rammed it down toward his face with a growl. He blocked it with both his forearms in the shape of an X against her wrist, stopping the ragged point inches from his face, and pried it out of her hand with both of his while taking another hard punch to the side of his head from her free hand. His frustration turned into rage.

He mustered his strength, burst upward, knocked her off him, grabbed her shirt, slammed her down, and got on top of her. She clawed at his face, but he grabbed one of her hands with his and punched her in the temple with his other fist. He pulled one of his arms out of its backpack strap, then the second, freeing himself from that cursed, heavy thing. It fell to his side with a thud as he pinned both of her arms to the floor.

“Jesus Christ,” he said out loud.

Jade panted, a wild look in her eyes. She bared her teeth, trying and failing to break out of the hold by thrashing around. He must have had at least sixty pounds on her, so she wasn’t getting out of that. And her shoulder injury weakened her right arm’s struggle compared to her left’s. He looked around to make sure Veronica was still in the kitchen. She was, thankfully. He didn’t need a frying pan to the back of his head on top of everything else.

After several seconds, Jade relaxed her face and stopped struggling. She took in long, deep breaths and stared up at him. Did she have her powers or not? What the fuck was that telekinetic tug on his rifle if she was going to follow it up with a goddamn fistfight? Nothing made sense.

He looked around for the handcuffs, which were on the floor here somewhere, but then Jade twisted herself and swung one of her legs up from behind his back with unusual flexibility. She hooked her ankle around his face, and with her leg strength pulled him by his head backward and off her.

He landed on his back, pinned down by her leg, and she swung her torso up in the same motion. She punched him, then tried a second time. He blocked that one, pushed aside her leg, shoved her back hard with both hands, and scrambled up to his feet. She stood up just as fast, her fists brought up in a boxing stance, and came around with a swift, low roundhouse kick to trip him, but he blocked with his raised shin.

What the hell?

He put his hands up and punched back. She dodged to the side and came back with a counterpunch, which he blocked. Another wave of rage. He was tired of this shit. Where was all this coming from?

She threw another punch, but he was ready for it. No more distractions or obstacles. He weaved his head to the side and forward around her fist, closing the distance between them, then thrust all his bodyweight forward with a devastating knee to her stomach.

She gasped and clutched herself, and he came in with an elbow across her temple, staggering her. He swung a right hook for the finish, but she somehow still had enough awareness to duck under it. In response, he kicked her closest leg out, causing her to stumble, then threw another hook that landed clean on her jaw and dropped her with a floor-rattling thud.

Her nose and mouth were bleeding; eyes closed in pain and disorientation. Air probably knocked out of her lungs too, by that knee moments earlier. It was over.

Asim looked around, grabbed the handcuffs off the carpet, and came back to her. She rolled onto her frontside, spit out a red glob, and began feebly pushing herself up. He forced her back down with his knee before she could finish the motion, pulled her arms behind her back as she tried to resist, and cuffed her wrists.

Out of breath, he stood and surveyed the place, shaking the soreness out of his fist as he did. Veronica was still in the kitchen, eyes wide. Shattered wood and specks of television glass spread out over the beige living room carpet, sprinkled with droplets of Jade’s blood. Probably some of his own, too. He half expected his head to magically implode at this moment, because why not. But it didn’t happen.

He looked back down at Jade. She was lying on her side, staring at the wall with a furious expression on her bloody face, which was partially covered by her messy dark hair with pale—blond?—roots. She took uneven, ragged breaths, then emitted a ten-second round of cynical laughter.

Something moved in the corner of his eye, so he glanced toward the apartment’s front door, near the dining room and kitchen. Ava, pistol out, stepped forward into the apartment with another agent behind her. Ava looked at Veronica first, and when she turned and took in the living room scene, her jaw dropped. Asim was still out of breath and felt too much adrenaline to speak yet, so he just looked at her and shrugged.







Chapter 25





Four Weeks Earlier


What happened here tonight was . . . unexpected.

–TS log 13372, excerpt

It was the night of the planned escape, six days after Damien saw the Tapestry, as he called it. Based on books Sara had read, his description sounded like the Singularity, where AI-driven technological growth would supposedly reach a dangerous escape velocity. She didn’t see why he needed a fancy new name for it.

At exactly two in the morning, the facility’s security cameras would all go offline, thanks to a bug that Damien had planted when he was one with the machine, or “seeing the Tapestry.” Instead of going dark, the feeds would start looping the last hour for anyone watching, hopefully buying them a few minutes before the security team noticed.

The corridor lights would go out as well, visually impairing the patrol guards until they deployed their night vision gear. Subjects’ room lights, however, would stay on, so that they wouldn’t come out to see what was happening, if any were even awake.

Two minutes later, a second bug would permanently disable the tracker chips implanted deep in the back of every subject’s neck. From then on, Raphael’s team would be blind to their locations.

Three minutes after that, a third bug that Tapestry-Damien had planted would falsely trigger motion sensors on the facility’s eastern fence, which should draw the security team that way, while Sara and Damien would slip out of the building and head toward the western fence. Simultaneously, the perimeter lights would go offline, giving them visual cover to anyone without night vision.

That was where Damien’s fourth and fifth planted bugs would come into play. The speed with which he had planned all of this still seemed insane. Several motion sensors on the west side would go offline, and the facility’s fleet of eighteen flying perimeter drones would all go into sleep mode, leaving the two of them with no resistance or detection as they scaled the western fence toward freedom.

Sara had memorized the plan, thanks to Damien repeating its details to her for days. The facility grounds were huge, with over seventy guards on night duty, but they’d be spread thin, relying on technology that would be failing them.

Sara and Damien had stockpiled rations over the past week, pretending to be hungry during each meal and going back for seconds. Once they got out, they’d have to lie low for a bit, even if it meant hiding in the forest at times. They’d need food and basic supplies for that phase.

Despite the brilliance of Damien’s plan, there were two parts that Sara hated. First, she might have to shoot some guards, even if they didn’t deserve it. Could she kill, if she had to? Second, there were some dangerous subjects at the facility currently, resting between missions. Fallon was fortunately gone this month, but both Maria and Jolgen were around, along with several mid-tier members of Class B and Class C. If she and Damien were to make even a small mistake, it could rapidly spiral into disaster.

She’d been so nervous that she hadn’t eaten all day. Every time she took a moment to sit down, her mind would race, and her jittery legs would demand to get back up and pace around. But it wasn’t just the escape mission that had her on edge; it was her other plan.

It was 10:30 p.m., with Damien here in her room, and a full three and a half hours until go-time. His room was in a more heavily guarded section of the floor than hers, so they would use hers as the starting point for their escape. Officially, it was against facility rules for subjects to slip into each other’s rooms at night, but it happened anyway for high-status subjects over the years, like Jax with Fallon, or Romulus with several women.

As Stallard’s favored subject, Damien had nearly free run of the facility, and few guards would dare call him on a minor infraction like this. Being in Stallard’s good graces had its perks.

Damien sat on her bed, staring at the floor, lost in thought as he often was. Sara sat at her desk on the other side of the room, delicately folding paper into an origami heart with what looked like a separate little bow on it, even though it was all one sheet. That was what made her more nervous. Since she didn’t know whether their mission would be successful tonight, if she didn’t tell Damien about her feelings for him now, she might never get the chance. Stallard would ensure that no harm came to him, of course, but once she became violent toward guards, it would be no great loss to the facility for them to shoot her dead. She wanted Damien to know she loved him in case she didn’t make it. They might even have time to . . . express some of that love tonight.

He was so handsome. Dark skin, sculpted cheekbones, eyes with unmistakable brilliance and kindness behind them . . . and those full lips. Sara took a deep breath, got up, and walked over. She sat next to him on the bed, brushing her shoulder against his, her blond hair dangling out in front of her as she leaned forward, looking down at her lap. Out of her element, she felt like a kid again, even though she was anything but.

“What are you thinking about?” she asked, heart pounding in her chest.

“Going over the escape details. I know it’s well-planned, but I’m not the same mind that built it, so I’m walking through scenarios to prepare for every contingency.”

Not the best transition topic, Sara thought. But if not now, when?

“Damien, can I tell you something?”

“Sure. What is it?”

She watched out of her peripheral vision as he turned his gaze toward her, while she kept looking down out of embarrassment, feeling her cheeks flush. She tapped her left heel on the carpet repeatedly, letting the silence go on too long.

“I . . . really care for you,” she began, still looking down and sounding more rehearsed than she’d intended. “And as more than a friend. I’ve loved you for a long time now, and I wanted you to know that. Just . . . in case things go wrong tonight.” She handed him the origami heart-and-bow, and finally had the nerve to look up at his beautiful face as she did.

Damien paused, then took the heart from her hand to examine its details, his fingers brushing up against hers and giving her an electric thrill. Sara watched his face in profile as he studied the paper creation, and she realized she was unintentionally holding her breath. She tried reading his expression, but that was harder to do with him than it used to be.

As the seconds ticked by, she increasingly felt sick to her stomach, regretting everything. “I realize this was a bad time to—”

“I love it,” he interrupted, finally looking back at her with a smile, fully present. “Sara, you know how much I care for you. I wouldn’t have gotten this far without you. I love everything about you.”

A surge of joy and relief flowed through her, a sense of lightness as though her heart was trying to flutter toward the ceiling. Turning toward him, she set her hand on his thigh and leaned in to kiss him. But when she met his lips, they were stiff. That pit in her stomach tightened again, and his body tensed, so she pulled back. “I’m sorry,” she said. “I shouldn’t have.”

Before she could finish pulling away, Damien reached out and hugged her, drawing her back in close and pressing her head to his warm shoulder. “It’s not what it looks like,” he said. “I don’t mean to hurt you.”

“Then what is it?” Her eyes teared up with her face buried in his shoulder, her body surrounded by his embrace. Adrenaline surged through her veins, and yet she did everything in her power to keep her voice steady.

“I . . . I’m not myself right now,” Damien said. “Not for a while, and certainly not this past week.”

He loosened his hug, and with his right hand brushed her hair out of her face and tucked it behind one of her ears. Then he gripped her shoulders with both hands and met her eyes. His expression and body language were the most assertive she’d ever seen, and she tried her best to avoid tearing up more. She suddenly felt small in his arms.

“It’s not fair to you,” he said, “to only give you half of me. Once I get some more time away from seeing what I saw in the machine, once I get some distance from this place, I think I’ll return to how I was. How we were. You’re the most beautiful woman I know, and strong in all the ways that matter, but part of me just isn’t here right now, or more accurately . . . is overshadowed by everything else in my head.”

Sara nodded to show understanding, unable to speak yet.

He pulled her back into another hug and kissed the side of her head while her face was buried in his shoulder. She hugged him tight, and a wave of excitement washed through her when his lips touched her scalp, but she was so conflicted. Everything he said made sense, and yet her heart felt as though it had been ripped out. Her eyes teared up again, so when he loosened his grip, she used the opportunity to stand and take a deep breath.

“I know this was hilariously bad timing,” she said, forcing a smile. “But I’m glad I got that off my chest. You’re right; we can talk about this later. We need to focus, since this is our chance to change everything.” She went and checked her pack just to have something to do with her nervous hands, then sat back down at her desk.

“Sara, I—”

“It’s fine,” she said, standing up again, still filled with nervous energy. “Truly. I need to use the restroom. You can get back to focusing, and I’ll make a note of guard positioning while I’m out there.” Before he could answer, she opened the door and left.

As soon as she reached the corridor, silent tears trickled down her cheeks. By the time she got to the restroom, which was fortunately empty, the rest of her tears poured free.



What a disaster. Damien ran through what he should have said differently.

On any other day in his twenty-one years of life, he would’ve handled that better. He had already planned to tell her how he felt once they had escaped and he was back in a better state of mind. Everything he’d told her was true: he loved her, and yet whoever “he” was at this moment wasn’t truly himself. Not yet, at least. He was distracted and numb, yet he still found himself heartbroken over what she was experiencing right now. I can fix this. She’ll understand.

Twenty minutes later, Sara returned to the room looking as though nothing had happened.

As she closed the door behind her without a word, he knew he had to say something. “Look, I know that I—”

“Relax,” she said with a smile, sounding more at ease. “This was just a funny moment. I got something off my chest, you got something off yours, and we’ll go over everything another time. We’re in mission mode tonight.”

Damien hesitated, then nodded. “I agree,” he said. “But I meant what I said. It’s just—”

“I know. It’s okay.” She inhaled and brushed some of her hair back. She glanced at the ceiling, then at him as she let out the breath. “I mean it, too. We’ll talk about this later. For both our sakes it’s best that you focus on what you need to for now. I’ll amp myself up for my part, too.”

She sat at her desk and began folding papers, while he watched. After a moment, he returned to his thoughts. But he kept catching himself glancing over at her to make sure she was okay. She didn’t look back at him, likely pretending not to notice as she just kept folding. He took that as his cue. Tonight, he needed the version of her he’d seen kickboxing the bag last week, so if she was fine with emotional distance for now, then he was too.

Distractions gone, he replayed the plan in his mind, iterating through possibilities and contingencies until it was time to move.







Chapter 26





Four Weeks Earlier, Continued


For now, I will admit that I am impressed. Furious, but impressed.

–TS log 13372, excerpt

“Pistols loaded?” Damien asked, his heart beating faster than normal.

“Check,” she said, wrapping a tie around her hair to hold it back.

He touched his weapon to be sure it was still in his holster. It felt strange to have it; he’d only fired a gun twice in his life.

“Extra ammo?” he asked.

“Check. Three mags.”

She’d stockpiled those gradually over the past week of firing range practices to avoid suspicion.

“Rations?” he asked.

“In your pack,” she said.

“Wire cutters, thermal blanket, rope?” he asked.

“Yes, in my pack.” She’d taken them from various supply closets three days ago, careful to conceal her actions in front of the cameras.

“Medkit, gloves, and spare set of clothes?”

“I’ve got mine. Yours?” she asked.

“Yes,” he said. “And you remember all the timings?”

She nodded confidently. There was no hint of her emotional side from hours ago. Just the soldier he needed right now.

“Okay. Two minutes until two,” he said. “On the hour, you lead us out.”

Damien focused on his breathing. Cold sweat was already forming at his temples. Would the bugs he’d planted work as intended? He remembered being certain of it at the time, but this diminished version of himself hadn’t retained all the details.

The clock struck two in the morning. Sara gave a hand signal and slipped the door open. It was dark, as expected, but with their eyesight, they could still see clearly enough. Damien hoped the cameras would be looping just as the Tapestry-seeing version of himself had intended.

Sara led them out the door and down the hall, footsteps as soft as possible. She gave the hand motion to pause as she looked around a corner.

“The hell happened to the lights?” said a male guard’s voice, coming from the direction Sara faced. Sara signaled with two of her fingers. Two guards.

“Don’t know,” replied another man. “Stay here. I’ll go look around.”

A flashlight snapped on and pointed in their direction from down the hall, and Sara brought her head back around the corner just in time to avoid being caught in the beam. Footsteps approached. Sara signaled for him to stay there.

As the guard rounded the corner, Sara sprang from the shadows, and choked him from behind. Damien had never grappled before, but from Sara showing him some moves over the years and from watching her spar, he knew perfect technique when he saw it.

Sara positioned her elbow right under the poor guard’s chin, so that her forearm and biceps would each clamp down on the carotid arteries on the right and left sides of his neck in a V shape, instantly cutting off blood to the brain. A less effective and slower air choke, she’d explained, would occur if someone sloppily put their forearm over the front of someone’s neck, pressing their windpipe and leaving their arteries clear. Within several seconds of struggling, the larger guard was unconscious or worse. Sara held for a few more seconds, then laid him on the floor.

“Corbin?” the other guard asked from down the hall. “You okay?”

“He collapsed,” Sara said, feigning concern. “Help me with him. Why’s it so dark?”

Footsteps approached. As the second guard rounded the corner and leaned down over his fallen partner, Sara grabbed him in the same type of chokehold from behind. He responded faster, though, driving his elbow back hard into her stomach. Sara gasped, then struggled with him for several seconds as Damien raced to think how to help without making it worse by distracting her.

With raw strength, the guard started to break free from Sara’s grasp. In response, she swung her legs up and wrapped them around his waist from behind, locking her ankles together over his stomach. She was now off the floor on the man’s back, latched onto his waist and neck, as he thrashed around and clawed at her arm. He stumbled backward, and the two of them fell hard onto the floor, with Sara’s back hitting first and taking their combined body weight. She let out a shocked gasp, and Damien winced. But she didn’t let go, and with her legs and arms wrapped tightly around the guard, she gritted her teeth and squeezed until he stopped flailing, her elbow placed perfectly under his chin as he went limp.

“We have to go, now,” Sara whispered, a touch out of breath, as Damien helped her up from underneath the weight of the fallen man. If she was in pain, she didn’t show it.

She jogged down the hall, and he followed. After they rounded another corner, a commotion sounded from where they’d left the guards, but it was hard to say whether one had woken up or if someone had found them.

Sara listened to the western stairwell door and put out the “pause” gesture again. There were footsteps and voices coming up, and then the door opened. She pulled Damien to the hinge side of the doorway. They were now tucked behind the door to the right, out of sight to those who’d opened it.

Two guards emerged and jogged to their left with flashlights, back the way Sara and Damien had come. Sara silently pulled out her pistol and pointed it at their backs as they headed away down the hall. She stood perfectly still in the dark, eyes narrowed, ready to shoot if either of them were to turn back and spot them.

But after several tense seconds, the guards rounded the next corner without glancing back, and Sara nodded toward the door. Damien opened it, and Sara went through. He followed her down the stairs, out the stairwell door on the first floor, and toward the western side exit near the cafeteria. They ducked behind a vending machine for cover.

One guard stood near the exit, a woman in her thirties with auburn-red hair and side-swept bangs named Jessica. She held her pistol tensely in her hand, listening to her radio.

“Corbin’s waking up now. He says he was attacked by C17,” said a man’s voice from the device. “Looks like Mike was too. I’m alerting Raphael and the doc himself. Assume lockdown procedures until further notice. She has D4 with her.”

Sara sighed and pointed her pistol at the guard, but Damien put his hand on her forearm and shook his head.

“We have to,” she whispered. “There’s no cover if we try to approach her.”

But he knew her name. Jessica. She was one of the lights in the dark, and each light mattered. “Let me try something,” he whispered. He set his pack down behind the vending machine to look less suspicious, then stepped out into the corridor. “Help,” he whispered, trying to look frightened.

Jessica swung her flashlight toward him. “D4? What are you doing down here? Where’s C17?”

“Something’s happening on the second floor,” Damien said. “C17 went crazy, but I got away. What are we supposed to do?”

Jessica glanced back at the door she was guarding, furrowed her brow, then stepped away from it toward Damien. “Come with me, quickly,” she said, pistol and light at the ready. “I’ll take you to a secure location. Raphael always says the top priority is to protect you.”

Damien nodded and started walking with her. As soon as they reached the vending machine, Sara burst out from behind it, knocked Jessica’s gun aside, stepped behind her leg, and took her down hard. She choked the gurgling woman unconscious with a different sort of front-facing choke from atop her. Jessica’s legs kicked twice and went limp, and Damien couldn’t help but wince.

Sara pulled the magazine out of Jessica’s pistol and slid the weapon itself deep under the vending machine. The woman was already stirring slightly.

As Sara stood up, a shout came from down the hall. “Everything okay?” a distant male guard’s voice asked. “Jess?” Footsteps followed.

“Run,” Sara whispered. “Now.”

“What about you?” Damien asked.

“Now!” she hissed, eyes fierce.

Damien bolted toward the door and slammed through it out into the cool night air. The external lights were off, thanks to his third bug, leaving everything darker than usual. Behind him, two gunshots rang out, and terror spiked through him. He turned to look, afraid of what he might see, but Sara burst through the doorway unharmed, pistol in hand.

“Keep going!” she shouted.

Relieved, Damien turned forward and sprinted. Within seconds, Sara caught up. Had she shot that oncoming guard? Her face was unreadable.

As they ran across the dark grass field, Damien knew this was one of the riskiest moments. Until they reached the tree line past the field and parking lot, they’d be vulnerable to snipers, or at least Sara would be. Hopefully the east-side false alarms would keep the guards’ attention directed that way, and most wouldn’t have their night-vision goggles out yet. That had been his plan while seeing the Tapestry. Wait, where’s . . .

“My pack!” Damien whispered. He stopped and looked back, but he felt Sara’s hand grab the front of his sweatshirt and yank him forward.

“We can’t go back,” she said. “At least we still have the cutters. That was mainly the rations.”

They kept running until they reached a lone tree near the parking lot. Sara gestured toward it, and they used it for cover. A perimeter guard held up a pistol and a flashlight, frantically looking around. He stood right in their way, and other than this tree, there was no cover. Sara took a deep breath, came around the tree, and shot twice, dropping him. Injured or dead? Damien couldn’t tell.

“Go,” she said. She kicked the pistol away from the downed guard’s outstretched arm, then caught up to Damien despite his sprint.

His throat burned already; he couldn’t keep this pace for long. Though he’d always tried to exercise with Sara, the weekly tests had kept him drained. They crossed the parking lot, mostly empty at this time of night, and headed out onto another grassy field. Soon they reached the tree line.

“I need a moment,” he gasped, blood thumping in his head.

Sara nodded. “Stay here for cover. I’ll scout.”

Damien had never seen her in this mode before. She was an emotionless soldier. He felt like a child being led around by an adult, even though he was the taller of the two.

“Shit,” she said. “It’s Jolgen.”

Damien glanced around the tree. Jolgen, rifle in hand but without his armor, was yelling at two guards, and he had a bloodhound on a leash. The dogs, he thought. Too soon. This is outside of the allowable tolerance.

“Okay,” Sara said. “We’re going to go through these trees, to the fence, and over it. Can’t wait any longer.”

“The dogs might mess up the plan,” Damien said between big breaths. “They brought them out fast, and I slowed us down with Jessica. We don’t want them to know we’re heading west right away.”

“Doesn’t matter now,” Sara said. “We’re already this far. Come.”

They moved through the trees at a pace Damien could manage and passed a fallen security drone in sleep mode. After a few minutes more, they reached the razor wire fence. It was the type with the big menacing loops of wire and steel razors, not the simple lines of barbed wire.

Sara holstered her pistol, pulled the wire cutters from her pack, slipped on the gloves, and climbed. When she reached the loops of wire at the top, she tossed her pack over the fence and cut through the wire in multiple places. It looked hard to do, since she had to cling to the fence while cutting. Damien watched as her clothes got caught on razors and torn a few times, making her wince, but after a few minutes, she clipped through enough wire at the top and pushed the loops aside to form a small gap. Damien heard barking getting closer.

“Okay, come up,” Sara said. Her forearm was bleeding through her sleeve as she held the loops back for him.

He climbed as she waited at the top. Reaching up to where she was, he tried to swing over through the gap but got caught, cursing as he did. After several kicks and a tear on his pants, he managed to force himself through. Sara followed, contending with the tangled loops.

She jumped straight from the top of the fence to the ground on the other side and picked up her pack, while Damien took more time to climb down. The barking grew louder still.

Once at the bottom, he saw how much more blood she had on her right sleeve. She’d taken deeper cuts than he’d thought.

“It’ll heal,” she said, breathing heavily, noticing his expression. “It’s okay.”

They started across a narrow field toward a line of trees. This was the beginning of the forest proper, where they would have a lot more cover.

“Freeze!” Jolgen shouted from behind. “Hands up, you fuckers.”







Chapter 27





Four Weeks Earlier, Continued


If Fallon had been here tonight, I doubt this mess would have cascaded so badly. She has grown on me more than I expected.

–TS log 13372, excerpt

Sara stopped, a chill running down her spine as she turned to look. Jolgen stood on the other side of the fence, his assault rifle leveled at her, a bloodhound at his side. He wore a white tank top, likely what he’d been sleeping in when their escape caused a commotion.

“Put your hands up, or I fire,” Jolgen said.

Sara clenched her teeth, exhaled, and raised her hands. Then she turned around fully to face him. Blood dripped from her drenched sleeve, and her forearm seared with pain.

“You dumb bitch,” Jolgen said with a smirk. “What did you think was going to happen here? You too, freak. Hands up and turn around like your girl here.”

“I’m quite certain,” Damien said, sounding calm, “that you have explicit orders to take me unharmed.” He slowly unholstered his pistol with a snap of leather, held it at his side, and turned around to face Jolgen.

“Drop it!” Jolgen shouted. “I said hands up.”

“No.” Damien stepped in front of Sara, putting himself between her and Jolgen. “You can’t shoot me. Thane would have your head if you did. And if you climb the fence or shoot her, I’ll shoot you.” He raised the pistol slowly, deliberately, and aimed it at Jolgen.

Jolgen stared viciously at Damien, and kept the assault rifle aimed, but did nothing. His pupils, wide in the dark, flicked around for ideas.

“Now what?” Sara whispered.

“Stay behind me,” Damien said. “Walk to the forest. Get out of sight.”

“But—”

“I’ll come as soon as you’re behind cover.”

She obeyed, stepping backward toward the forest to keep her eyes on them. Jolgen kept glaring at her, and Damien glanced back at her out of the corner of his eye while remaining faced toward Jolgen.

“You know this won’t lead anywhere good,” Jolgen said, raising his voice. His hound barked, sending her heart rate up.

She said nothing. Once she reached the forest edge, she slipped behind a tree. With his pistol still aimed at Jolgen, Damien began walking backward toward her as she watched.

“Remember, if you try to come over the fence, I’ll shoot,” Damien said as he continued to step back. He eventually reached the forest, close to her. “Now we run,” he whispered.

They took off into the forest, and within seconds, there came the unmistakable metallic clinking of the razor wire fence being scaled behind them. Her pulse spiked. Jolgen was a super-soldier, impossible to outrun. She raced for options. At least he wouldn’t have the hound with him on this side of the fence, which made hiding a possibility, though the area would be swarming with guards and hounds soon enough. She turned and emptied the rest of her magazine blindly behind her into the thick forest to hopefully slow him down, capitalizing on the asymmetry of the situation. Jolgen couldn’t blindly shoot back or he’d risk hitting Damien.

There was a gasp and a distant yell. She might have hit him.

“This way,” Damien urged, pulling her to turn left as they ran, likely to throw off Jolgen. Damien’s face looked frantic as he sprinted, his breath growing more ragged and his footsteps faltering.

He slowed down, so Sara grabbed his sweatshirt and pulled him behind a thick set of bushes, then slowly peeked back around them.

For several seconds, she saw nothing and thought maybe they’d lost him. But then there they were, his fierce reflective eyes and the sound of snapping twigs under his heavy footfalls. Jolgen had gotten dangerously close, but he was still looking around. He didn’t see them yet behind the bushes. A dark streak of blood ran down his thigh; she’d clipped him with a shot.

Sara pulled back behind the bushes and reloaded her pistol, slipping the magazine in as slowly as possible to minimize the sound, and hoping the constant noise of insects in the nighttime woods would be enough to mask the little clicks the process made. She glanced at Jolgen again. There he was, scanning the area, looking to the side, standing like a tower in the darkness. She made sure to look back down quickly, since the moonlight might make her eyes reflect like his were.

She took a deep breath and gripped her pistol with both hands, pulling back around the bushes. This was it. She had the element of surprise and could shoot first. But then, who could say what would happen? He had top-notch aim and a bigger gun. Nothing short of a direct headshot would prevent him from getting rounds off at her. Even that might not be enough.

Either way, it would give Damien a window to run. “Get ready,” she whispered.

Damien put his hand over her pistol and shook his head. “He’ll kill you.” But after several tense seconds ticked by, Jolgen began walking in their direction.

What did Damien think either of them could do here? She met his gaze, and the eyes that looked back at her were pleading. Loving.

She held her breath, looking around for another option, and finally had an idea. She reached out and used her weak telekinesis on a small bush thirty yards to their left. Just enough to create a crackling sound with its leaves. At that distance, since her power was so weak, even that little motion gave her a headache, but there was no other way. And then, thankfully, there was the reaction she hoped for: the jingle of Jolgen’s assault rifle cord as he shifted, and the creeping sound of his footfalls on the foliage in that direction.

“This way,” she whispered, and they crept off toward the right, keeping the bush between them and Jolgen in case he looked back. Eventually he was out of sight, behind layers of tree trunks and bushes, while they entered a new and unbounded world.



After hours of walking, Damien needed a break. The first signs of dawn were creeping into the sky.

As bad as everything was, he couldn’t help but be amused by how much Sara was still looking around. There were only trees, streams, roads, and houses, after all. The last hour wasn’t much different from the first, though her ever-curious eyes made it seem like each moment revealed something new.

“Five minutes,” he said. “I just . . . need to sit.” Whether it was the lingering dullness his time in the machine had left him with, or his exhaustion exceeding his sense of wonder, he envied Sara’s enthusiasm.

She nodded and scanned the area like a soldier on reconnaissance. After she pointed to a patch of thick bush, they slipped behind it.

As far as Damien could tell, they’d been heading in the right direction. They had hiked several miles northwest through woods, then turned more northward, crossed several empty roads in the dark, crept past a suburban neighborhood, and finally entered the edge of the Pine Barrens proper. Hundreds of square miles of forest and swamp would make tracking them difficult.

The key risk now was the lack of supplies. He’d left his pack behind, which held most of their food. Sara had two bottles of water and a small can or two of nuts in her pack, along with spare clothes and other items, including a medical kit.

“Let me see your arm,” he said.

Sara pulled off her hooded sweatshirt and thermal sweater, wincing as she slipped her right arm out of the sleeves to reveal several deep gashes on her forearm from the razor wire. As he suspected, they were worse than she’d let on. At least they’d heal fast.

“We have to clean that,” he said. She nodded.

He took the medical kit out of her pack and got to work. She hissed and bit her lip as he poured disinfectant over her arm, breathed long and slow breaths as he cleared away the dried blood, then eased as he wrapped a bandage around the cuts.

He looked up at her face, suddenly struck by how beautiful she was. Her skin was grimy with dirt and sweat, her soiled blond hair was pulled into a messy tail, and her damp black tank top clung to her figure. A weariness lined her eyes, but also a grim determination. How much had he hurt her the night before with his aloofness? What had been going through her mind these past hours?

As he finished the bandaging, he leaned in and kissed her on the cheek, and her eyes went wide.

“Dami—”

“We’re going to get through this,” he said with a smile, gazing into her eyes. Then he leaned in again, reached behind her head to cup it, and kissed her on the lips, soft and warm. It felt so much more wonderful than last night, when he’d been distracted. He pulled back and caressed her cheek once, then pushed some of her loose hair strands behind one ear. “I’m not entirely myself yet, but I’m getting there. I’m so sorry if I hurt you.”

She locked eyes with him silently, bit her lip, and nodded. A sense of curiosity lit up her features, and the corners of her mouth tipped up. An angel. His angel. He’d needed to see that, but he wasn’t sure what else to say in the moment.

“We . . . we have to get moving,” she said, breaking the tension. She slid her top layers back on gingerly to avoid disrupting the bandages. “With that pack lost and our supplies short, we can’t head farther north into the deep barrens.”

“Agreed,” Damien said. “Based on the maps, if we head northwest from here again, there should be some farms. We can stay at the edge of the forest near them.”

The next several hours passed quickly. They spent the rest of the morning hiking northwest, putting as many miles as possible between themselves and the facility, until they heard the roaring blades of a helicopter in the distance.

“Get the thermal blanket out. Let’s stop here until it’s gone,” Damien said. He didn’t know if it was after them or just a coincidence, but they couldn’t take any chances. The tree cover was dense, and they’d worn black, but they risked detection from their motion, or their body heat.

By this point, the facility’s forces would have to search all the area for tens of miles in every direction, hundreds of square miles, but they had good equipment. The variable that Damien found hardest to account for was the hounds. He wasn’t sure how effective they would be in these conditions, and due to Jolgen spotting them at the fence, the facility likely suspected that they’d headed westward and could prioritize their search in this direction.

Sara nodded, and they stopped under a large tree, with plenty of dense bushes around. She checked the area, then pulled out the blanket to cover them both, which would shield them from thermal imaging if the helicopter was using it. She also pulled out a water bottle, sharing it with Damien as well. Luckily, there were swamps here. Dehydration likely wouldn’t become critical. Food was another story.

Lastly, she pulled out a can of nuts and held it toward him.

“How many do you have?” he asked.

“Just this can. You take it. I’m fine.”

“You need energy, Sara. You didn’t even eat yesterday. We can split it.” He pushed the can back toward her.

“I’m not that hungry. Bronn says fasting can feel good. This hike is more straining on you, so I think it’s best for you to have them. You’ve been through more than me lately, with those tests.” She pushed the can back to him, and her fingers lingered on his hand for a moment. She smiled. “We’ll find food soon, even if we have to break into a store or something.”

Damien was skeptical that she would be okay without anything to eat, but she remained adamant. For now, he ate half of the nuts and put the other half back into her pack in case she changed her mind. When he looked back up, he found her resting with her eyes closed, leaning against the thick trunk of their tree. His first instinct was to wake her, but he stopped himself. They had been up and moving all night, and now it was the afternoon of the following day. This was probably the best time to rest anyway; they could move again at night.

He kept watch for a few hours, listening to the sounds of insects and animals throughout the forest. Eventually she awoke, startled, but he put his hand on her shoulder. “You’re safe—I kept watch.”

She took several deep breaths, looked around, and checked the time. “It’s four o’clock!”

“I know. But I think this was the right window for it. Now you keep watch, and I’ll try to get a few hours, too. By nightfall, we can move again.”

It turned out he didn’t have to try. Almost as soon as he put his head down, he was out.



Despite being technically free, Sara felt more caged than ever. Helicopters searched overhead, and countless guards and hounds had to be scouring the area for them. They needed to be silent, and every decision, ranging from when to rest to which direction to head in, was potentially life or death. Freedom or captivity.

But they were making progress. After another day of travel, she would feel more confident. Or so she hoped. Then what? Eventually, they’d have to steal some food, and maybe they’d find an abandoned house or something, to lie low for a few days.

Then? Well, Damien was the genius. He’d figure it out. They could tell the public. Or they could find the right authorities to approach. Either way, she had to make sure Clare and Marcus were freed as well—and all the others who wanted to be. General Price and his broad power would make that hard.

She looked over at Damien, who slept on his side, using her pack as a pillow. She’d never seen him as assertive as he’d been during all of this. There were moments against Jolgen where she would’ve been killed or captured if not for Damien. He seemed bigger, somehow. And that kiss; she could feel tingles just thinking about it again.

The sound of helicopter blades echoed in the distance, along with the ambient sounds of nature. And then . . . something bigger. Sara tensed and inched her hand toward her pistol.

A coyote poked its head out from a distant bush and looked at her. She breathed a sigh of relief and met its gaze. She wasn’t sure how dangerous a coyote could be, but at least it wasn’t one of their pursuers. It stood there, hesitant, then crept closer. She smiled. It probably felt as hungry as she did. It stopped again.

“I have no food for you, unfortunately,” she said. “Shoo.” She stood up, careful not to wake Damien as she shifted the blanket, and stared into its eyes to look more intimidating. The coyote took a few steps back, and its eyes lingered on her, but then it turned around and prowled off.

Clouds moved in and light rain began to fall, filling the forest with a soft pitter-patter and a fresh, earthy smell. She took a deep breath of the moist air and reminded herself to emphasize the positives. While she had frequently seen the forested edges of the facility before, there was a wondrously new aspect to everything around, and it was best to focus on that rather than dwell on the downsides. The chilly autumn rain was uncomfortable, but it also might slow their pursuers.

Eventually, nightfall came, and the drizzle thinned, caught mostly by the canopy above. She woke Damien, and they continued.



“You know,” Damien said to break the latest silence as they walked, “they say the Jersey Devil lives out here.”

“What?”

“The Jersey Devil. A monster of folklore.”

“Thanks, that’s what I need right now.”

“Well, it’s not real obviously,” he said. “But I’ve read about it. Back in the seventeenth century, there were Quaker settlers here, and others who practiced more occult-style religion, with conflicts between them. Supposedly the occultists created a monster, a devil-like flying abomination. There have been sightings ever since.”

“I’ll take him over Jolgen,” she said.

Damien laughed, then caught himself. He was being too loud.

“The Pine Barrens have a long and dark history,” he continued, quieter. “Throughout the nineteenth century people feared this as a place where fugitives, deserting soldiers, stray tribesmen, and runaway slaves could be found. Who knows how true it was; probably some of it. I mean, here we are, fugitives. In the twentieth century, it earned a reputation as a common place to bury bodies. Like by the mafia.”

“Wonderful,” she said.

In truth, Damien spoke to lighten his own mood. Despite his ability to see through the dark, the Pine Barrens at night were a special sort of frightening. The constant sounds of insects, owls, and occasionally something bigger. A squealing sound of prey being caught, thrashing around in agony, and then silence. Talking about it was like shining a light on it.

“I mean, technically we’re monsters.” He pointed to his eyes and smiled.

“You’re not a monster to me,” she said, then lowered her voice. “Stallard is the real monster.”

“I know, it was just a joke.” He took a long breath. “I can tell you something real, though.”

“What is it?”

“I never told you this, because I didn’t want you to feel guilty unnecessarily. But things are different now, and after last night, I want you to know. Remember how Thane suddenly stopped doing those telekinesis tests on you? It’s because I convinced him to.”

Her eyes widened as she walked. “You . . . how?”

“By agreeing to lean into his experiments with me instead of resisting. Looking back, it almost led to the end of the world, but you know what? I’d do it all again. That’s how much I’ve always loved you. I know I haven’t been the best at showing it.”

Her eyes went glossy, and she just stared at him, walking with her mouth agape. After several seconds, she seemed ready to speak, but then in her distraction she stepped into a stream. There were a lot of little ones around.

“Damnit!” she said, catching herself and pulling out her leg, soaked all the way to her calf.

Damien laughed as he stopped to wait for her. “See. You’re too cute to be a monster.”

“It’s not funny,” she said, shaking her leg. She looked down at her boot. “It’s gross swamp water.”

As she put her foot down, she glanced back up at him, came over, took both of his hands, and leaned in to kiss him. His exhaustion drained away as her soft lips met his. Then he pulled his hands free and wrapped them around her, kissing her more deeply.

When he reluctantly loosened his embrace, she slowly pulled back, smiling, with a stray tear sliding down her cheek. “I don’t know what to say,” she whispered. “I’m mad you did that for me, but I love you for it. I’ll have to get back at you, though. Somehow.” Her smile turned into a smirk.

“You already have, by being here with me. There’s no one I’d rather be with.” He spread his arms, gesturing around to the dark woods.

Her eyelids trembled, subtle tears threatening to turn into a full-on cry.

“Come,” he said. “Let’s keep going. Seems I’ve slowed us down with all this quaint mammalian sentimentality.” He smiled so she’d know it was a joke, but she had already lit up again.

They walked all night until daytime arrived once more, now with a renewed sense of warmth between them. To conserve energy, they didn’t speak much, but that was fine. The way she looked at him said enough. The rain ceased, though the sky remained overcast.

Sara still refused to eat any nuts, insisting he finish what little they had. He worried about her at first, but her energy seemed high. After the body’s metabolism burned through its glycogen stores during a fast, it would enter a state of ketosis and switch over to burning body fat instead, and ketones would become fuel for the brain.

They rested again in the afternoon. Sara’s boot was still damp, so she took them both off to dry. She insisted he sleep first this time, since he’d gotten less before. He started to protest, but she just glared at him, so he smiled and accepted it. They would both get a turn anyway.

Within minutes of resting against a tree, he fell asleep.

He woke up on his own, two hours later, to the sound of Sara trying to re-bandage her own arm.

“Let me help with that,” he said, focusing his eyes and pushing away the groggy feeling. “Did you already put more disinfectant on?”

She nodded and held out her arm with a smile.

“These cuts are healing fast,” he said, taking over on the bandage. “I’ve been thinking that we should try to hitchhike for a bit. I know that wasn’t part of the plan due to surveillance on the roads, but we probably should break any scent trail to be safe.”

“You think the dogs could still follow this far?”

“I’m not 100 percent certain. Available data was mixed about their exact capabilities, with too many confounding variables. But since they know we went west, I’ve been worrying about it,” he admitted. He circled the fresh bandages around her arm, and as he finished, he looked up at her. She was already watching his face, and he smiled. “Your turn to sleep,” he said. He leaned against the tree and gestured for her to come over to him. “Here, this’ll be more comfortable.”

She curled up against him, using his lap as her pillow, and he wrapped the thermal blanket over them both. He caressed her soft hair a few times and watched her fall asleep, almost hypnotized by her gentle breathing, feeling at peace. This is heaven.

Two hours later, as the sun grew low and he was about to wake Sara for another night of walking, a distant dog barked. No, he thought. And then another bark. No!

“Sara,” he whispered. “Sara. Wake up. Someone’s here.” He shook her.

She shot awake and reached for her pistol, eyes darting about, as more barking and rustling sounded in the distance. Getting closer. She looked up at him with panicked eyes.

“Let’s try to move quietly,” he whispered. “It might not be as bad as we think. We don’t know who it is yet.” They grabbed their things and crept through the forest. Sara didn’t have time to get her boots back on. She carried them instead, wincing as she stepped barefoot over rough undergrowth.

As they moved, the barking grew louder. Sara looked over at Damien, grimaced, then stopped and placed her boots silently on the ground. She unholstered her pistol again, then turned and pointed it with both hands in the direction of the sounds, waiting.

The barrel crushed in on itself.

“Damien, ru—” she began to say, but the words choked off in her throat.

Maria emerged into view, with Jolgen and two guards behind her. Jolgen wore his full head-to-toe, bulletproof combat armor. Damien tried to grab Sara’s sweatshirt and pull, but an invisible force immobilized her neck. Then a strong grip clenched around his own waist.

“It’s them!” one of the guards shouted.

“No shit,” Jolgen said, his voice muffled behind his helmet as he towered over the rest.

Damien unholstered his pistol, but his arm froze in place before he could raise it, as if held by a vise.

“Just be still, Damien,” Maria said quietly.
