“Listen to me!” Damien shouted, locking eyes with her. “You don’t understand what’s coming if you bring me back to Thane. It’ll be too dangerous if he hooks me up to the system again. Not for me, but for everyone else.”

“Call back to Raphael, and to the other teams,” Maria said to the guards, not taking her eyes off of him. “Tell them we found them and have them in our custody.”

Beside him, Sara thrashed around for a moment, then went limp from the choke. With no other choice, Damien opened his hand and dropped his pistol in surrender.







Chapter 28





Four Weeks Earlier, Continued


What happened here was bound to happen eventually, I suppose, although I do not know the catalyst for the change. I was so focused on expanding the inner world that I underestimated the power that could be unleashed in the outer world.

–TS log 13375, excerpt

Sara awoke as she landed on something hard. She instinctively tried to push herself up but found that she was restrained. Plasticuffs bit into her wrists behind her back, and terrifyingly, duct tape was spread across the lower half of her face.

“Mmmphh!” She looked up and saw Jolgen. He had dropped her into the back of a utility van, onto its cold metal floor. Where’s Damien?

A moment later, both relief and terror struck her. A facility guard escorted Damien, wrists bound in front and without a gag, to the back of the van. He was alive, fortunately, but captured along with her. Just treated with a bit more dignity. His head was lowered in defeat as he walked, but as he reached the van, his eyes met hers, and they looked grim.

This can’t be happening, Sara thought. Almost everything had gone according to plan. Had it been impossible all along? She pulled hard at her bindings but found them unbreakable, and Jolgen grinned at her. She screamed again in frustration, panic setting in.

Maria appeared at the van’s back doors, stone-faced, unreadable. Eyes tired and cold. She watched as they were loaded in, then without a word walked toward the front passenger seat.

Jolgen climbed into the back of the van with Sara and Damien. The two guards closed the doors behind him and piled into the second row of seats up front, the hound with them. A metal wall with a small window separated the back portion of the van from the two rows of seats in the front half.

“Seems we have a bit of a road trip,” Jolgen said, eyeing Sara. He still wore his heavy combat armor, except he had taken his helmet and gloves off.

“Anything you do, I’ll tell Thane,” Damien said.

“Who gives a shit?” Jolgen said. “As long as we bring your creepy ass back in one piece. That’s all the old man cares about.”

The van began moving on what sounded like a dirt road, the floor rumbling beneath them. Leaning back against the wall, Jolgen pulled out his combat knife and twirled it around in his fingers with the skill of a surgeon while staring at her. He began softly whistling as he did. Minutes went by, and her heart pounded in her chest.

“You fucking shot me,” Jolgen finally said. “And the doc is furious at you.” He stopped twirling the knife and pointed at her with its tip. “One guard dead, others injured, and you aren’t worth shit to the facility. You’re disposable. He doesn’t even care if you’re captured alive or dead, as long as Damien is brought back unharmed, and you with your brain intact.”

After a long pause, he slid over, inspecting her. His face was uncomfortably close, and she could smell his sour breath, sending a pulse of dread through her.

“If you hurt her, I’ll ensure Thane makes your life a living hell,” Damien said.

“Oh?” Jolgen looked back at him. “Are we not already in hell?” Amusement dripped from his voice, almost theatrically. “I mean, what’s the doc going to do, send me to a fucking warzone?” That tone drained away, replaced by a hateful glare. He put his sharp forehead near Damien’s, staring into his eyes, challenging him. After a moment, he turned back to her.

He leaned in and put the knife right between her legs, touching her with its tip over her pants. Her breathing intensified. “You know how much my leg hurts from your damn shot? Or all the cuts I got climbing over that fence, in my fucking sleepwear?” he asked, slowly applying some pressure with the knife. “And do you realize how little your condition matters when you’re brought back? Alive, dead, or somewhere in between? I like the ‘in between’ option the best.”

Damien, wide-eyed, opened his mouth again. “Jolgen, I don’t thi—”

“For every word you say, freak, I’ll make it worse. Shut the fuck up and she’ll at least be alive by the time we make it back,” Jolgen said, turning to face Damien. “Whether it’s hard or easy will depend on her.”

Sara used Jolgen’s distraction to try to kick him in the head, but he caught her ankle and slammed her leg back down to the van floor. Pain surged through her heel at the impact. He brought the blade right to her face, forcing her to wince.

“The hard way, then. Let’s start with an eye.” He grabbed her forehead with one hand and pushed his knife tip closer with the other, while she thrashed with every bit of energy she had, pinned down against the van floor. Kicking, squirming, screaming into the tape, trying and failing to burst out of the plasticuffs with pure fury.

The knife tip pierced the skin over her left eyebrow, she closed her eyes hard, and he carved sharply lower, over her eyelid and down toward her cheek. She screamed and kicked, her thrashing turning involuntary from the pain. Blood and tears mixed, pouring across her cheek.

He came in again with a horizontal cut. Starting from her temple, he sliced the blade slowly across her skin until he reached the corner of her eye. Then he hooked it into her socket, trying to get it under her eyeball. Never had she felt such pain. She fought with all her might, but his abhorrent strength pinned her down. Bathed in unbearable agony, she lost the ability to think, trying and failing to detach herself and retreat inward.

“Jolgen!” Damien shouted and tugged on Jolgen’s knife-wielding arm with his bound hands. Jolgen stopped, blessedly pulling out his knife. He slammed Damien back hard into the van’s wall. The hound barked.

“What the hell are you doing?” shouted another voice from far away. Maria, from the front of the van. “Jolgen, what the actual fuck?”

“Everything’s fine,” he said, leaning back in toward Sara with the blade in hand.

“It’s not fine!” Maria shouted. “Do you have to screw everything up? We’ll be home in little more than an hour. I don’t need this on my report. Just do your actual job for a change!”

Sara had never heard Maria yell like that. Her heart still pounded, pain and fear flowing through her mind. She was traumatized by the knife, shivering from the agony. Her own warm blood spewed across her cheek and temple, and she watched as it pooled on the floor. She couldn’t even wipe the blood from her eye, and every time she blinked, her cut eyelid flared in pain anew.

Jolgen snarled, paused, then angrily leaned back and wiped his knife on his pants to clean it off before putting it back onto his belt. He looked toward the front of the van, likely at Maria. “I was just messing around.”

Sara, gasping for breath behind her gag, glanced at Damien. His eyes met hers, wide and scared. The worst expression to see on the face of someone you loved was powerlessness. He didn’t know what to do, and neither did she.

For the next half hour of riding, as the road shifted from dirt to some sort of highway, Sara coiled into herself, bringing her knees up to her chest and closing her eyes. Back into a ball on her side, like all those years earlier when Fallon had broken her wrist and choked her out at a reclassification test. Afraid of everything. Afraid to look at Jolgen for fear of his aggression, and afraid to look at Damien for fear of his emotion. Trying to distract herself from the pain. She wanted to die. To not exist anymore. To never have been born in the first place. If she agreed with Jolgen about anything, it was that this world was hell. And he was one of its devils.

Eventually, a woman murmured up front, saying something about the battery running low. The van slowed down on the highway, then began creeping toward what was likely a rest stop. Sara cracked her eyes open.

“Keep them quiet,” Maria said, a haunting lack of emotion back in her voice.

Jolgen smiled at Damien. “Make a sound, and I’ll cut her worse once we get moving again.” He reached his hand up Sara’s shirt and grabbed her. She tensed as a feeling of wrongness surged through her body, but she mentally distanced herself from it. He was toying with her. She’d take the hand on her skin rather than the knife in her eye, given the choice. The van stopped, probably at the charging station, though she couldn’t see well through the tiny windows in the back doors of the van.

She weighed her options for escape. She could scream in a muffled way and attract attention. But Maria and Jolgen might kill everyone here. Would the place have cameras? Could police track them? If they did, would General Price just make the problem go away?

She glanced over at Damien, and he shook his head slowly. No.

After the battery had been charged, Maria spoke to the van driver. “Pull behind the convenience store. I’ll switch and sit in the back with them now. Jolgen’s making a mess back there.”

Jolgen frowned. “I’m just—”

“It’s literally nonstop!” Maria shouted. “It’s always been like this. You make easy things hard for the rest of us.”

The van meandered about, then came to a slow stop again. Maria and the guards got out. Jolgen’s hand still lingered on Sara, getting ready to pull away as he looked toward the back doors, and she got an idea. His pistol was right there, in his holster. It was heavier than she could normally lift, but if she tried her absolute hardest, she might be able to levitate it a couple of feet over to Damien. His hands were bound in front, so he could wield it. It was a long shot, but with Maria outside of the van, this seemed like the last opportunity they had. She doubted the plan’s chances, and wanted to run it by Damien, but she couldn’t speak and Jolgen was right there, looking away. It was now or never.

She concentrated. It should’ve been the most difficult lift of her life, but to her surprise, it was easy. She made a gripping motion with her fist behind her back, visualizing it around Jolgen’s holstered pistol as her focus reached toward it, and pulled it out. Effortless.

Huh? It felt like lifting air. It was nothing. Easier than even picking it up with her own hand.

She mentally moved the gun over to Damien, and his eyes went wide. He readied his hands to grip it, determination settling into his features. As the silent, flying gun reached him, he grabbed it and pointed it at Jolgen’s head.

But at the last second Jolgen flicked his eyes toward the gun, ducked to the side with blinding speed, took the shot in his armored shoulder, and bashed Damien across the temple.

The world stopped, then crawled forward in unnatural slow motion. Every detail intensified, followed by time catching up all at once with a sickening pop.

Damien’s head whipped to the side and flopped around. His eyes went blank, and his body collapsed to the van floor.

Sara screamed into her gag. Jolgen widened his eyes. Two guards opened the back doors of the van and looked in.

“What did you do?” Maria shouted, coming around to the two guards in the back a second later. The hound started barking again, the sound coming from the van’s second row.

“They tried to pull my gun!” Jolgen answered as he stepped out of the back of the van, almost stumbling. He turned around and looked at them, a panicked expression on his face.

“Did you . . . we’re screwed,” Maria said, frozen, staring at Damien.

Sara’s entire life rushed through her thoughts. She looked over at Damien, and his face stared back at her, lying on the van floor, eyes lifeless, his neck at an unnatural angle. Dead. From just one hit by Jolgen. Damien had been here with her moments ago, and now he was gone. Snuffed out so easily, leaving her alone.

Damien. Was. Dead. Her world . . . ended.

“Jolgen, we are so . . .” Maria began. Then she looked over at Sara.

Sara sat up and concentrated on Jolgen. She planted her bracers, gripped her fist behind her back, and mentally pushed with one of her foci.

Jolgen flew back with more speed than she’d ever seen into the store’s concrete wall. Killed on impact, the back of his head shattered with a loud crack. His body slid down to the ground, leaving a trail of blood and bits of brain on the fractured wall. The hound’s barking grew louder.

Something was different. Everything was easier. Her mind felt clearer. Why had Jolgen’s gun been so easy to move? Why was his heavy body so weightless to her now? The things she gripped felt lighter than paper, and her heart pounded so hard it seemed as though it would burst from her chest.

Maria’s expression turned from shock to ferocity. She bared her teeth and pushed out her hand, sending one of her foci toward Sara. The two other guards lifted their assault rifles toward Sara as well, fear clear on their faces.

In response, Sara used one of her foci for offense and one for defense. She wasn’t used to pushing bodies, let alone multiple bodies. It was hard to know where to best grip. She thought of her water tests at the facility pool. Clare had taught her how to move water itself, which helped her manipulate complex objects, and more numerous ones. She conceptualized a grip on all three of them.

Maria’s push was about to reach Sara first, but she grabbed and nullified Maria’s oncoming focus with her defensive focus as easily as she would have stopped a child from pushing on her. The telekinetic equivalent of grabbing Maria’s wrist with her hand to block it.

As Sara drained energy from the air to perform her offensive push, frost settled on the van’s floor. She shoved that kinetic energy toward Maria and the guards, trying to restrain herself, since she didn’t want to kill them and didn’t understand this new power. Maria tried shielding herself and the guards with her second focus, but Sara pierced straight through that attempt. With their guns about to fire at her, she had to act fast.

The remaining force that broke through was . . . far too much. Maria’s eyes went blank, and blood shot out of her back, through her armor, spraying onto the wall. The blood of the two guards on either side of her did the same. Red gore painted the wall and the ground alike. Sara had meant to grip and push their three bodies back, but by focusing so much on water, she had mainly gripped their blood and insides by mistake. And she’d pushed it all back with insane force compared to what she’d intended, to get through Maria’s defense. How had she become so strong?

Maria and the two guards toppled to the asphalt like discarded marionettes, their lifeless bodies dead before impact. Maria’s head made a floppy crack as it landed, staring open-eyed as a line of blood oozed from the corner of her mouth.

Sara glanced over at Jolgen again. His body rested motionlessly against the wall. Catching her breath, she looked at Damien, as though somehow all of this might make him come back to life, but his eyes just stared to the side. There was no life to be found.

Focusing on her own hands, she mentally crushed the plasticuffs’ connector to free them. Then she ripped the tape off her mouth. “Damien!” she screamed, clutching his shirt and shaking him. “Damien!”

She heard the front left van door open. The driver, she realized.

An eerie silence set in, and neither she nor the driver moved. The hound had even stopped barking. Sara inched toward the back of the van and stepped out while readying one of her foci to push against any potential gunshots, widening its tip into a shield-like shape as she’d seen Fallon do, and making sure it was backed by enough force to counter a bullet on each square inch. It took an excessive amount of energy, but she somehow had so much of it to spare.

As soon as she rounded the van’s corner, a bang sounded out. The bullet stopped midair against her shield. The driver fired again, but that one stopped as well. Both bullets began falling toward the ground.

With fury churning through her mind, Sara’s first instinct was to thrust the falling bullets straight back through the guard’s armored chest. She intuitively felt that she could push the bullets faster than the gun had shot them, by an order of magnitude. She used her second focus to grip them while keeping her shield up with her first focus, but then she looked up at the face.

It was Jessica. The auburn-haired woman she’d choked out when escaping the facility. The guard Damien had wanted to spare.

Jessica lowered her pistol and looked around at the gore. “You monster,” she whispered, trembling.

Sara smiled, despite feeling nothing but rage. She, a monster?

Jessica tightened her jaw and stood up straighter. The hound began barking again from the middle of the van. Sara glanced at it, and it quieted, making only a faint whimper and then nothing.

She turned back to the guard and examined the details of her face. Was she ready to die? Killing someone felt as easy as glancing in their direction now, as far as her strange new powers were concerned. She could crush her throat, push her back with fatal force, or shoot a focus through her chest like an invisible spear. Maybe just rip the blood out again. There were multiple ways, all of them effortless.

Was this how Fallon had always felt? No, this amount of power seemed beyond even hers.

Jessica swallowed and met Sara’s eyes. “I . . . have a son,” she said. “He’s six.”

Sara kept staring. Normally that would have hit her hard, but she felt shockingly unconcerned. What did a single life matter? Damien was dead. Maria too. There were supposedly nine billion people in this world. Every guard she killed probably had a kid. Jessica had chosen to work at a black-ops genetic facility. Was she supposed to feel sympathetic now?

“So what?” Sara asked. “I don’t need witnesses.”

Jessica’s eyes widened, and Sara wondered what she looked like to her at this moment. Blood had dried across her face from Jolgen’s knife cuts earlier, and red-stained strands of blond hair crisscrossed her vision. Her slitted green eyes probably looked as though they glowed, light reflecting off of them from the parking lot lamps in the distance.

Jessica slowly put her pistol on the ground. “Look, I . . . don’t want to leave him alone. He doesn’t have a father. Can you understand?”

Sara tilted her head, watching Jessica put the gun down, studying her face as she spoke. Her own makeshift family was gone. Why should she care about this woman’s family? She pictured Damien’s blank, dead face, and her fury renewed itself. But then . . . that same face again. Damien was the one who’d insisted on trying to spare this woman to begin with. She couldn’t override his intention like that.

“Take off your boots,” Sara said.

“What?”

“Your boots. Take them off. And your gear belt. And vest.” She looked down at her own bare feet on the asphalt, standing in a pool of her victims’ blood. She’d never gotten a chance to put her shoes back on once they were captured in the forest, and didn’t even know where they’d ended up.

After a brief hesitation, Jessica unclasped her gear belt and dropped it to the ground, next to her pistol. Still trembling, she took off her armored vest followed by each boot, one by one. When she finished, she stood in her socks on the asphalt, avoiding the bloody area. Sara let the two bullets that she held aloft drop to the ground, hitting with two metallic clicks, followed by the sound of one of them rolling.

“His name’s Max,” Jessica said. “My son.”

“I don’t care,” Sara said, looking down at the gear. “Run.”

“Where?”

“Not here. Before I change my mind.” She flicked her eyes from the gear on the ground back up to Jessica’s face.

Jessica’s eyes went wide again, and she stepped back. She turned and opened the van’s middle door, and got the hound, which had remained quiet as death. Then she turned and ran, with the sound of her socks slapping on the pavement, along with the jingling of the hound’s collar. All the way to the tree line.

Sara looked around. A black van, some of its doors open, with lights on inside. Blood and bodies everywhere. Damien.

She went to the back of the van and looked at him. Still in the same position. She crawled in and checked his pulse. Nothing. A cut marred his temple, his eyes were vacant, and his neck rested at a strange angle.

“Damien,” she whispered, her eyes growing wet. “Please come back to me.”

She pushed down on his chest several times, then blew into his mouth. And repeated. And repeated. And checked his pulse. He was a corpse. After twenty-one years of life, he was gone, as fast as that. Almost by accident.

Sara lowered her head, tears dripping from her clenched eyes. Her heartbeat wasn’t pounding anymore; it’d gone eerily slow and soft. Rage had drained away into emptiness. As Damien lay there dead, she died with him. Her future—their future—was gone.

Regaining her composure after a few breaths, she looked around. This was a public place. The police would come soon.

Well, maybe I should kill them all when they do, she thought. Then she shook her head. No. Their plan had been to escape, get help, and go back for Clare and Marcus, others too, and shine a light on that wretched place. Damien was dead, and Sara with him, but that plan still existed. If she were to fail, it would mean Damien had failed. Stallard would turn his intentions toward Marcus and repeat everything that Damien had feared for the world. That malicious singularity, or whatever. That dark god.

She climbed out of the back of the van and glanced around again. Looking at Damien, she exhaled and mentally lifted his body out of the van, placing him on the ground away from the gore. Seeing him still bound, she mentally ripped apart his plasticuffs and threw them aside. She crouched down next to him, and with her hands she moved his arms to rest them peacefully at his sides. She closed his eyelids with her fingers and leaned down to kiss him one last time.

Damien, she thought. I’m so sorry.

The silence was unbearable. As she put on Jessica’s boots, holster, and vest, with her hooded sweatshirt on top, she ran through her actions to get away from it. It’d been a mistake to go for Jolgen’s gun. It was her fault that Damien was dead. And when had she gained this power? Why couldn’t she have realized it minutes earlier? What was going on?

She reached up and touched her face, feeling the rough, dry blood and the sting of torn flesh. Everything else felt so numb that the sharp spike of pain from her fingers touching her sliced skin almost felt refreshing. A painful jolt of life amid a numb sea of death.

She walked over to Jolgen’s body, uncaring about stepping through the blood, and looked down into his blank eyes. He stared out like a fool, mouth agape. His death made the world better. But she didn’t feel the satisfaction that she’d imagined she would after all these years.

She pointed Jessica’s pistol at his forehead and pulled the trigger, partially to make sure he was deader than dead, but really to see if it would give her a rush.

That’s for Clare, she thought, as the gunshot rattled her ears. But she felt nothing. Only frustration. The bullet casing clinked on the ground, bounced twice and rolled for a moment, then left her with more silence.

She wanted to break something, wanted to shatter the world. Her eyes landed on the van, sitting there so uselessly. She gripped its chassis with a focus and mentally hurled it, her arm moving and body twisting as if throwing a fastball.

The metal chassis moaned as the van tore from the ground. It soared silently through the night air, hundreds of feet, before smashing down at the far end of the rest stop in a burst of glass and steel. The sound, violent and raw, barely began to quench what she craved. There was no headache. No strain. It’d felt easier than lifting her paper cranes, and she didn’t know why.

Sirens whined in the distance. It was time to go, or she’d have to start killing police as they came. She planted one of her bracers on the ground, used her corresponding focus to lift herself carefully, and began flying a few feet off the ground toward the tree line to make herself harder to track. Behind her, the van exploded into flames.

She felt like a different person. Dead, but reborn.







Part III





Lost and Found








Chapter 29



Two hours after Jade’s arrest, Asim found himself at a military police station in Fort Hamilton, a small Army base on Brooklyn’s coast. Although it wasn’t set up for it properly, it was the closest installation capable of temporarily holding someone as dangerous as Jade. From the moment of the arrest, he’d started making calls to his bosses, and after a quick interagency coordination between INSCOM and the Stolguard facility, this was the chosen spot for now.

Stallard was flying in via helicopter, and much to Asim’s frustration, he’d been given a direct order from Major General Scholl not to interrogate Jade until Stallard arrived. The order likely came from above even her.

Jade sat handcuffed to a chair, blindfolded, with six soldiers surrounding her with rifles. One of them held the base’s only laser rifle, aimed squarely at her back at all times, and there were dozens more soldiers on standby.

As the next best thing he could do, Asim took a seat across from Veronica in the next room over, since she had also been arrested. A strong but pleasant scent of frankincense and flowers suffused the air around her.

“I want my phone call,” Veronica said, chewing gum. It wasn’t clear where she’d gotten it; she had been searched. She crossed her arms and tapped her foot impatiently, as though she was the one being inconvenienced here. Asim, Ava, and a sergeant named Durst who worked at this place were in the room with her.

“You’re not owed one; this isn’t that kind of arrest,” Asim said. “You’re in a military police station, and this is a national security matter. Unless you start talking and help me understand what’s going on, you’ll be in a world of trouble. And where’d you get that gum?”

“What about my cat?” she asked. “Scorpio.”

“Officers are searching your apartment as we speak,” Durst said. “The cat’s probably been transferred to animal services, and you can reclaim it later if you’re released.”

“They better take good care of him. Can I have tea or somethin’?” she asked. “Which one of you is the good cop in this scene?” Her eyes darted to each of them.

Asim reached up and pinched the bridge of his nose. He was bruised and sore from several unnecessary punches to the face, and he would much rather have been talking to Jade right now.

“I can go get her some from the kitchen area, if that’s okay, Sergeant Durst,” Ava said. Durst nodded, and Ava walked out.

“There’s the good cop,” Veronica said.

Asim cleared his throat. “Look, Veronica, this can—”

“It’s Jitters to you, asshole.”

“Look. Jitters. This can go smoothly. I can be a good cop too. I thought for weeks that you were either captive or dead, and we worked so hard to find you. I certainly didn’t expect you to be harboring this terrorist like a friend. What happened here?”

Her foot-tapping intensified. She bit her lip, looking first at Asim, then at Durst, then back at Asim. “Oh, I was a captive all right,” she said. “Just a cooperative one on account of not wantin’ to get magically strangled. What do they call it? Stockholm Syndrome? I had a case of that stuff. Real bad.”

Ava came back in with a paper cup filled with green tea and put it on the table next to Veronica.

“Thanks a bunch, lovely,” Veronica said with a wink. “At least someone around here’s got manners.” Ava blushed and sat down.

“Jitters. You’re in a dangerous position here,” Asim said. “I have no desire to bring trouble to you, but trouble’s coming unless I do something to stop it. Personally, I don’t give a shit about your muggings or illegal sex work. I’m focused on national security. If you help me make sense of what went on here, I might be able to get you off easy.”

Veronica sipped her tea and smirked.

“We have an arrest warrant out for Aisha, too,” Asim said. “She’s the listed owner of that apartment unit. Did she know she harbored a terrorist?”

“I want immunity,” Veronica said, leaning forward. “I’ll tell you everything, and you let me go. Scorpio is a gentle soul. He needs me.”

“That’s not how this works. I can’t simply let you go. But, depending on what you tell me, I can strongly push things in the right direction. My focus is on keeping people safe, not whatever else you’re into.”

She narrowed her eyes and bit her lip again, then made a show of fixing her voluminous hair for several seconds as she leaned back. “What do you wanna know?”

“Why were you helping Jade?” Asim asked.

“Her name’s Sara,” Veronica said. “Or at least it used to be. Managed to pry that outta her on the first night. Jade’s just what the media calls her. Aren’t you a detective?”

Asim eyed Ava. She was taking notes. Sara was a new name to them in this case. “Okay, why were you helping Sara?” Asim asked.

“Well, at first she made me,” Veronica said. “She was bein’ all scary that first night, but then I saw her face had been gashed open. I was scared at first, but then I realized she only needed some stitches and a warm place to sleep. Aisha’s a nurse. So, I told the girl to put away the pistol, that she wouldn’t need that with me, and to come to our place for the night. I said I’d take care of her.”

Asim glanced over at Durst, then Ava, before looking back to Veronica. “So, you invited a murderer back to your home?”

“Well, technically Aisha’s home. But yeah. She wasn’t happy about me bringin’ back a stray at first, but I told Sara to just not talk that night, on account of her being so creepy when she talks, and that I’d handle it. Aisha agreed to let her stay the night and stitched up her face and arm, and then I got Aisha to extend the stay.”

“How’d you convince her?”

Veronica shrugged. “I know a thing or two about gettin’ people to see things my way.”

Asim thought for a moment. “We saw that your street colleague’s bitcoin moved from one blockchain address to another two days after his death in the alley. That was you, right?” He purposely overstated it; they only had an 87 percent confidence estimate that the bitcoin belonged to him in the first place, and they weren’t sure that Veronica was the one to move it.

“I, um.” Her face went stiff.

Bingo. “Did you move it, or did someone else?” Asim asked.

She started tapping her foot again. “Well, I don’t wanna get Sara in trouble . . .”

“She’s already in trouble, including for killing your colleagues in the alley.”

Veronica eyed him. “Those thugs she, uh, dealt with . . . Sara grabbed their stuff, and I told her that one of them carries a lotta bitcoin on his phone. And his ring’s got a hidden key for it, too. I offered to show her what I know about how he stores it and said we could split it three ways if we can put the pieces together and get it. So, I showed her, and we figured it out.”

“Thugs?” Asim asked. “Weren’t they your partners? Your crew?”

“Not really,” Veronica said. “I, uh, heh. Trust me, there’s no love lost there. They made life hard for folks like me. I was only workin’ with them on the temp to help pay off a friend’s debt. Being free of them is pretty good, you know?” She took a long sip from her tea and crossed one long leg over the other, more relaxed.

“So, you’re claiming you did this out of pragmatism. Sara killed your colleagues and threatened you, but you responded instead with kindness and shifted the nature of the encounter toward a milder direction. You became less of a captive, and more of a helper. And with the bitcoin, you got Aisha onboard and benefited yourself in the process.”

“Well, that’s kind of a fancy-pants way of sayin’ it, but yeah. The girl just needed some care is all.”

“What happened in the days that followed?”

“Well, first I got Aisha to calm down and ignore Sara’s weird eyes and the creepy things she would say. The bitcoin plan made it worth everyone’s while. Sara cleaned herself up good and had a meal, and Aisha stitched her cuts. Then Sara was gonna give herself a buzzcut as a disguise and go on the run, but I said that would be a crime given how cute she was. She didn’t care, but I certainly did. So, I convinced her to dye it instead, and then I did it for her since I know a thing or two. From blond to black. Well, technically very dark brown. If you dye it pure black, then you get that inky gothic look which looks like shit you know, while very dark brown gives you that natural black hair look. I told her that would stand out less than a buzz cut. And—”

“Are you aware that she attacked NewsCon and the Pentagon in the subsequent weeks? She’s killed about a hundred people.”

“Oh, was that her?” Veronica said with a confident smile.

Asim frowned.

“Hey, it’s not polite to pry into roommates’ private matters,” she said. “And as you may have noticed, she’s not the easiest person to talk to. What she gets up to on her own time is her business.”

“It’s a felony to harbor someone sought on a felony warrant,” Asim said. “That’s worth several years in prison. Why didn’t you or Aisha call the police? You had several opportunities.”

“She was convincin’. She said I might have been compromised by surveillance, so I should lie low. She said Aisha should keep actin’ normally. Said if we turned on her, she would get violent, so we shouldn’t go there.”

“What about when she left the apartment to commit her crimes? Why not contact the police then?”

Veronica shrugged, and rotated the foot of her crossed-over leg in slow circles as she spoke. “I mean, she could come back and find us. And, uh, she did seem to have some good reasons for whatever she may or may not have been up to.”

“Such as?”

“Stoppin’ the end of the world or some such. From a robot god, I think. Or a cyborg god, I forget which one.” She scratched her head and frowned in thought. “Look, she’s weird as hell and barely speaks, but she was nice enough to Aisha and me. And Scorpio, too. He’s a great judge of character, Scorpio is, and he liked her a whole lot. Turns out she’d never seen a cat in real life before, and she pet him whenever he went over to her. Can you believe that? Someone never seein’ a cat? Imagine watchin’ that interaction for the first time.”

“So basically, you could have contacted the police but didn’t want to. I bet . . . it’s because Sara controlled the address that the bitcoin was moved to, and she didn’t divvy it out yet, did she? It was like a bribe that you wouldn’t get if you turned her in. You and Aisha convinced yourselves that her motivations were good enough and that you weren’t doing anything wrong because . . . she was fun to watch with cats?”

“Like I said, Stockholm Syndrome,” Veronica said with a mischievous smile. “A real bad case. I was so scared and vulnerable and latched onto what I could to survive, you know?”

Asim sighed and decided to shift this in a different direction. “Why is she so sickly looking?”

“That’s not polite.”

He raised his eyebrows. “She’s lost weight rapidly since the day you two met. From her newsroom appearance to her Pentagon assault, and from then to now.”

“Because she don’t eat,” she said.

“She was literally eating when I came in today.”

“Barged in, is more like it.”

Asim leaned back, crossed his arms, and waited for more.

“It’s not that she never eats. She just . . . barely eats. Maybe one day a week.”

“Do you know why?”

“Not sure. She just don’t want to. Makes her sick, apparently. I kept tryin’ to get her to eat more. Even offered to cook all sorts of fancy things. I’m a pretty good cook, you know. Honestly. But she rarely would. I’m worried about her. She might have cancer or somethin’. Maybe radiation related to her superpowers?”

“Why doesn’t she have most of her telekinesis now?”

“I don’t know. That’s news to me.” She shrugged. “I thought for sure she’d snap your neck with her mind when you barged in.”

“Do you know what her next move was going to be?” Asim asked. “An initial search of your place found that she’d looked up various special forces military bases in the country, as well as military R&D funding hubs, with sketched diagrams for them that might represent attack plans. And she had lists of politicians with various notes on them that my team is still looking through. She apparently searched for ones with anti-military positions. Maybe seeking allies?”

“She didn’t talk about any of that type of stuff. Or almost anythin’ else, really. She said it would be better for us if we didn’t know. And I stayed inside, lettin’ Aisha handle all our outside needs. Sara was firm about that, what with all the cameras out in the world.”

Asim heard activity out in the corridor. He looked at Durst, then stood and opened the door to check.

Stallard had arrived with four armored operatives, all wearing sunglasses. Two women and two giant men, the latter being roughly seven feet tall each. The men carried laser rifles, while the women had holstered pistols. Stallard himself had a standard assault rifle slung by a cord around his shoulder.

“Where is she?” Stallard asked, looking around.

The senior noncommissioned officer in charge of the military police station, a woman in her fifties Asim had already met, stepped forward and offered her hand. “I’m Master Sergeant Skylar Smith. Dr. Stallard, I presume? We have two of your suspects in these two rooms here, and a third on the way.”

Stallard gave her a distracted handshake and turned toward the two rooms she’d pointed at. None of his four operatives removed their sunglasses, despite being indoors. Asim wagered a guess what color their eyes were. Stallard had come here packing some serious power.

“Santiago, go check,” Stallard said. The largest man nodded and walked over to the room where Jade—Sara?—was held, and went in. “Colonel Rahal, did I understand your report correctly? Her abilities are mostly drained?”

“It seems that way, Doctor,” Asim said. “Other than a small tug on my rifle, she didn’t use telekinesis while I arrested her, despite it unfortunately turning rather violent. But I recognize her face up close from the Pentagon; it’s the same person. And I’ve obtained initial answers from her roommate—or captive, depending on how you look at it—but we’ve held off on interrogating Jade as ordered.”

“I’ll handle the interrogation,” Stallard said. “When I’m finished, I’ll provide you with a redacted version to help close your case out.”

Asim gritted his teeth. This wasn’t what he’d been told by his bosses. “This case falls squarely within ACI jurisdiction, Doctor. I get to be present for any interrogation.”

“Nobody gets to be present,” Stallard said. He reached into his beige trench coat pocket and pulled out a phone, then displayed a code on the screen. “This is an emergency authorization from the Secretary of Defense for private enhanced interrogation techniques, justified for national security, and because the subject is not legally a citizen. We must determine the precise nature of the threat immediately.”

That particularly large man, Santiago, came out of Jade’s interrogation room. “It’s her,” he said.

“Okay, go in,” Stallard said, gesturing to the others. “Master Sergeant Smith, was it? Rotate your men out and disconnect the camera feeds from that room. I need privacy for this.” Santiago, along with the other large man and both of Stallard’s women, went into Jade’s room, sunglasses still on.

“I’ll need to scan that code to validate it, Doctor,” Smith said. Stallard held out his phone, she scanned it with hers, and the approval ping verified that it was signed by the Secretary of Defense’s key. “Very well,” she said, though she didn’t look happy about it.

Asim couldn’t stand to stay there. He slammed open the front door and walked out of the military police building. The crisp autumn air of Fort Hamilton helped clear his head. Pacing back and forth, he tried to think as gulls squawked stupidly overhead.

Then he called Brigadier General Davis.

“Yes, Colonel?” Davis answered.

“Sir, Stallard’s not letting me have access to the interrogation at all. I followed orders to hold off until he arrived, but now he’s going around me. This is ACI jurisdiction, too.”

“This came from the top,” Davis said. “From Major General Scholl, and above her to General Rodriguez and the SecDef himself. Believe me, I fought as best as I could here to get you access. There’s nothing I can do. They’ve managed to keep the FBI away from the whole base for now, too.”

“They’re going to torture her before I even get a chance to ask anything. She hesitated to answer my questions in prior encounters because she was concerned that anything she said would be used to find her. Now that she’s in custody, I believe I can get her to actually talk. But they’re going to mess that up. I don’t trust Stallard at all. Sir.”

“Prior encounters?” Davis asked.

Shit. He hadn’t wanted to reveal that yet. “It’s a long story, sir.” Asim waited. Silence on the line, lasting seconds.

“Look, I’ll try again from my side, but no promises,” Davis said finally.

“Thank you, sir.” Jesus Christ.

After hanging up, Asim turned and punched the brick wall of the building. Hard enough to break skin and draw blood.

“Fuck!” he shouted, even angrier now thanks to the pain. He went back to pacing instead, shaking out his hand. If he could speak to Jade now, he knew he’d get somewhere with her and bring clarity to this absolute clusterfuck of a situation. What little trust he’d manage to establish with her was being shattered in there.

A few minutes later, Master Sergeant Smith came out, sighed, and looked around. She nodded politely, then pulled out a pack of cigarettes and gestured for him to take one.

“Thanks, I don’t smoke,” he said, leaning against the wall. “Probably not a bad day to start, though.”

She chuckled, lit one for herself, and exhaled a long plume as she leaned against the wall next to him. “I don’t like this any more than you do, Colonel. I certainly don’t need one of those documentaries coming out about how torture occurred under my watch.”

“Walking in there, sunglasses on indoors like they’re all from the fucking Matrix, and doing whatever they want,” Asim said.

“What’s that, sir?” she asked.

“An old movie. Good one. And you can drop the sirs out here. Doesn’t fucking matter.”

“Ah, I think I’ve heard of it.”

They stood in silence for a while as she continued to smoke.

“Let me know if you need anything, Colonel,” she said when she finished. He nodded, she went back inside, and he stayed out there, thinking. Eventually, Ava came out, face pale. “I can hear screams coming from the room now, sir.”

Asim rubbed his temple. He’d never felt this helpless. He took a deep breath and went back inside, and Ava followed. At first, he heard nothing, but after a few moments a faint scream reached his ears. He stepped back into Veronica’s room.

“What are they doin’ to her?” Veronica asked, eyes wide. It was just her and Durst in here, both looking uncomfortable.

“I don’t know,” Asim said, barely sparing her a glance. He grabbed a chair, dragged it over to the wall that separated Jade’s room from Veronica’s, and took a seat with his head leaning back against the wall, eyes closed. He couldn’t be in Jade’s room, but he could still try to listen. Because, well, fuck Stallard.



After more than an hour of hearing occasional gurgles and screams—and laughs?—from the torture room, Ava felt sick to her stomach.

This day had started surprisingly well. But now their case had practically been stolen from them, and in the most horrifying way.

“Who the hell keeps laughing in there?” Colonel Rahal asked, breaking a long silence in the room and glancing around. He hadn’t looked this angry in years.

“That sounds like Sara, actually,” Veronica said. “She laughed a couple times when Aisha stitched up her face cuts, and when she tended to her shoulder burn. I told you she’s weird.”

“I don’t feel great. I’m going to use the lavatory,” Ava said, standing.

She left the room, walked down the hall, and entered the lavatory. After using the facilities, she splashed some cold water on her face to calm down and prepare herself for what she was about to do.

On the way back, she walked into the wrong room as though it was by accident. Sara’s room. Just barged right in with a smile past a shocked hallway guard before he had time to respond.

“Colonel, do you thi—Oh,” she said, looking up in mock surprise as the guard finally reached in front of her chest to hold her back. The smaller of the two female operatives held her palm a few inches from Sara’s shoulder wound, which had fresh blood dripping out of it as Sara thrashed around and bit her lip. She was still handcuffed to the chair, still blindfolded, and her ankles had now been duct-taped to the chair legs. Her black-dyed hair was soaked, and the floor had puddles of water all around. The room smelled of stale sweat.

“Again. What triggered your . . .” said the small woman, holding her palm to Sara’s wound. Dr. Stallard gestured as though to stop her from talking, and everyone turned to look at the doorway.

“Sorry,” Ava said with what she hoped was an apologetic face. She backed out, and the other woman in the room made a motion with her hand. The door magically swung shut inches from her face.

The guard next to her stood there, mouth agape. Ava met his eyes, raised her eyebrows, and shrugged emphatically. “Oops. Wrong door. It’s been a long day.” He was young and worked at this little military base rather than for Dr. Stallard, so she wasn’t sure if he was more rattled by the sight of torture or her intrusion. Either way, she patted him on the shoulder and went back to Veronica’s interrogation room next door.

“I heard some commotion in there,” Colonel Rahal said as she entered.

“That was me, sir. I accidentally walked in on them. These rooms don’t lock from the inside, so that detainees can’t barricade themselves in if left alone. This station wasn’t really built for war crimes. Anyway, they’re peeling open her shoulder burn wound. I think they’ve been waterboarding her, too. They’re asking her what triggered . . . something. It was cut short by my entry.”

“Triggered?”

“Her defection, her powers, her killing spree—something like that maybe, sir.”

“Doesn’t Stallard already know about her powers? He certainly knows her reason for defection, and her killing spree,” he said. “Unless she lied to me.”

Ava shrugged. “I don’t know, sir.”







Chapter 30



Asim waited, feeling tension mount with each passing minute. After the second hour in the room, Stallard finally sent out one of his operatives—he’d heard Stallard call him Santiago—for Master Sergeant Smith.

“Dr. Stallard is finished now. He requests the camera feeds be turned back on and for the other soldiers to be sent back in to relieve us from guard duty,” Santiago said.

Asim made sure to pre-position himself in the corridor to catch this. Stallard and the rest of his operatives came out, but Stallard went straight to the men’s restroom, and his other male operative followed as a sole bodyguard. After a minute, Asim followed.

At the sinks, rinsing his hands beside Stallard, Asim spoke. “You know, it’s pretty fucking stupid to jump straight to bad cop, when good cop is an option. I might’ve been able to get what you’re looking for out of her.”

“What makes you think I failed to acquire what I need?” Stallard asked.

“Your shit mood.”

Stallard paused and eyed him. “Well, my determination is that she’s too dangerous to transport or keep in custody, since the answers to certain questions elude us. I’m going to motion to have her put down tonight. If she had given me those answers, the outcome could have been different. I don’t relish having to do any of this. It’s out of necessity.”

Asim’s chest went tight. “You can’t just—”

“Are you slow of learning, Colonel? She’s not protected by the same rights as citizens are, especially given what she has done and how much attention she has brought. Certain risks cannot be taken at this scale. You are out of your depth on this.”

“Give me one chance,” Asim said. “You and your goons can be in the room. Unlike you, I don’t have that many secrets to hide. I’ll ask a couple of questions for you, and a couple of questions for my unit to have closure. I have a rapport with her. Or had, I guess.”

Stallard seemed to think as he dried his hands. “I’ll give you five minutes, Colonel. Her telekinesis was once trivial, but then it surpassed all my other subjects’, including my best. I need to know how, and why she seems to have lost it again. Has she been hiding it all along? Or did it emerge somehow, and what was the trigger if so? She cannot be safely transported or securely held in custody unless I know this information. That is my reason for this distasteful business.”

“Ten minutes,” Asim said. “I’ll ask that for you, and a few other questions, and you can have your people present.”

“Five.” He turned toward his bodyguard. “Carter, go tell the master sergeant to reverse the prior order. Have her cut the camera feed and send her soldiers out of the room again.” The big man nodded and walked out. Once they were alone, Stallard turned back toward Asim. “Whatever her appearance, remember they are weapons, Colonel. Underneath their masks, they’re designed to kill.”

“And yet they still feel pain,” Asim said.

Stallard sighed and walked toward the door.

“I have to ask,” Asim said. “Why do you have a standard rifle rather than a laser, when you obviously know the nature of the threat?”

Stallard looked over his shoulder. “My back is too old for that kind of thing, Colonel. Those heavy battery packs are for the young. But as I’ve said, telekineticists can be overwhelmed by threats from multiple directions. I know my way around a firearm when necessary.”

“Fair enough,” Asim said. The old man was tougher than he looked, perhaps.

They left the restroom, and Asim went straight to Jade’s room. She still sat in the same chair as before, though now she was slumped over, leaning forward. Her hair and shirt were wet, and a line of blood oozed from the wound on her right shoulder. Her thin face was swollen and bruised from their fight in Aisha’s apartment. Three of her fingernails had been ripped out. She seemed to be unconscious, though with the blindfold it was hard to tell for sure.

After a few minutes of commotion and setup, it was just Asim, Stallard, and his four operatives in there with Jade. “Take off her blindfold, please,” Asim said.

“Absolutely not,” Stallard said.

“If she had her powers, she would have used them at some point in the past couple hours of agony, don’t you think?”

“It’s not worth the risk.”

“It is if we want true answers. I’ll take that risk. Maybe that’s your problem.” Asim got up and untied Jade’s blindfold himself. Stallard nodded to his people to let him do it.

Her eyes were closed. She remained slumped forward, wet and bloody, but she stirred a bit, as though in a dream.

“You guys really fucked this up,” Asim said. “Jade. Or, Sara. Can you hear me?” As violent as she was, Asim couldn’t help but see a woman not much older than his own daughter in the chair, which gave him a chill. He tapped her cheek lightly, then did it again more firmly, and her eyes opened a bit. “Here, drink this,” he said, holding a cup of water to her lips. “I’m sorry.”

She hesitated, eyes barely open, but then sniffed the cup and drank. Asim noticed that Stallard had quietly positioned his two big men with laser rifles to stand behind her, holding their guns toward her back, outside of her field of view. Stallard himself stood behind her as well. Smart. That left just Asim and the two female operatives in her field of view. They probably had powers like hers.

“Sara, is it?” Asim asked.

She blinked several times and squinted, seemingly sensitive to the light. Her pupils were inhumanly large and round rather than the vertical slits he’d grown used to, since she had been without light for a while. That made her look less aggressive. But they swiftly constricted back toward those familiar predatory slits as the ceiling lights shone on them. She slowly glanced left and right, taking in the people behind her, then turned forward again and stared at him through the damp hair hanging over her face.

“You won’t talk to me?” he asked.

“Why would I?” she whispered. Her voice was hoarse.

“I tried to prevent this from happening to you,” he said.

“You put me here. I should’ve killed you at the Pentagon. My mistake.”

“You’re at risk of being put down tonight. All you have to do is answer a few questions and you’ll prevent that,” he said. “It’s not my decision. I’m trying to help.”

She still stared at him, unblinking now. She looked exhausted rather than frightened.

“Why did your telekinesis grow strong, then weak again?”

“I don’t know,” she said. “I answered that already.”

“Why are you losing weight?”

“Because I get sick when I eat. My extra power took its toll, I guess. I’m not a scientist.”

“You always had that power, didn’t you?”

“I already told Stallard, no. Why would I have been grappling guards and cutting myself on razor wire if I had this power all along?” She gestured with her chin toward her right shoulder, likely to draw attention to the scars on her right forearm. “It was a temporary deal, apparently.”

“When was that? With the razor wire and guards?”

“When we escaped his facility. A month ago.”

“Who is ‘we’? Where’s the second captive from the rest stop incident?”

She furrowed her brow. “What?”

“There was one African American body found at the scene with marks on his wrists. A captive. And there was evidence of another one missing. Two sets of broken plasticuffs. Footprints. Did you kill that other one, or what happened?” Asim said.

“That was Damien. The second captive was me. Or are you referring to me letting Jessica go? That’s another person I probably shouldn’t have spared.”

Asim scratched his head.

“Jessica is one of Raphael Costa’s guards,” Stallard said from behind Sara. “C17 and Damien left our facility without authorization, and they were being brought back safely by our team, until C17 here killed everyone except that one guard, took her gear, and caused the mayhem you have seen since, Colonel.”

“I said I wasn’t the one who killed Damien!” Sara shouted, her voice still hoarse. She leaned forward with a vicious expression and pulled tight on her steel cuffs against the back of the chair, causing all four operatives in the room to startle. Her eyes grew wet. She squeezed them shut and looked down.

“What do you . . .” Asim began, but he stopped as she started to move again. Slowly this time.

She looked back toward Stallard out of the corner of her scarred left eye. Both his male operatives tensed and pointed their guns more firmly at her. “Damien wanted to escape the hell you were causing him, and that you would bring to the world through him if you kept at it. Until Jolgen killed him. Not me. How many times do I have to say it?” She turned back and stared at each of the two female operatives in front of her. “Zarina. Jolce. Look at me. He only calls you by your names now to use you. None of you know what you’re fighting for, or what’s coming.”

“You speak without knowledge, C17,” Stallard said. “Damien was on the cusp of something truly revolutionary. Marcus as well.”

“A revolutionary level of danger,” Sara said, her eyes glancing down and not meeting anyone’s face. “Damien told you, but you dismissed him. So, he hid the full extent of his abilities from you.” She was smiling now, but her eyes were aggressive, a combination Asim had noticed from her whenever she got pressed. He looked around the room, and one of the women seemed particularly agitated.

“You killed Maria. What did she ever do?” that woman said, as if on cue. The taller one with dark skin. Asim wasn’t sure which was Zarina or Jolce.

“I did,” Sara agreed, looking up at her and softening her voice. “Not on purpose, but to escape. Now, killing Jolgen, that was on purpose.” She looked back over her shoulder at the biggest guy, Santiago, and smiled enough to show her teeth. He stared back at her with an unreadable expression.

“All experiments at the facility are done with utmost caution,” Stallard said. “Damien exaggerates.”

Sara shook her head. “He experienced it. Not you. Anyway, you can all kill me if you want. I don’t care anymore. I’m done trying to protect you from yourselves.”

Asim began to ask another question, but Stallard spoke up. “That’s enough, Colonel. We’re finished here.”

“One more,” Asim said, looking over at Stallard. “Relevant for my case.”

“This has gone off the rails already, Colonel.”

Asim nodded and stood up, then looked back down at Sara and spoke again anyway. “You posted social media messages about domestic assassinations and other things. Would you go on the record for that, if there’s a trial?”

“Yes,” she said, barely more than a whisper.

“This is over,” Stallard said. “Santiago, please remove the colonel. Jolce, put her blindfold back on.”

Asim let Santiago escort him out, and they waited in the corridor with Smith, Ava, and several guards. Asim eyed Ava and discretely signaled for her to slip down the corridor, farther off to the side. She understood.

A few minutes later, Stallard emerged with two more of his operatives, leaving the shorter one apparently named Jolce in the room with Sara.

“Master Sergeant,” Stallard said, pointing back toward the open doorway. “You can rotate your men back in now. We need to plan our next steps.”

“Before you do anything rash like kill her,” Asim said, “I’m going to call my headquarters. We need more time to sort out jurisdictional authority on something so extreme.”

Santiago shifted his gaze toward Asim and tightened his grip on his weapon. “The doctor has already presented authorization.”

Asim took a step forward and looked up at the big man, keeping his voice calm. “For interrogation, not murder. And from a politician who isn’t present. Here, in the flesh, we need more checks first. Unless you feel like causing a scene.”

Santiago held his stare for a few seconds, then glanced toward Stallard. The other two operatives kept their eyes locked on Asim. Smith nervously eyed her own men. Absolutely no one was paying attention to Ava, far off to the side as she was, where Asim had positioned her in case things got out of hand. She had a concealed carry and a surprise angle. As hopelessly outmatched as they were, Asim couldn’t accept not having any options if Stallard’s team decided to get all “black ops” in here.

“Patience, Colonel,” Stallard said, drawing out each syllable. “I’m sure we all have calls to make.” He glanced toward Santiago, then Smith, and back toward Asim. “I grant that C17’s lost power seems genuine. For now, she’s useful alive to understand more details, so I won’t push for deletion tonight. But I need her back at my facility, with more secure conditions and proper equipment.”

Asim felt a flicker of relief. But still, once Stallard brought her to his facility, he’d lose access to her, and the case could go cold forever.

“We’ll make our calls, then,” Asim said, pulling out his phone. “It’s not clear you have authorization to transport her yet.” He pointed toward her room. “And she needs medical attention. Torture authorization or whatever you’re calling it doesn’t last indefinitely.”

Stallard eyed the clock on the wall. “It’s getting late anyway, and I can’t risk bringing her back on a single helicopter in the dark. I’ll organize a larger transport fleet to fly her out tomorrow during daylight, to ensure there is plenty of firepower and visibility. I trust that our jurisdictions will have been fully sorted by then.” He gave Asim a knowing look, then turned toward Smith and softened his voice. “For tonight, keep her sedated, blindfolded, and under heavy guard, Master Sergeant. My operatives will rotate one or two at a time as well, to bolster your defenses.”



An hour later, things had partially settled down.

Stallard had been assigned an undisclosed residence on the base by Fort Hamilton’s commander to retire for the night. Master Sergeant Smith had seen to it that Sara was cleaned up, given medical care, and transferred to more comfortable psychiatric restraints on a bed. She was offered a rations bar but had refused it, then was given a heavy enough dose of sedation to put a horse to sleep. Stallard’s operatives made sure nobody could get a word in with her, as per their boss’s orders.

Veronica and Aisha had been jailed on site for the night in the building’s holding cells. Representatives from the FBI had finally managed to get access to the base and had spent hours questioning them, and Jolce asked them some questions as well, on behalf of Stallard’s team.

Asim had called both Davis and Scholl to update them and try to get their support to push back on Stallard’s unilateral control, but there’d been limited progress on that front. Davis seemed to be in Asim’s corner, but Scholl was not. Since Stallard had the fucking Secretary of Defense on his side, working around him was almost impossible.

Later, a CIA representative arrived, followed by reinforcements from a nearby military base, bringing four more laser rifles and plenty of hands to wield them on rotation. Extra security drones hummed throughout the night sky over the base.

Asim and Ava booked rooms at a small hotel adjacent to Fort Hamilton. After trying to retire at a reasonable hour for the night, Asim couldn’t sleep, so after midnight he grabbed a beer from the mini-bar and walked down to the lobby, stepped outside, and gazed out at the parking lot to think in the fresh coastal night air. As fresh as it could be in Brooklyn, anyway.

“Sir?” came Ava’s voice. He turned to see her sitting on a bench in casual attire. Her hair was loose instead of pulled back into her typical bun, and she tucked her knees up against her chest.

“Can’t sleep either?” Asim asked.

“Not really, sir.” Her voice was quiet.

Asim sighed. “Anything in particular?” He hadn’t seen her this subdued in years, which was unnerving.

Ava shook her head. “None of it seems right.”

He waited for more, but nothing came, so he broke the silence himself. “Jade, or Sara, is dangerous, no doubt. But we mostly know what happened with her case now. The question we need to answer is whether the worst things she’s claiming about Stallard’s program are true. If so, that falls under our jurisdiction. Potential insider threats. An expanded case rather than a solved one.”

“But we’re blocked on all fronts,” Ava said. “All we have are her words. Against everything else.”

He nodded. “Frankly, this kind of shit is why I left foreign work in the first place.” He walked over and sat on the bench beside her, taking a sip of his beer as he did. “I hated feeling queasy after a mission, wondering if I was on the right side or not. With counterintelligence, we’re always on the right side, keeping things secure, both people and data, and that makes things easier. But this one . . . I don’t know what to think.”







Chapter 31



Jade woke up in bed again, still in darkness.

She had slept on and off for a while, but she couldn’t tell how long. Was it still night, or already the next day? Her head was spinning, and exhaustion pulled down like an anchor. The drugs mercifully numbed some of her pain, but they also numbed some of her mind. And she needed her mind, still. A little while longer.

How many guards pointed their guns at her this very moment? And how many wielded those terrible laser types? Was Santiago, or Jolce, or any of the others among them?

It felt strange hearing her name again. Sara. That person seemed so distant. As far as she was concerned, Sara was dead. Monsters didn’t have names.

Despite all the waterboarding, the tearing of her burnt shoulder wound by Jolce, and the ripping of her nails, she’d managed to keep her most important secret to herself. Now she needed time for that secret to take effect. Only a little longer . . .



“Aisha,” Asim said as he walked into the room. “Good morning. We didn’t get to meet yesterday. I’m Asim Rahal. I’d like to understand why you harbored a wanted felon.”

He sat down in an interrogation room across from Aisha, a dark-skinned woman in her early thirties, and smiled as he slid over a cup of coffee. She didn’t have a criminal record, and she worked as a nurse at a Brooklyn hospital. By all accounts, an upstanding citizen.

“I plead the Fifth,” she said, then took a sip of the coffee. “I told the others that last night, too. I’m not as stupid as Jitters to talk without a lawyer.”

“Well, Jitters was quite helpful, actually,” Asim said. “I’d like to ensure she doesn’t get into too much trouble, given how cooperative she was. She already told us everything, but I want to hear it from you as well.”

Aisha crossed her arms, saying nothing.

Asim continued. “It’s just, I’d hate for you to take the fall for this by default since the apartment’s registered under your name. You seem like a good person. The military can do some weird things for unusual cases like this, like wait a couple years to go to trial and keep someone in custody for national security reasons during the whole process.”

She stared at him, too stiffly. Rattled, but trying to hide it.

He shrugged. “I’d really hate to see something like that happen here, you know?”

She studied his face, thinking for a second, and sighed. “Look, I was trying to help someone out. The woman was cut up when Jitters brought her home that night. I didn’t know she’d go on to do what she did. And then what was I supposed to do?”

“I don’t know, call the police, maybe?” Asim asked. “After the newsroom incident when she came back to your place.”

“And risk getting killed?”

“You could have left the apartment for work, called the police, and not returned until she got arrested. This is basic stuff.”

“She could’ve blown up the whole block. That’d put all my neighbors at risk. Plus, if Jitters had tried to leave too, then Sara would have been suspicious. She let me leave for work and other duties, but she convinced Jitters to stay in.”

“She didn’t threaten Jitters to stay in? She convinced her?”

“I plead the Fifth.”

“Are you claiming there was no way to alert police safely without causing a hostage situation? What about the times when Sara herself left the apartment?”

“I. Plead. The. Fifth.”

“It was the money, right? You kept quiet so you’d get the money. If police came to arrest Sara, you wouldn’t get the bitcoin from the thugs Sara murdered in cold blood.”

Aisha scrunched up her face and eyed him skeptically.

“Aisha, I’m not after you at all. I just want the truth,” Asim said, leaning forward. “You save lives. I’m trying to do the same. Including Sara’s if I can.”

Several seconds passed, and Aisha exhaled, shaking her head. “It wasn’t about the money. I wasn’t sure what to believe and didn’t want to rush into anything. She said she had to do it.”

“And you simply accepted that?”

“I was skeptical, but I didn’t want to make any rushed decisions. Government conspiracies are true sometimes. We’ve all seen how many of those have been uncovered. She was convincing.”

“About a cyborg god?”

“Kind of. Some sort of biohybrid system.”

Asim raised an eyebrow. “Any details?”

“Just that it could take over all our systems and would be too many steps ahead of everyone to stop in time if it were to emerge. It would supposedly disarm us, then turn our weapons against us. She said it solved problems that pure AI still couldn’t solve, and not for good purposes.”

“Mention any names? Damien? Marcus?”

She furrowed her brow, recalling. “Yeah, a little. They’re the ones plugged in as the biological side of the system.”

“Did she talk about why she didn’t eat?”

“Not really. She didn’t talk much at all. She said eating made her sick. She’d go days without food. She would drink water and eat pure salt, though. She’d pour salt onto her palm, lick it up, then drink a glass of water. Seems gross, but that’s what she’s like.”

“Why salt?”

Aisha shrugged. “Probably for electrolytes. Helps when not eating.”

“What did she spend her time doing?” Asim asked.

“She mostly stayed in Jitters’s room alone, which she took over, using her devices to search the internet. Probably to plan those attacks. And sometimes Jitters walked in on her practicing her powers, like levitating herself and moving dozens of origami birds.”

Asim held out his hand, palm up. “Why did you let Jitters stay with you in the first place? With the illegal parts of her work and all?”

“For the record, I don’t know anything about her work other than her stripping, which is legal.” Aisha gave him a knowing look. “But she’s paid her share of the rent for nearly a year now. Didn’t cause me any trouble, at least until she brought this mess home. I know lots of people who came from bad starts in life, and Jitters did as best as she could. Helps others where she can, too.”

“Paid her share of the rent off the record,” Asim said. “And you didn’t notify your landlord that you were subletting to a roommate?”

“He knew, but he didn’t ask too many questions,” Aisha said. “All you authority types like to pin things on the bottom rung.”

“That’s not my goal. Anything else you want to tell me?” Asim asked.

“No. You can keep the stupid money. I only want to go back to my normal life. Never wanted to hurt anyone. Just wanted to hear people out and provide shelter for someone injured. One of her fellow mutants cut her face up, you know.”

“Who?”

Aisha shook her head. “Wouldn’t talk about him. She killed him already, she said.”

Asim stood up. “I’ll do what I can to get you back to your life. See how smoothly this went?” He stepped out into the corridor, then walked outside to check the skyline. He wanted to watch them take Sara. To see how she was. Stallard had confirmed that six combat helicopters would come to collect her shortly after noon.

A tight feeling spread through his chest. He’d gotten so little time in there with her. He still needed to find a way to get to the bottom of this, and maybe get another chance to question her, on the record. Everything was moving too fast, and he lacked enough options to contest it. This could be the last time anyone outside of the Stolguard facility would ever see her.



Someone walked in, but they didn’t say anything. The guards tended to rotate in and out.

Jade listened carefully. This wasn’t a guard—too soft-footed. A nurse, probably. Based on the crinkle sound of a plastic wrapper, they were likely preparing another injection.

“More sedation?” Jade asked.

“Just a little something for the pain,” replied a woman’s nervous voice.

No, Jade thought. This was more sedative; it would put her to sleep again. Hopefully enough time had passed by now. She wished for a little more, to be sure. Maybe it had been longer than she thought already, since she couldn’t track time properly like this. She instinctively pulled at her restraints, but they were so tight. Everything was dark.

She refused food, not by choice, but necessity. For reasons that she still didn’t understand, her powers only worked after she fasted. If she ate, she could barely move a few pieces of paper with her mind. But after a couple of days without food, her telekinetic power soared, surpassing even what she’d seen from Fallon. It felt like temporarily unlocking heavy chains that had always held her down.

It wasn’t until eating for the first time after Damien’s death that she’d realized fasting was the key. At Aisha’s place, her first meal had stripped away her power almost completely. She’d then fasted again, regained it, and kept the secret even from Jitters and Aisha. From limited testing, it seemed small meals only needed a day of fasting to recover from. If her captors figured it out, they would force-feed her with tubes, keeping her helpless. She couldn’t let that happen.

This poor nurse. But Jade had only been harmed by showing mercy so far, and there was no other choice. Sara had died for a reason—because she was weak.

They thought this stupid blindfold would help keep them safe. No. Comically and tragically, no. It only meant that more people would die once her amplified power came back. Without sight, she couldn’t target just the people holding guns, nor could she target the guns themselves, since she didn’t know how many kept watch or where exactly they stood around her. Instead, she’d have to hit the entire room, and do so before this nurse stuck her with sedative again.

She made sure to concentrate without clenching her fists, since she couldn’t give the gun-wielding guards any warning. And she’d only plant her bracers at the last second, to avoid tipping off Jolce or Zarina if they were watching.

With her left focus, she blasted a huge cone of force to her left, and with her right focus, she blasted another cone to her right. The room turned frigid. These were powerful enough blasts to kill. A strong resistance formed against her right focus, but she pushed through it until it snapped. Less than a second later, she rotated her foci to sweep the blasts in front of her and behind, covering the full circle.

She gritted her teeth as screams and sounds of breaking walls hit her ears. Guns flew, walls crashed, and wetness splattered. Dusty ceiling tiles fell harmlessly down on her head, dislodged from the broken room.

She ripped apart her wrist straps with her foci, then tore off the blindfold by hand once she was free. Just in time. One injured guard, on the floor with a severed leg spewing blood, feebly lifted his laser rifle up at her. What a patriot. She crushed his head and used her other focus to hold the room’s door closed against reinforcements.

She unstrapped her ankles and stepped onto the cold floor. All she had on was a hospital gown—they’d put her in it after they’d removed her bloody clothes the night before. She wanted to change into one of these guards’ outfits, with their armored vest and boots, but there was no time. Someone was already pounding on the door, and portions of the walls were blown out. There were gaps for them to push through, or shoot through.

She stepped over the nurse’s ruined body, grabbed a pistol from a dead soldier in case it could come in handy—and then noticed Zarina lying there, dead. Her body bloody and torn, eyes open and lifeless.

Zarina must have been that brief resistance she felt on her right-hand side. She’d likely tried to shield herself with her foci, but Jade had cut straight through that attempt. It pulled tight in her chest, like when she’d looked at Maria’s lifeless corpse. Zarina and Maria had been friends with each other. Neither deserved to die. Why couldn’t this have been Jolce instead, as cruel as she was? Why did it always have to be the decent ones who had to die like this? Was the universe mocking her?

Furious at the thought, she blasted a hole in the ceiling and flew into the sky, higher and higher, crushing every security drone in sight with her other focus as she climbed.



Asim gazed out and spotted the fleet of helicopters on the southern horizon. Then, behind him, an explosion went off. A split second later came another. From inside the building.

A sense of dread filled him as he turned. Seconds later, Sara burst through the roof and soared toward the clouds, with a hospital gown and a pistol.

There was nothing he could do about that insanity, so after a moment of horrified indecision, he rushed inside to see how bad it was. The building itself would potentially be unstable now. Inside, past the lobby, the devastation became clear. Walls around Sara’s room had blown open, throwing debris and bodies into the corridor and adjacent rooms. Soldiers from other parts of the building scrambled in that direction to help, many with guns drawn.

Aisha. He ran to her interrogation room. The wall between her room and Sara’s room gaped open, and debris covered the table and floor. He found Aisha lying on the floor coughing, covered in ceiling tiles, blood dripping from her head.



Nearly half a mile into the sky, Jade slowed her ascent. She’d reached enough height to avoid most gunfire. Her bracers extended all the way to the ground, and any more altitude would strain them. It was freezing up here in just a hospital gown. Six incoming military helicopters thrummed on the horizon.

She wished she knew more about radar. Would they be able to detect someone her size flying around? She assumed so. She imagined them scrambling fighter jets against her, then imagined tearing them from the sky.

Shifting her course northward, she accelerated, flying faster and faster. Away from the helicopters to start with. Her right focus was split into parts, spreading the grip across her body, and it pulled her in the direction of flight, while her right bracer transferred the corresponding momentum to the ground. Every half mile, she replanted her bracers on the ground far beneath her to avoid straining their length. She kept her left focus ready to shield herself from any surprise, or crush what might need crushing.

After several miles of flight, she descended, figuring that a lower altitude might help against radar and ease the strain, even as it would lead to more witnesses. How low was low enough to slip under radar detection? She flew down to right above the rooftops.

Over Brooklyn. Then Queens. After that, she came upon water and dropped down to a few feet above it, with misty wind whipping at her hair so harshly it ached. She tried to remember her geography studies. This was . . . the Long Island Sound. As she reached the far shore, the wooded suburbs of upstate New York or Connecticut blurred beneath her. The farther she went, the sparser the neighborhoods became, until stretches of pure forest replaced them.

She used the opportunity to descend and think. Dropping through the forest canopy, she landed softly on the ground. She looked around, then fell to her knees. How could she know if she was being tracked or what to do next?

Her body hurt all over, and her right shoulder seared as the rest of the drugs wore off. Rage filled her as she remembered Jolce telekinetically tearing into her wound, ignoring her thrashing screams, as Stallard kept asking the same questions, promising the pain would end once she told the truth.

She’d vomited twice, and laughed whenever she couldn’t take it, just like Damien had taught her. But the repeated feeling of drowning, the burning sensation of water filling her sinuses as Santiago held her down, had been too much. Drowning over and over, without the peace of finally being dead.

A raw sensation of wrath surged through her, pure fire burning from within.

She’d doubted herself these past weeks. After the news station, after the Pentagon, she would sit up at night wondering if she could’ve done anything differently. If there’d been a way to hurt fewer people. But now she realized that she’d been thinking in the wrong direction entirely. She’d been too soft, taking unnecessary chances with people. Her power was too asymmetrical toward offense and lacking in defense for something so vapid as mercy. She could throw a dozen cars like tennis balls but couldn’t risk taking a single headshot from an unexpected angle.
