Asim sat virtually in Ava’s private room, styled after her living room. Sara was late, but the young man, Damien, had shown up on time. Or the mimic version of him, as it were. They had been talking for a while. Asim liked him, since he actually answered his fucking questions for a change rather than making him pry answers out like a dentist with teeth. He also asked questions of his own.

“Do you know if my body was returned to Thane?” Damien asked.

Asim nodded. “Yes. Yours and the others with green eyes at the rest stop were. He was insistent on that. Every blood and tissue sample, too.”

“As expected,” Damien said. “They consider all our bodily matter their property.”

Ava frowned.

“I still don’t get something,” Asim said. “How problematic can the supercomputer version of you people be, if the facility is kept offline when it’s active?”

“Well, I’m here, aren’t I?” Damien said. “Because that version of me created me, and weeks later when the facility came online, I slipped out. They keep access very narrow and tightly controlled, and yet I got through. If the system turns malicious, as I nearly did during my first run, there’s no telling what it could sneak out. All sorts of dangerous code. Plus, I could have convinced Thane to open a live connection to the outside world while I was plugged in and really let loose, which he basically wants anyway. Or I could have hacked the facility’s drones to force him to. Then it’s over.”

The door opened, and Sara walked in. She had blond hair now.

“You’re late,” Asim said. “Getting your hair done?”

“I had to tie some people up; they were becoming a problem. You’re using a different identity key than normal. How do I even know you’re you?”

“Straight to the chase, huh? The proof is in my charm,” he said with a smile. “No matter how much I fuck you up, you keep coming back to chat. You should generate a new identity key too.”

She remained stone-faced and narrowed her eyes. Not one for humor apparently. “What did we talk about on the beach that one time?”

“About why you look like shit. And about how my wife and daughter don’t like me anymore because I act like shit.”

“Sir . . .” Ava said.

“Good enough,” Sara said. She turned to Damien again, and her expression softened. “Your suggestion worked. That’ll buy me a lot of time. Thank you.”

“I’m glad it did,” Damien said, smiling. “I figured.”

“What suggestion? And time for what?” Asim asked.

Sara’s expression hardened again, and she only glared.

“Sara, sit here,” Ava said with a smile, tapping an empty seat on the couch next to her. “Does anyone want tea?”

“Thank you,” Sara said, her posture relaxing. She went and sat down where Ava suggested, pulling her feet up to sit cross-legged. Thin and bruised, she stared down at the coffee table.

“I’ll have some as well,” Damien said.

Ava looked at Asim.

“Uh, sure?” Asim said.

Ava manifested four cups, and Asim took a sip. “Delicious.”

“My mother’s recipe,” Ava said.

“Why should I trust you?” Sara asked, raising her eyes toward him. Damn, she was awkward. Her intensity of body language and tone were always dialed up to eleven, regardless of the context. Even the mimic was more charismatic than her.

“Well, you shouldn’t, to be honest,” he said. “And I don’t trust you, given how many people you’ve killed. I’ll be direct—you’ll never be pardoned for what you’ve done. The scale’s too big, too public. But I want to get to the bottom of this, and all my normal channels are either outgunned or complicit.”

“I don’t care about a pardon. What are you doing about the rest?” Sara asked. “Filing reports? Thinking about thinking about maybe investigating the Stolguard facility? Spinning in circles?”

“I filed a whistleblower complaint on the ethics of how subjects like you are treated, about credible evidence of domestic assassinations at the highest levels, and about a human-machine threat that needs outside safety review.”

“Oh, a complaint. That’ll do the trick. A strongly worded letter to some higher-ups that Stallard and his allies will no doubt make sure is buried? Great work, detective. Thank you.” She smiled in a way that didn’t reach her eyes again.

“I don’t see—” Asim began.

“I don’t see why I’m even still talking,” Sara interrupted. “They’ll just kill you like the other whistleblowers. What can you possibly do? Can you at least let Jitters and Aisha go?”

Asim sipped his tea and stifled his annoyance. She’d been tortured partially because of him, barely a day ago. She had every reason to be angry, even if all he’d done was arrest her, which had been the right thing to do.

He looked over at Ava. “Did you get a chance to check their status while I was off today? I told Master Sergeant Smith yesterday that ACI’s questions were done for now, but what about the Brooklyn police? And this tea is fucking amazing, actually.”

“Thank you, sir.” Ava beamed. “Veronica was transferred to NYPD today. I doubt their investigation will go far with her mugging crew all dead, and considering how hard it was for us to gather information on her in the first place. What would they go on? Aisha was released already, with the caveat that she has to stay in Brooklyn for now in case they have more questions. She picked up Scorpio, too.”

“So, can you get Jitters out on bail?” Sara asked.

“I can look into that,” Asim said. “If they don’t have enough evidence of her street crimes, they’ll have to let her go soon anyway. You told Damien that he bought you a lot of time. Does that mean you’ll stop rampaging so we can approach this more carefully? And who are those people you’ve got tied up?”

“You think I’m still stupid enough to answer any of your questions?”

Asim reflexively went to pinch the bridge of his nose, but then scratched it instead. “Look, I can provide some resources to help dig into the Stolguard facility. But it will take time. If you’re out there flying around killing people like a fucking supervillain, it limits my options. You’re already legally unrecoverable. Technically I’ll be aiding a fugitive. But if I can show that you’re back on a leash, at least temporarily, it gives me more cover to take legally risky steps if they work out in the end. Going after insiders is part of my job.”

“I won’t be on anyone’s leash,” Sara said. “Not anymore.”

“It’s just a figure of speech. Can we agree on no killing for now?”

Sara stared at him for several seconds, then sighed. “I need to stay secure, but other than that, yes. As long as progress is being made. You were right that I was on a tight clock before.”

“What resources can you offer, Colonel?” Damien asked conversationally, then sipped his tea.

Asim turned back toward him. Although this one was helpful, mimics were creepy as hell. Why would he drink the goddamn tea? Who did he think he was fooling? It wasn’t like he could taste it.

“In the coming weeks,” Asim said, “I’ll keep pushing whistleblower pathways. I can also provide you with basic updates to the case, assuming you’re not using them for violent ends. We could even have both of you record detailed testimonies that I can personally take to senior leaders. This is incredibly risky for me, but I’m willing to try.”

Sara glanced at Damien, who looked thoughtful.

“I think this is our best direction for now,” Damien said to her.

“But how—” Sara froze mid-sentence, her brow furrowing. She reached out and swiped at a menu only she could see, her eyes narrowing.

“What?” Asim asked.

She ignored him, focusing on Damien. “It’s from Fallon, or claims to be. She sent me a message.”

“What does it say?” Damien asked.

Sara pressed an invisible button, and her menu became visible to everyone, like a holographic notification in front of her avatar. A woman’s brash voice filled the room.

“Sara. Father sees your avatar is active again. Yes, we know it’s you now, thanks to that hooker. I have an important message for you, and only you. Meet me at the destination in the link below. Only your identity key can access it. I’m waiting there now. Love, Fallon.”

“Sounds promising, actually,” Asim said.

“That’s because you don’t know Fallon.” Sara took a deep breath, swiped the menu away, and exhaled.







Chapter 38



Sara logged into the private room Fallon had invited her to. It was nothing but a virtual field of wind-rippling grass beneath a crisp blue sky, dotted with fluffy white clouds stretching for miles in every direction.

Fallon stood tall, arms crossed, wearing her black armored combat outfit. Her chin-length black hair whipped in the wind, and she had a visual verifier flag proving it was her unaltered form, scanned by the device she was using. She smiled as Sara emerged as if out of a portal.

“It seems the dull blade has sharpened itself. It’s good to see you, Sara. I mean that.”

“What do you want?” Sara asked.

“Well, I have good news and bad news, I’m afraid. Which would you like first?”

“The bad news.”

“That’s practical,” Fallon said. “But I think I’m going to override that. You’ll take the bad news better after I give you the good news.”

Sara stayed silent. She didn’t feel like playing whatever game this was.

“The good news is, you have my respect, and my apology,” Fallon said. “I know I’ve been unfair to you. You have every reason to hate me and the facility. I’m not the person I once was, and I’m sorry for how I’ve treated you.”

“Is that supposed to mean anything to me?” Sara asked.

“Whether it does or not is up to you. I just thought I should tell you. It’s not easy for me to do.”

“You respect me because I have power now? Because I sharpened my blade? That’s how your mind works?”

“No, actually. It’s not only because you’ve changed. It’s because I have as well. Look, I had . . . issues when I was younger. I took them out on you unnecessarily that time we dueled. And that other time, well, that was right after Jax died. I wasn’t in a good place. Given what you just went through with Damien and what you did to Maria afterward, maybe you can understand now. It doesn’t excuse what I did, but at least I didn’t kill you like you killed Maria. She didn’t deserve that.”

“Why are you telling me this?”

“Because when I give you the bad news, I want you to know it’s not out of spite. It had to be done. It’s not personal.”

Sara concentrated, trying to think of things she’d missed. What bad news could Fallon surprise her with? “Fine. What’s the bad news?”

Fallon sighed. “You don’t believe my intentions. That’s fair, given how I’ve treated you. But remember this. I used your chosen name as soon as you picked it, just like I did with everyone else. Our names matter, Sara. I bullied you not because I viewed you as a number, but because I viewed you as a person. If I only viewed you as a number, I wouldn’t have bothered.”

“That’s great, thank you.”

“I’m serious. Back before I got so competitive, we spent time together, remember? When I was ten or eleven, and you were six, maybe seven. That was when you picked your name. We were almost friends back then, but we grew apart. That was my fault, not yours. I should’ve done better.”

Sara waited.

“Father . . . never really paid attention to us back then, did he?” Fallon said. “He’s warmed up since then, at least for some of us. He deals with adults better than children. But I did pay attention. I lived on the same floor with the rest of my, well, sisters. Saw who they spent time with. What they did. I knew you, in some way, even after we drifted apart. So, for example—and this is the bad news—I know how close Clare is to you. Almost as close as Damien was, I think. And so, I told Father that. That’s the kind of detail he wouldn’t otherwise know.”

Sara felt a spike of dread. “What are you saying?”

“You know what I’m saying,” Fallon said. “Clare’s a hostage now, though she doesn’t know it yet. She misses you and wonders why you’ve done such terrible things. I came here on behalf of our father to deliver a message. If you don’t turn yourself in within three days, Clare will die. Slowly. Very slowly. It’ll be awful.”

“You’re bluffing. Aside from me, why would Stallard kill one of his own subjects? She’s never caused a problem for anyone.”

“Clare’s a small price to pay for your capture,” Fallon said. “Besides, if you turn yourself in, she’ll be fine. That’s how this should go. I certainly don’t want her to die.” She looked down at her palm. “Unlike you, I actually went on missions with her. Taught her things. Did the dirtiest parts myself so she could keep her precious hands clean. In some ways, I know her better than you do. I promise, I’m not bluffing. I wish I was.”

“Fallon!” Sara raised her voice. “Why are you so loyal to Stallard now? Why even consider doing this to Clare, without listening to me? I’m trying to stop Stallard from doing to Marcus what he did to Damien. You could help. You don’t know the danger he’ll cause if he—”

“Spare me.” Fallon looked up from her palm. “I already had Santiago fill me in on your ramblings from Father’s interrogation. You’re afraid he’ll make some Class D threat he can’t control.”

“It’s true. Damien experienced it. He could reach into everyone’s systems, their weapons. He nearly turned evil. Marcus is next.”

Fallon shook her head. “Damien had a fraction of Father’s experience. You act with false certainty, willing to kill to stop a theoretical problem. By that logic, should I have finished you off when we fought, to prevent you from killing so many people years later? I’ve already admitted I was at fault there. But by your reasoning, maybe I didn’t go far enough. Are your kills on my hands now?”

“Your violence had nothing to do with knowledge of the future,” Sara said. “Mine directly does. It’s not the sa—”

“Just admit you’re trapped, Sara,” Fallon said, waving her hand around dismissively. “You know what I think? You want to do whatever you feel like. You’re acting out of anger and spite, and you hide behind grander justifications. But you know what? I get it. If I was in your situation, I’d be furious. You were the runt of the litter, and were punished for it unfairly. That’s why I opened with an apology. I want you to think things through rationally, for Clare’s sake. I’ve chosen a side. Father’s side. You can turn yourself in, trust that Father knows how to keep his experiments under control, and nobody else has to get hurt. Maybe in time, you can even reintegrate with us. I’ll try to be the big sister I failed to be before.”

“We both know he’ll either kill me, or worse. He’ll never risk me going against him again.”

“Perhaps. But then it comes down to whose life you value more. Yours or Clare’s. You’ll use other justifications to favor yourself over her, like bringing up this supposed Class D threat again. But—”

“It’s not a justification, it’s literally—”

“Look, I’m not much better.” Fallon smiled, showing her palms. “Admittedly, when I first prepared for you coming to attack, I was excited. I lusted at the thought of taking you down, flashy new powers and all. But then I realized how immature that was. Not everything is proven in fights. It’s also proven through strategy, loyalty, leadership, and avoiding unnecessary fights in the first place. That’s what it means to protect people. To be a commander. Let’s solve this peacefully, Sara. Don’t make me hurt Clare.”

“If you find yourself on the side that hurts the nicest person in the world, don’t you think you should reconsider?”

Fallon rolled her eyes. “Your entire approach is about the ends justifying the means. If one person suffers and dies to rein in a killer, isn’t that worth it? And like I said, hopefully it’s only the threat of it. We haven’t even told her yet, so you can make this all go away before anyone suffers at all, mentally or physically. I don’t like it either, but since she’s your best friend, she’s the best leverage we have over you if we’re going to avoid a full-blown conflict. We can’t have you out there causing problems for us anymore, bringing all this bad attention our way. My job as a commander is to protect those who report to me and to stop you from hurting anyone else. If I must sacrifice one for many, I will, just like you. But her blood will be on your hands. Painfully so.”

Sara wanted to say something, but her mind raced in too many directions.

“It’s okay,” Fallon continued. “I convinced Father to give you three days instead of one. I knew your kneejerk reaction would be to say no, but that eventually you’d say yes. Given some time, I know you’ll make the right choice. I’d even ask for my own sake, because I’m going to have to do this if you decline. Father doesn’t want most others to know, since it would hurt morale. I’ll have to tell Clare that you chose this for her, not me.”

Fallon clenched her fist in front of her, stared at it, and lowered her voice. “I’ll do it over days and send you videos, so technically if you’re a day or two late and reconsider, you’ll still be able to save her, or what’s left of her. But waiting to see if I’m bluffing would be a mistake. You’ll get the proof you want, though everyone will have lost. I’m speaking to you as earnestly as I can so we can both avoid that. You’ve always been too stubborn for your own good. This one time, I’m asking you not to be.” She opened her fist and turned her palm upward, invitingly, and met Sara’s eyes.

Sara found herself looking away. “It’s easy to fake a video.”

“I’ll make her say things only she would know, just for you.”

“If you hurt her . . .” She forced herself to look back up toward Fallon’s gaze. “I’ll make it my life’s mission to hunt you down.”

“Ah, there you are! I wouldn’t expect anything less.” Fallon smiled again. “We are who we are, but it doesn’t mean we always have to act like it. You love your new powers. You’d love nothing more than to use them on me, or at least try. But regardless of how a fight between us would play out, it wouldn’t undo Clare’s fate. Instead, it would only prove my point; you’re acting out of spite.”

Sara stared at her, suppressing a surge of anger.

“Here are the rules, straight from Father,” Fallon continued. “By Monday, three days from now, turn yourself in at our front gate. If you don’t, you’ll receive distressing videos, starting that evening. Don’t try any tricks when you come. We have guards with lasers all over the facility grounds now. Rionz made sure of that. You’ll be sedated and brought in. I’ll advocate for Father to treat you well once you’ve surrendered. I mean it. It’s my duty as a big sister. I want to atone for what I did to you. You didn’t deserve it. Neither would Clare if you refuse.”

Fallon reached out her hand, tapped a few invisible buttons, and vanished.

Sara lingered for a moment, watching the wind flutter across the endless grass. Such a beautiful place for such an ugly threat.

Eventually, she brought her menu up and switched back to Ava’s private room. When she opened the door, the three familiar faces turned toward her.

“What did she want?” Damien asked.

“Me. Either I surrender, or Fallon tortures Clare to death starting in three days. On Halloween, of all dates, which is a detail that I don’t think is lost on Fallon either.”

“She’s bluffing,” Damien said. “That’s ridiculous.”

Sara exhaled, noticing her breath tremble. “I don’t think she is. Stallard’s behind this. Not only Fallon. She just gave him the clue, since she knows more about me than he does. It’s the best leverage they’ve got. And she was very specific.”

“Well, you can’t turn yourself in, obviously,” Damien said.

“Either I try to attack the facility and risk both Clare’s death and mine, or I surrender. There’s no world where I would do nothing and let her be tortured to death.”

“Sara. We need to think logically about this. They’re preying on your emotions.”

“I won’t be able to function if I know Clare’s suffering. Emotions are all we have!”

“Is Clare one of your fellow subjects?” Asim asked. “Maybe we can get Fallon to say that on a recording. It would strengthen our whistleblower case.”

“I doubt it,” Sara said. “That’s why she only spoke to me, without witnesses. We could trick Fallon alone, but I think she’s only doing things Stallard approves of, and it’s hard to trick him. She said she’ll send proof, but they’ll probably make the videos’ context unclear to outsiders, like who’s being tortured and why. I need to think.”

Asim gestured for calm, as though it mattered. “Let’s—”

“Let’s not,” Sara said. “What do you even want from all this?”

“The truth,” he said, staring straight into her eyes and raising his voice. “To protect people. I’m fed up with all the corruption. The sheer persistence of this shit. If any of this is even remotely true, I want to fucking crucify those responsible. But Damien’s right. To do that, we need to think logically, strategically, and can’t rush. We’ve only got one shot.”

She looked back at him but couldn’t hold his gaze. She glanced around the virtual apartment instead. Nobody could be trusted. She logged off before hearing another word.

These people didn’t understand. Only one of them knew Clare, and he wasn’t even alive anymore.







Chapter 39



As the sun set, Sara leaned against the yacht’s railing, watching the waves she had always wished to see, thinking. Their supplies were dwindling, almost gone.

She’d been replaying that horrid exchange in her mind for the past hour. Maybe it was time to stop. Maybe enough people had died. Maybe Fallon was right, and she’d really been doing all of this for herself.

With Damien’s death, she’d lost what little connection she had to this world, and as a fugitive, she found herself with two options. She could roll over and give up, or she could fight. She’d chosen to fight.

But for what? Was it out of spite, like Fallon said?

She’d told herself it was for Damien’s legacy. For Clare and Marcus. For the children of the new classes, so that they might have a happier life. To stop all the corrupt assassinations they’d been born to carry out without even understanding why. For the countless lives that could be saved by exposing the dark god before it emerged. She told herself history was written by the winners, that there was no room for weakness. Innocents had died, and that was tragic, but didn’t they always?

She’d become a hollowed-out shell of power, left to carry out Damien’s will.

And yet, what if she really had done this for herself? To give herself a reason to keep moving? Maybe her selfishness caused unnecessary deaths, and it was all for nothing. Had she become a bigger monster than Fallon ever was?

With the real Damien gone, Clare was the closest person she had left. Even if she’d never get to see her again, she wanted her to be happy. Would Fallon really go through with it? Torture Clare to death? If anyone could, it was her.

Sara knew that if she were to receive a video of Clare in agony, she’d lose her mind. Time was ticking.

Damien, she texted. Can we talk alone?

Of course, he replied. I’m here for you.

She created a private room from one of the device’s default options: a penthouse suite overlooking the Hong Kong skyline, with the sun sinking behind mountains as the city lights flickered on in the blue-gold dusk.

A minute later, Damien entered. He wore a fake smile, trying to look cheerful but failing, which was a detail so realistically him that she wondered if Damien had programmed it that way on purpose. He sat beside her on the couch and stroked her hair once. A performance of a loving boyfriend, and it worked. She’d been physically touched so little in her life that each instance felt marvelous. She leaned her head on his shoulder.

“What is it?” he asked.

“I’m going to turn myself in.”

“Sara, you can’t. Please.”

“It’s either that, or I attack the facility from the sky and rain hell on it. Maybe fight Fallon if she makes it up that far. Though . . . with all the new defenses they have, I doubt I could do enough damage before I’m stopped.”

“As bad as that plan is, it’s better than turning yourself in. I don’t think Colonel Rahal’s whistleblowing alone is going to prevent Thane from getting Marcus hooked up to my levels soon. And you’ve seen the scale of what could happen next.”

“Maybe it’s okay,” she said. “You’re dead. I’ll be dead too, or kept in a state worse than it. Maybe your fears about the superintelligent entity won’t come true. And even if they do, does it really matter? Humanity would have done it to themselves. Why should we care? Are we even human?”

“The Sara I knew would’ve cared,” Damien said. “And you’re still her. You’ve just been through a lot of things you didn’t deserve.”

She straightened up. “You helped me off the rushed clock I was on, but Fallon put me right back on an even worse one. All I see are dead ends, arguments, and distant numbers of hypothetical lives. I put other people through a lot of things they didn’t deserve, and for what? Now that I know you’re here, I think you and Asim can carry on without me. Maybe my death can be the last.”

Damien was silent. Thoughtful. Eventually, he spoke again. “Yours is the last death I would ever want. Despite the numbers.”

Tears came to her eyes. How was he so good at that? “The night we escaped together,” she said, pushing through the emotion, “I was worried I would die before telling you how I felt. I even foolishly thought maybe we might . . . make love before we left. It was stupid in hindsight, but I figured that, if something went wrong, at least we’d have that experience together once. Could we have that experience now?”

Damien met her eyes, sympathy clear on his face. “We could, if that’s what you want. But . . . I don’t think that is what you want. Not truly. Do you really want your first time to be with someone who isn’t experiencing it with you? And in a limited virtual world? I’m honest about what I am. I’m only a mimic, Sara.”

“It’ll be my only time, not my first time, Damien. Then I’ll turn myself in. Maybe a good lie is better than nothing at all.” A tear slid down her cheek.

“We don’t have to think that way,” Damien said. “I know part of you has had a death wish for years, but you’re accepting this too easily. There are still options here.”

“Death wish!” she shouted. “I was born powerless in a prison where only power mattered. Humiliated, isolated, beaten. We were relentlessly experimented on, frequently in pain, and for what? The moment we tried to change any of that, you died. I never asked to be born in the first place! Forgive me if I’m not too clingy to my life.”

Damien reached out and hugged her without words. She was too furious to reciprocate at first, but eventually she hugged him back. It was crazy how realistic his touch was, warm and soft. She loved that, and hated it.

Damien released her and leaned back, smiling. “Oh, Sara. Come here. Let’s try this instead.” He stood up and held out his hand.

What was he planning? Sara eyed him, then took his hand. So smooth. So warm. Virtual warmth, she reminded herself. He helped her up from the couch and smiled at her, then reached down to her legs and scooped her up off her feet, holding her aloft, with a big grin on his face.

“Damien!” she said. An unexpected laugh broke out of her. She couldn’t remember the last time she’d laughed out of joy. The VR headset and haptic suit simulated the sensation of being carried better than she’d expected.

“Shhh,” he said, and brought her over to the bed. Butterflies fluttered through her belly. It was almost enough to forget about the pain everywhere else.

He rested her on the covers and climbed next to her. He put his arm around her, spooned her, and began stroking her hair. Then he kissed her on the cheek.

“The real Damien, the one who created me, would have wanted me to comfort you,” he said. She could feel his breath caressing her ear as he spoke, as his fingers ran through her hair, giving her tingles. So realistic. “But he would have wanted you to live, and to find someone else, in time. He wouldn’t have wanted me to pull you into a delusion. So, let’s stay here. With affection only. I can tell you haven’t slept much. Now that I’m here, you can let yourself sleep in peace. I’ll monitor your surroundings from your VR headset and wake you up if there’s danger. We still have time to think things through before making any rash decisions about you turning yourself in.”

Sara wiped her eyes and cuddled deeper into his embrace, feeling her eyelids grow heavy. For just this once, she let herself be who she was before. No hardened exterior. No purposeful dissociation. She deserved one delusion. One moment of peace.

She imagined herself with Damien back in her room before his death. This was an extension of him anyway, made by him, so she enjoyed his embrace as she drifted off.







Chapter 40



When morning came, Sara promised Damien she’d return soon, then logged off to watch the sunrise from her stolen yacht.

For once, she felt . . . okay.

But their food had run out. She’d given all the carbs to the family, which they’d eaten, and kept just the meat sticks for herself. It’d only been two days since she’d taken the yacht, but they’d been out on an afternoon cruise and hadn’t packed much. Last night, she’d been forced to tie up the parents after the father tried to break through the barricaded door. She didn’t want to kill them, so it was time to move on and let them go.

Part of her still wanted to fly straight to the facility and end it all there in battle, one way or another. Maybe she’d find a way to do enough damage before getting struck down.

Realistically though, it was probably time to surrender. She’d acted harshly with what little time she had, wasting away, and she’d killed people, each with families and rich inner lives, with little progress to show for it. People were right to hate her. Maybe all of it had been for nothing.

With that thought, she sighed and went to open the barricaded closet, where she’d put the boy with some blankets and a flashlight. As terrible as it was to lock him in there, it was better than tying him up like his parents. As she opened the door, he recoiled from her, frightened, clutching a turtle action figure in his hand. She had let him take his toys in there for comfort.

She looked down at the boy and felt another wave of guilt. She hated being the source of a child’s fear.

Crouching down, she smiled. “You’re safe. What’s his name?”

He glanced up, then back at his toy. “Le . . . Leonardo,” he whispered. “He’s a ninja.”

Sara stared at the figure for a moment, then smiled. “It’s funny. I wanted to be a ninja when I was your age. Things didn’t turn out how I’d hoped. Don’t worry. Today you’ll be on your way home, safe and sound. Come, watch the sunrise with me?”

After he used the restroom, they sat awkwardly together on the deck in silence, watching the golden rays light up the clouds in the chilly air. He still clutched that little turtle ninja, and eventually . . . it stirred a thought.

Maybe there was a middle path. Could infiltration be an actual option here?

Instead of raining hell on the facility and getting shot down, or surrendering herself in complete failure, could she somehow get Clare and Marcus out? Or could she sneak in and assassinate Stallard to give Asim’s division more of an opening to contest the facility through formal channels?

The Stolguard facility’s defenses would now be immense, with subjects recalled from missions, more guards, more drones, and countless lasers. Price and Asim had both told her as much. Impenetrable.

But what if it wasn’t? Even if the chance was slim. They probably didn’t know she still had Damien on her side, after all. Or at least, a version of him. And potential allies in the government. If what Asim needed was time, how could she best give it to him? Her mind worked through possibilities.

Damien, she texted eventually. That guard Jessica. You had access to the facility database. Do you know her last name? Can you find out where she lives?

Yes, he texted back. But what are you planning, Sara?

To be a ninja for Halloween, she wrote. Message those other two. I have an idea, but I need all of you to help make it smarter.

Will do.

As she waited for them to meet up, her decision crystallized in her mind.

She wasn’t blindly trusting Damien, no matter how much she loved and missed him, the way Fallon blindly trusted Stallard. She’d seen the evidence with her own eyes. Damien described the exact sequence of bugs that he pre-built to strike the facility for their escape, and they manifested perfectly. He’d aligned it in such a short period of time, while holding back only out of kindness.

What if he’d taken control of all the facility’s security drones and used them violently, rather than just deactivate them as he’d done? What if he had let her shoot Jessica near the exit rather than take time to spare her? They would’ve gotten out more quickly, potentially before Jolgen caught them at the fence and visually confirmed which direction they’d gone.

The unleashed version of what she saw that night, actively connected to the rest of the world with him lost in the machine, would have been beyond comprehension.

And she wasn’t doing this out of spite. If she had been, she wouldn’t have given Asim so many chances after how badly that jerk had hurt her. His intentions had been good; she was a monster in his eyes.

Stallard was obsessed and callous, leading others toward danger, either in the grand scheme of things like Damien feared, or even just on the personal level for more classes of subjects who would never have a choice. Fallon went along with it because otherwise it would challenge her own position. She’d only rebelled against the system until it embraced her.

Clare and Marcus deserved freedom. They all did. And if a false god was one day going to be born into this world, no good could come from it being under Stallard’s hand. Not now, not like this, and certainly not through Marcus.

She would do this because she felt it was right, at her core, with guideposts built from everything she’d learned from the people she trusted most in this world.







Part IV





Hades








Chapter 41



Clare picked at her eggs and toast with her fork. She wasn’t particularly hungry, since this was earlier than she normally ate. There was also her unusual company.

Fallon sat across the table. She had knocked on Clare’s door early in the morning and invited her to breakfast. They’d of course eaten together countless times in the past; that wasn’t the unusual part. She, Fallon, and Dalia had shared meals all the time during their missions in Iran, and ever since then they’d often find themselves at the same group table, either in the facility or in the field somewhere. She’d never liked Fallon, but they’d known each other all their lives, and Fallon had protected her in the field in more ways than one.

Just the two of them together, though, was rare.

“Is everything okay? Do you want to talk about something?” Clare asked.

“Not at all. I just wanted to spend some time with you.” Fallon flicked her eyes up from her plate.

Clare smiled, trying to conceal her unease. “Well, it’s been a while.” She forced herself to take another bite.

“Did you know that in the wild, only one in ten cheetah cubs survive to adulthood? Isn’t that pathetic?” Fallon asked.

Yep, this was going to be weird. “Um. Well, nature can be kind of—”

“If I was a cheetah,” Fallon continued, her eyes lighting up as she gestured with her fork, “I’d consider anything short of the reverse to be unacceptable. At least nine out of ten cubs must survive. You know?” With a flick of her fingers, she levitated a plum to her mouth and took a bite, then put a thoughtful expression on her face as the plum levitated back above her tray.

“I guess so,” Clare offered. “Is this leading up to something specific?”

Fallon finished chewing, then smirked. “No. I just figured I’d check to see how you’re holding up since Damien died and Sara lost her mind. It’s not my strong suit, but I wanted to be here for you, and I realized I haven’t done enough of that.” She mentally floated up a knife, sliced the untouched side of the plum, and levitated the crisp piece across the table to Clare.

After a brief hesitation, Clare plucked it out of the air and ate it, which gave her a moment to think. “I don’t know what to make of Sara,” she said once she swallowed. “None of it makes sense to me. I get why she wanted to escape. But I don’t understand why she killed all those people afterward. I’d give anything to talk to her again, if only briefly.” She fought back a surge of emotion behind her eyes and kept them dry. Sara wouldn’t have hurt Damien no matter what, regardless of what Dr. Stallard claimed. She loved him with all her heart.

Fallon eyed Clare as if noticing her sadness, then nodded and ate a mouthful of eggs with her fork while the half-eaten plum still hung in the air. “I can understand that. Loyalty’s important. People naturally want to give those close to them the benefit of the doubt. But when loyalties clash, it’s our duty that matters most. We need to keep that in mind.”

The hair on Clare’s neck rose. Was Fallon testing her? “Are you sure there’s nothing more specific you want to talk about?”

Fallon smirked again. “Honestly, I’ve been frustrated at how many people keep doing whatever they want. We’re soldiers. We have a command structure, and responsibilities.” She tapped the table. “But it starts with me; I have to lead by example. Part of me wants to rip Sara apart for what she did to Maria and Zarina. That’s not a constructive thought, though. As a commander, my job is to protect people. That means putting my personal feelings aside. And as I do that, I ask others to do the same.” She grabbed the plum by hand this time, bit into it without breaking eye contact, then set it back in the air as though on an invisible hook. Invisible to anyone outside of Class C, at least.

“I already told you I’m compromised when it comes to Sara,” Clare said. “I admitted it from the start. And we don’t have all the information. That’s why I want to focus on other things. Like helping Bronn protect the fallback areas if any of the worst-case scenarios happen. To protect the children.”

Fallon looked softer now. “I get that, Clare. I do. But those worst-case scenarios aren’t going to happen. Those plans are for optics, for those rattled by the Pentagon footage. This facility isn’t like that. Look around.” She held out her hand to the full cafeteria. “All these people, all this equipment, geared toward her. She can’t touch this place. If she tries, she’ll die. The only question is how many people she’d take with her first.”

“So, what do you want?” Clare asked.

“Nothing. Like I said, I wanted to check on you. I could’ve used someone doing that for me over the years. But whenever Bronn tried, I always pushed him away. You’re not as hot-headed as I am.” Fallon smiled. It was uncharacteristically warm, with no hint of sarcasm. “You know, I’d take back some of what I did to Sara if I could. But that’s not how things work. We have to deal with reality in the present.”

Clare studied her. Maybe this wasn’t a test after all. Maybe Fallon wanted to get something off her chest.

“Is there something you’re conflicted about?” Clare asked, doing her best to make it seem warm. Some part of it truly was.

Fallon raised her eyebrows and pushed a chunk of her short hair behind an ear. “My philosophy has always been to refuse adequacy and pursue greatness.” She took another bite of the plum and chewed for an awkward number of seconds. “People think greatness comes down to luck, but it doesn’t. It’s about choosing every day to hold yourself to a higher standard than the day before, and higher than others expect. It’s about being vigilant, and catching yourself whenever you start to settle for good enough. It’s built from relentless, incremental decisions to improve. You know?”

Clare hadn’t heard Fallon open up like this before. Maybe she’d spoken this way to Jax or Maria or Bronn over the years, but never to her.

“Makes sense,” she said. “I think that view can be pushed too far, but I see your point. What’s the conflict, then?”

“Let me ask you a personal question,” Fallon said, putting both elbows on the table and leaning in. “What would you give your life for?”

The answer came out of her, almost without thinking. “To protect the people I love.”

“Good answer. And unsurprising,” Fallon said with a respectful nod. She leaned back and crossed her arms. “I think about that sometimes. Before Jax died, I thought greatness was about myself, being the best at whatever I did. Like if I was a cheetah, I’d have to be the fastest one. Because running fast is what cheetahs do. What’s the use of a slow cheetah?” She waved her hand dismissively. “But Jax put my safety over his own. He distracted himself in battle because he was trying to get me out. By doing that, he lost his life but saved mine. We all know about sacrifice, of course, but it’s different when it happens right in front of you. I realized then that greatness needs a wider circle of relevance to be worth anything. It’s about being the cheetah that’s faster than the others not just for her own sake, but because the purpose of that speed is to keep more of her cubs alive than other cheetahs can.”

Clare nodded, unsure of what to say next. She thought about how to phrase something regarding Jax, but then Fallon spoke up again on her own.

“Raphael’s plans are all about defense, like minimizing casualties and quickly taking Sara down if she attacks here,” Fallon said. “It’s sensible, and we need someone who thinks that way. But the best option would be to avoid that fight altogether. To stop her before she can hurt anyone else. And before she can draw any more attention toward our home from those who would demonize us. It’s time to go on the offensive.”

A chill ran through Clare. “Offensive?”

Fallon’s face was unreadable. “Yes. I can’t go into specifics, but if the mission is to keep the most people safe, here or anywhere, that makes sense to you, right?”

Clare sighed. “It would depend on those specifics, but I get the logic.” She fought back another surge of emotion. Sara, where are you? Are you okay? What are you doing?

“Well, I’m glad you agree.” Fallon glanced around the guard-filled cafeteria, her jaw tightening, then fixed her gaze back on Clare, sharper than before. “That’s the job of a commander, after all. To make the hard choices.”



Thane watched as Marcus screamed, clenched his teeth, and screamed again. And then some more. He had given Emmett the day off for this session and decided that he would start doing that more often when it came to Marcus. He didn’t want the man’s distractions today; it was time to accelerate.

The sheer amount of subtle damage Damien had inflicted on the facility’s codebase proved how powerful this capability could be once fully developed. They were still uncovering his little bugs, hidden here and there. At first it seemed like a setback, but in the grand scheme of things, it had been a successful proof of concept.

The boy stopped screaming and began breathing heavily, deliberately, in a pattern. Exactly the way Thane had taught him to do when the pain became unbearable, rather than the inappropriate laughter that Damien was prone to letting out during these peak surges.

It wasn’t that Thane was callous toward the boy, strapped down and suffering as he was. Rather, it was that he knew Marcus was strong, like Damien had been. Plus, Thane had learned from experiments with Damien how to get there faster this time. Within months, Marcus would reach the level that Damien had taken years to achieve. They were right at the finish line.

At the control dashboard, Dr. Cornell Frost, one of Thane’s senior scientists, operated the system in Emmett’s place. Five more minutes remained in this interfacing session, and there was little left for Thane to do unless more serious warning signs appeared.

So, he walked over to Marcus and ran his fingers over the boy’s brown hair, eyeing the large plug in the back of his head. Thirteen years old already. He did try to be more fatherly these days. Little touches of comfort. Brief words of encouragement. Using their names once they’d earned it. Things that were more important for the subjects than he had originally realized.

He glanced toward the observation window, where Raphael, four guards, and two scientists observed. Michelle would normally have been there, but he’d given her the day off as well. He would have to do this more regularly to keep up the momentum. It wasn’t that he disregarded Emmett and Michelle’s perspectives, but there was a time for caution, and a time for progress. They had already charted the cautious course with Damien, and now it was time to retread it more progressively with Marcus. With Price dead and DoD politics uncertain after this mess, it was time to move faster.

Marcus’s breathing faltered, lost rhythm, and he screamed again.

Thane felt sympathy for the boy in his gut, but if achieving godhood demanded pain to get there, then so be it. It was truly within reach now. Marcus would thank him when all was said and done.

Everyone would.



Raphael answered his phone. “What is it?”

“Sir, I have Colonel Rahal from ACI on the line for you. He says it’s urgent. Should I connect you?” asked Deborah, his coordinator.

“You mean his man Flanagan?”

“No, sir, it’s Rahal himself.”

Huh. “Alright, connect us.”

“Yes, sir.”

As Raphael waited, he watched Thane stand there next to the screaming boy. He thought he’d be used to it after all these years, but these tests just seemed to get more unsettling over time.

“Costa, you there?” The colonel’s voice.

“Yes,” Raphael said. “But your guys have my guys’ number. I’ve got my hands full, given the state of things. What do you want?” Ever since the facility had been given surveillance resources equivalent to what ACI could bring to bear, Raphael hadn’t been in much contact with the colonel’s team.

“Well, good morning to you, too,” the colonel said. “I just wanted to call and give you a tip directly. You know, given the state of things. But if you’re going to be an ass, maybe I should’ve let our bureaucracies misplace it instead.”

“Just tell me, Rahal. I’m sure we’re both busy.” Raphael pushed open the door and left the observation room quietly, careful not to disturb the researchers.

“We just flagged a series of 83 to 86 percent matches for Jade down in Florida,” the colonel said. “With all the copycats out there, it might be nothing. But these sightings were in Tampa. Close to MacDill.”

Raphael paused. MacDill. Was she really going for General Rodriguez? With all their defenses?

“You still there, Costa?”

“Are you sure?” Raphael asked.

“No, I’m not fucking sure. That’s what 83 to 86 percent means. But it’s high enough that I wanted to let you know directly. I just called and warned MacDill, and the FBI. Most flags turn out to be nothing. But this is MacDill. You know that was on her list.”

Raphael found himself pacing in the hall. He’d been focusing almost all of his team’s surveillance resources on Jersey, around the facility. This would complicate things. “Can you send us more details?”

“I’ll have one of my agents, Zhou, send them over,” the colonel said. “Now if you’ll excuse me, I’ve got more calls to make.”



Yasmin groaned and rolled over in her sheets to check her buzzing phone.

It was Dad, again. Two missed calls back-to-back. She’d been meaning to reply to his message from nearly a week ago, but time had flown by. It was the heart of fall semester, after all.

Another buzz. This time a text.

Yas, it’s serious, just give me two minutes or I’ll get really annoying, it read. I’ll call the university or do other embarrassing stuff.

She imagined it in Dad’s voice and couldn’t help but smirk. As the phone buzzed yet again with a video call, she forced herself to sit up and answer. “Hey.”

“Oh, so you’re still alive. Good to know, Yas.” He was in the driver’s seat of his parked car somewhere, wearing his trench coat, smiling. The morning sun lit half his face.

“I was sleeping,” she said.

“I figured. That’s why I called now, so you wouldn’t be in class. You okay?”

“Sure. Why wouldn’t I be?”

“Well, sweetheart,” he said, sarcastic as ever, “it is a national state of emergency. The President’s probably shaking under his desk in a bunker somewhere. Least you could do is give me a thumbs-up on my texts.”

“All that stuff is on the East Coast, it’s not like—” She stopped. Wait. “Did it affect you?” How hadn’t she thought about that?

He chuckled, running a hand through his hair. “You could say that.” Something was different about him. A warmer, livelier look, despite the serious topic. “Listen, things are an absolute shit show here and I can’t really talk about it, but I want you to do something. Stay in one of your friends’ dorms for the next couple nights, okay? Not your own. Just in case.”

“Why?”

“I can tell you more later. It’s probably nothing, but I might have a few extra enemies at the moment. Humor me, okay? I’m having your mother do the same thing. And try to keep an eye out in case anyone follows you around campus or something. Call me if they do. Encrypted, of course.”

Yasmin imagined trying to explain this to Katie while asking to sleep over, without sounding like a total weirdo.

“Yas, did you hear me?”

“I’ll do it,” she said, and sighed.

He smiled again. “Good. If this case doesn’t . . .” He trailed off, then seemed to reset himself. “This Thanksgiving, I want to see you. I’ll fly out there, or wherever you’ll be. Just for a day—I know you’ll probably have other stuff with your mother or friends, but I can work around that. Okay?”

“I . . . yeah. Is everything all right?” She brushed her hair back, suddenly self-conscious. How had she not thought to ask him if he’d been caught up by all the stuff in the news?

His eyes grew glossy, but his smile widened. “Well, now that I got in touch with you, yeah,” he said. “I love you, Yas. Always have.”

A surge of emotion formed behind her eyes in response, and she smiled to contain it. “Love you too, Dad. I know.”







Chapter 42



A day after leaving the yacht, Sara sat on Jessica’s living room couch with the lights off. The house was only ten miles from the facility, and sneaking here undetected had been complicated, but Asim had improved the odds by diverting a portion of multiple agencies’ surveillance resources toward MacDill.

She watched through the wide front window as Jessica pulled up to her driveway, the last rays of sunlight flickering through the pine trees from the west. Jessica was either the luckiest guard in the world, or the unluckiest, depending on how you looked at it. Sara preferred to think of it as the former.

The woman stepped inside with her son and closed the door, bringing in the musty scent of dry leaves along with a brief howl of autumn wind. After flipping on the foyer light, placing her keys on a nearby console table with a metallic jingle, and hanging her coat, she froze. Slowly, she turned toward the half-lit living room.

“C17?” she whispered.

“Yes,” Sara said quietly. She had slipped in through a second-floor window, using her telekinesis to unlock it. Then she’d kept her distance from the cleaning bot as it made its rounds every hour, since that was an alarm risk. Infiltration had been part of her training, and burglary wasn’t so hard when you could fly and had incorporeal arms that could reach through glass. “Deactivate the security system. And don’t enter the fake code that silently calls the police, either. I’m not stupid.”

Jessica hesitated, then nodded and tapped the code into the panel. Her son stood beside her, staring at Sara.

“What do you want now?” Jessica asked after she finished. Her face was pale, she took slow, deep breaths.

Sara rose from the couch. “I need a few things, then you and Max can go back to whatever you were doing. I had a similar interaction with another family for the past couple of days. They’re fine.”

Max seemed more curious than afraid. “Who are you?” he asked.

“I used to work at the same place as your mother.” She forced a smile but knew it came off wrong. She didn’t have much experience with kids other than Marcus, and he’d been smarter than her since he first learned to talk.

Max inched back closer to Jessica. “What happened to your face?” he asked.

“A bad person cut me,” Sara said.

“Don’t talk to him!” Jessica shouted. “What things do you need me to do? Haven’t you done enough?”

“Only a little more,” Sara said. “I need to stay here tonight, and tomorrow I’ll need a few favors. But for now, let’s keep Max comfortable. Does he have a favorite movie?”

“Spiderman!” Max shouted.

They both looked down at him.

Sara shrugged. “Let’s put on Spiderman, then.”



Sara sat with Jessica at the kitchen table. Small and cozy, with the muffled sounds of Spiderman leaking in from the living room. Sara looked around, appreciating the normalcy of the place and trying to imagine what it would have been like to grow up here, with parents and all.

“Now what?” Jessica asked.

“Now, you keep Max completely in the dark. Tell him I was playing a prank, that I’m your work friend. Because if you mess this up, I’ll have to lock a six-year-old in a closet, which neither of us wants.”

“And if I go along? Then what?”

“You give me intel, and I use your credentials to infiltrate the Stolguard facility as you. After that, you and Max never see me again.”

“That’s treason on my part,” she said.

“Not really. Tell them I threatened you. They’ll understand. Let’s make this easy like last time. You’re guarding a horrible place. I need to break into that horrible place. Nobody with their kid threatened would get in trouble. Probably.”

Jessica glared at her and then, with some hesitation, nodded. “What do you need?”

“First, I need you to do nothing. And your promise that you won’t find clever ways to reach out. I’ve collected your electronics, but even if I missed something, please don’t use it. Don’t try to outsmart me. If the police come, I’ll have to use you and Max as hostages or kill more officers. So, let’s skip all that, okay?” she said tiredly. “I let you go before,” she added.

“Fine,” Jessica said.

Sara reached incorporeally into Jessica’s chest with her right focus, placing it on her heart. “I can feel your pulse, your lies if you try them. Tell me about the enhanced security at the facility.”

Jessica swallowed. “Raphael . . . he put me on leave for a week after you escaped. His team grilled me to make sure I wasn’t complicit. By the time I came back, they’d tripled the number of drones and guards. Way more of us carry lasers now, including on the roof and grounds. Colonel Torbeth’s Air Force base keeps flights up constantly, with tons more on active standby.”

“And Stallard? Where is he?”

“In the facility. But he doesn’t stay in his quarters now, since he knows they’re a target. He moves around, and only Raphael, the guard subcommanders, and his closest bodyguards know where he is at any given time.”

“Tell me about the drones. What can they do?”

“They’ve got normal vision, plus night vision and thermal imaging. They still patrol the fence like they used to, but now there are more inside and around the main building, too. They have lethal and nonlethal projectiles, but lethal requires human authorization first. They try to detain intruders nonlethally by default.”

Sara nodded. That matched Damien’s data. Jessica’s heartbeat was elevated but not too much. “Do the guards all know each other?”

“Some of us do. The long-timers from Eidolon Solutions. But since they brought in new firms, there are lots of new faces. Most guards from the same firm know each other, but not really across firms. Everyone wears ID badges, though, and you’ll get stopped without one. Front gate guards know the most people. Door guards are often the new ones.”

“How do you all coordinate?”

Jessica sighed. “I’m so screwed for this.” She looked down at the table. “My radio gives access to the facility-wide main guard frequency. Security leaders like Raphael, Fallon, Santiago, and the guard subcommanders have a second frequency. I don’t have access to that. Guards report to their subcommanders, and ultimately to Raphael. And since they were called back from the field to protect against you, Raphael gave us instructions to follow Fallon’s and Santiago’s orders during an attack if they issue any.”

“Do you know what Fallon is planning?” Sara asked. She found herself staring at the drawings pinned to the refrigerator. Eight papers filled with colorful images. Max’s work, clearly. Some of them showed him standing with two smiling parents: Jessica with her auburn hair and a man with short blond hair and a halo over his head. Others showed Jessica with Max alone.

Jessica shrugged. “I mean, that’s not really part of my briefing. Fallon’s coordinating a lot of the defense with Raphael and Santiago, though. I just guard the halls.”

“Do you know of any plans Fallon has for Clare?”

“Um, no. That’s C14 right?”

“Yes. Is Clare there? At the facility?”

Jessica nodded. “She’s one of the subjects that was called back from the field.”

“Is anyone expecting me to come there? Turn myself in?”

“Should they be?” Jessica asked.

Sara studied her face to see if she could sense any lies and found nothing. No heart rate increase, either. Fallon had said that they would keep that plan unknown to most. “Tell me about the facility’s identity verification systems. There’s the ID badges and what else?”

“We have to wear our ID badges everywhere,” Jessica said. “The front gate, the doors to the building, and displayed on your person in the building.”

Sara waited for more, but none came. “And what else? Facial scans, right?”

“Right, but facial scans have some issues,” Jessica said with a shrug. “So they’re used more selectively. Everyone’s face is scanned at the front gate and the building front door, but not at the building’s employee-only side doors, since they’d jam up with hats and sunglasses as people go in and out frequently. Really secure areas like Dr. Stallard’s quarters also have facial scanners.”

“What about the security drones? They scan faces too, right?”

Jessica’s heart started beating quicker.

“Careful,” Sara whispered. “Tell me.”

Jessica took a deep breath. “They do. But here’s the thing. When drones scan from a distance, it’s too glitchy. Early on, they stopped people too often in the corridors. Bad angles, hair in the way, whatever. Workflow broke down, and researchers complained. So, Raphael had the security team tune it down. Inside the building, drones still scan faces, but they only act if they get a clear scan of someone not on the list, rather than acting any time they have an obstructed scan. The drones still check everyone’s ID badges in the corridors, since there’s an RF chip in them and they don’t need line of sight for those, but their facial scans are more of an extra check now.”

Sara thought for a moment. “Does anyone check back seats or trunks each time when employees go through the gate?”

“Only for deliveries, not for employees, since it would create a delay at the gate, especially in the morning. We’ve all had background checks, and we go through the front gate facial scan and ID badge scan, so they consider that enough.”

“You only have a pistol here. Where do the rifles go?”

“We check them in and out of the armory daily. First floor, north side. No one takes them home. Except Raphael.”

“Anything else I should know? If my plan fails from you withholding something, I’ll have to come back for you and Max.” She wouldn’t, of course, but Jessica didn’t need to know that.

“No,” Jessica said quickly. “I swear.”

“Good. The more you give me, the safer you both stay. Now,” Sara said, leaning back in her chair, “I need to look like you.”



Jessica made dinner, including a plate for Sara without the carbs. She put Max to bed, and then Sara put Jessica to bed. She handcuffed one of the woman’s wrists to her bedframe with her own set of guard handcuffs, warning her that if she even tried to break free, Max would die.

Sara now had access to all of Jessica’s equipment: armored vest, uniform, radio, pistol, handcuffs, and ID badge. She still had the yacht family’s electronics as well. The augmented reality sunglasses from the yacht would be particularly useful, with their hands-free recording function.

The hardest part was still ahead, though: hair dye. She eyed the box where it sat on the bathroom counter, amping herself up. Jitters had previously handled it for her and had been the one to suggest it in the first place.

On her way here, dressed as the yacht mother and using that family’s cash, Sara had bought auburn-colored hair dye from a pharmacy to replicate Jessica’s appearance, along with makeup and hair bleach. Black-dyed hair apparently couldn’t turn auburn without first bleaching it, then re-dyeing, which she’d only found out from scrutinizing the directions on multiple boxes.

Jessica wasn’t any help, so Sara worked through it alone. The bleaching, the waiting, then administering the dye. Half an hour in, frustration nearly made her quit, but she forced herself to finish. The result wasn’t perfect, nothing like the outcome Jitters would get effortlessly, but it was passable. She even trimmed the front to mimic Jessica’s side-swept bangs.

In the mirror, an unfamiliar thin face with sunken eyes stared back at her. The scars were a problem, too. She flinched as memories of the van came flooding in, but pushed them away with a shake of her head.

Testing the concealers she’d bought, she found the one that best matched her pale skin and set it aside. Tomorrow, she would spread more of it on to make the scars less noticeable.

Lastly, she went through Jessica’s nail polish, which she’d forgotten to buy. These details mattered. Jessica had purple nail polish on, and so Sara applied the same. It was another frustrating process, since she’d never done it before, though it didn’t really matter whether her work was sloppy. She wasn’t fooling the drones, or even the guards up close. She only needed it so that from a glance, guards would see someone with their nails colored. She’d have to minimize showing her right hand anyway, thanks to the three nails Jolce had ripped out. Another memory to push away.

With Damien’s virtual help, she disabled Jessica’s car horn. She also asked him to update Asim and Ava, telling them her part was going as planned and to be ready for tomorrow.

Sleeping, as always, would be tough. Since her escape, she’d barely managed more than short bursts of it, except for when Damien kept watch for her. Max slept in his bed, and Jessica was only restrained by one hand. That opened a risk; the boy could wake up and go talk to Jessica, and she could give him instructions to slip out and get help. Sara could have restrained both of them more thoroughly to prevent that, but it didn’t feel right. Maybe this would be the mercy that would come back to haunt her.

She curled up on the floor in front of Jessica’s bedroom door. If it opened for any reason, she would hopefully feel it fast enough to act.

With the faint clicks of the kitchen clock and the subtle scent of detergent drifting from the laundry room, she closed her eyes and slipped into a fitful rest.







Chapter 43



Ah, the sweet smell of treason in the morning, Asim thought as he sipped his cappuccino.

He didn’t like the plan, he would pretend he didn’t know about the plan, he expected failure from the plan, and yet here he was, going along with the fucking plan. Hell, he’d even helped to plan part of the plan.

Given an impossible situation, sometimes a man had to pick the best out of a bunch of bad options. Since Sara was going to do something extreme either way, he could at least help maximize results and minimize collateral damage. After all, he knew a thing or two about how to fuck a place up with proper sophistication.

That was what he’d done with Roy and other spec-ops teams in his prior life: help them identify and strike targets as surgically and effectively as possible for the desired outcomes. Some of the things he’d done in the war were arguably worse than this. At least this one was his choice.

The difference, of course, was that this would be highly illegal from the perspective of his own government. Then again, his government’s actions were illegal here too, or at least the portion he was after. They just had more guns on their side.

And assassins, of course. Flanagan’s crew had spotted a short-haired telekinetic woman keeping watch on Asim’s apartment over the past two days. A skilled killer named Dalia, according to Damien. Sent by Stallard, no doubt. It would’ve almost been insulting if the doctor hadn’t sent someone to poke around for a hit by now. But Asim had been sleeping in a spare office at ACI headquarters ever since filing the whistleblower report, so at least the uncomfortable nights hadn’t been for nothing. It was best to look on the bright side.

Sara would have three objectives in her infiltration today. Two of them he supported. The third one, well, it was what it was. He understood it, even if he couldn’t quite condone it.

Lately, he’d been feeling irrelevant. With the FBI, CIA, NSA, DIA, DHS, Stolguard facility, and several alphabet soup parts of the DoD all going after Jade the terrorist, what difference could one man make? He was just another cog in the machine, and whether he did his job well or not, someone else would. That’s what redundancy was for.

His career felt hollow. He’d hated his role in the war, had grown disillusioned with it, and ruined his family along the way. Shifting to counterintelligence work gave him a modicum of fulfillment, focusing on defense rather than offense, but that too had dulled over time. His cushy job practically ran on autopilot—surveillance feeds, his team doing the legwork—while he coasted, directionless and more alone than he’d ever expected to be at this stage of his life.

Well, what he was about to do today was something that nobody at those other agencies would step up and do. If he didn’t, then it wouldn’t get done.

By risking his career, and even his freedom, maybe he would regain some sense of purpose, and a man needed a sense of purpose. In that way, as much as he disliked the plan, it still somehow felt right.



Sara woke up curled against Jessica’s bedroom door, ready for the most dangerous day of her life. Most people would have found the prospect terrifying, but there was almost something comforting about it. An end to this, one way or another.

Sure, the plan had more nuance than that thanks to Damien and Asim, but her part would likely be violent, as always. Sometimes it takes a monster, she reminded herself.

It was Halloween, after all. A day of ghosts and ghouls.

She donned her gear, covered her scars with makeup, released Jessica, gave her instructions, then ate breakfast with her and Max. Sara noticed the boy kept sneaking glances at her, more than he had the night before.

“What is life, to you?” Sara asked Jessica after finishing a bite of bacon. They’d been silent for a while, so it came out more awkwardly than she’d intended.

Max stirred his cereal and slurped down the last soggy pieces, eyeing her.

Jessica looked up from her plate. “What?”

“It’s just, I want to know what you think. You pleaded for your life that night at the rest stop. What makes a good life?”

Jessica glanced at Max, and Sara winced. She wasn’t supposed to say things like that in front of him.

“A good life . . .” Jessica said, looking at Max, “is when you get to act on your own accord. And when you get to spend time with your family and friends, and with God.” She rubbed Max’s shoulder, and he smiled.

“Then the subjects at the facility don’t have good lives by that definition,” Sara said. “Why work there?”

Jessica froze, then set her fork down. “I . . . figured it was for national security. The subjects seemed satisfied enough, and there’s that well-being therapist. And it pays a premium, which I needed after . . . well.” She shrugged. “I never signed up to keep subjects locked in. I guarded it as I would any other building, like my last job. Just more lucratively, with all the extra clearances required.”

Sara shook her head. “You signed up for all of it. Can’t pick and choose the nice parts. You knew the subjects weren’t free.”

“Why do you look like Mom now?” Max asked out of nowhere.

That’s why he’s been looking at me, Sara realized. “It’s my Halloween costume. How close do I look?”

“You’re not as pretty as Mom.”

“Max!” Jessica said, stifling a laugh.

Sara smiled. “Fair enough.” She glanced at their mostly empty plates, then stared at Jessica.

Jessica checked the time. “Okay Max, bus comes in fifteen. Time to get ready. You’re looking forward to seeing Miss Walters, right?”

Max smiled and nodded. Sara could feel the corners of her lips turn upwards as she watched the spark in his eyes. Pure, innocent excitement.

“Good,” Jessica said. “Time to get your shoes on.”

Max slipped into his sneakers while Jessica gathered his school supplies and lunch box into a little pack. She helped him sling it onto his shoulders, then crouched to his eye level and ran a hand over his hair to smooth it out. She tapped her own cheek and smiled at him. Max looked over at Sara shyly, then turned back and pecked a kiss onto Jessica’s cheek. Jessica still smiled as her gaze lingered on him for several seconds.

“Mommm,” he said, drawing the word out, sounding impatient.

“Sorry. Just admiring how handsome you look today.” She leaned in and kissed Max on the forehead, then stood up. Her eyes had gone glossy, holding back tears.

“Where does the bus pick him up?” Sara asked.

“Just down the street. I’ll walk him there and be right back.”

“Can you see it from here?”

“Um, from the lawn, yeah.”

“Maybe today, let Max walk down the street to the stop. You could wait on the lawn and watch until the bus comes.” Sara locked eyes with her to make clear it wasn’t a request. She couldn’t risk Jessica going out too far and signaling anyone. Besides, the things she’d been expected to do at six would terrify these people. That was the year she fired her first gun. A twenty-two caliber.

Jessica stared back, then looked down at Max. “Sure,” she said after a long pause. “Max, we’ll show Sara how much of a big boy you are, okay? Let’s go.”



The morning outside was crisp and clear, with a spotless blue sky overhead and the musty scent of fallen leaves hanging in the air. Sara lay motionless on the backseat floor of Jessica’s SUV, her thin body hidden under a scatter of random junk. She listened intently as Jessica rolled up to the Stolguard facility’s main gate.

“Jess,” the gate guard said through the open window.

“Hey Donnie, happy Halloween,” she said back. Two beeps followed, indicating the facial scan and her ID badge scan were both successful.

“Doing anything tonight with Max?” he asked.

“Just taking him around the neighborhood.”

“Good weather at least, for a change. You’re clear, go ahead.”

The car started moving again. Once they were far enough from the gate station, Sara sat up and looked around. “Alright, stop there,” she said, pointing over Jessica’s shoulder from behind.

Jessica pulled into a quiet corner of the massive lot and killed the ignition. Overhead, a pair of fighter jets roared past, patrolling the airspace.

“Keys and ID,” Sara said.

Jessica handed them over, then put her hands in her lap and lowered her eyes toward them. “You’re going to kill me, aren’t you? That’s why you asked me about life. About why I work here. To try to justify it.”

Sara smiled faintly. The thought had crossed her mind. Knocking people out wasn’t as clean as anyone liked to imagine. They wouldn’t stay unconscious for long without a serious head injury. And a nonlethal choke would only put someone down for a few minutes at most. With all that was on the line, she should just kill her, quickly and painlessly.

Yet she found herself too weak for that and had planned accordingly. “Not if you listen. Hold out your hands.”

Jessica paused, then obeyed. Sara handcuffed the woman’s wrists together through the steering wheel, speaking as she did.

“I disabled your car’s horn last night. Don’t bother honking once I’m gone. And don’t do anything else to attract attention. Just sit here for the next half hour, and then you can start trying to get someone to free you. If you do that, you and Max will live happily ever after. If you mess this up, then you’ll have me as your enemy.”

Once the cuffs were in place, she leaned in close to the side of Jessica’s face. “And trust me, you don’t want me as your enemy.” As she said that last part, she used one of her foci to grab and twist part of the driver’s side door, rendering it impossible to open, and filling the cabin with the grinding sound of steel.

“. . . I won’t mess it up,” Jessica said. She swallowed and put her chin up.

Sara leaned back. “Good. Max needs you more than this place does. Be still, and tonight you can take him trick-or-treating, or whatever it is you do.”

Jessica nodded, and Sara stepped out of the SUV, hoping she’d pushed the intimidation hard enough. Without a working horn or door, and parked far from patrols, it would take time to get attention even once she started kicking and shouting.

Sara walked across the long stretch of asphalt, disguised as Jessica as closely as possible. Armor, gear, auburn-red hair, scar concealer, nail polish, and most importantly, her ID badge. Jessica’s pistol was holstered on her hip. The augmented reality sunglasses from the yacht concealed her eyes, doubling as a video recorder to transmit whatever she saw. As a final touch while walking, she put in wireless earbuds to make it look like she was listening to music and slipped a piece of chewing gum into her mouth.

She spotted guards everywhere. Many of them had lasers, and they’d been strategically spread out to make them hard to disrupt. Several stood on the roof as well. Drones continuously flew around the building perimeter now, rather than just the fence perimeter. Her worst fears about this place were on display—any sort of flying around out here would get her shot down instantly, unless she flew high enough to be out of the lasers’ reach, and up there she’d have the jets and drones to deal with. It would have been impossible to enter the facility without a disguise and genuine ID badge like this, and without Jessica’s real face at the front gate.

Once inside, she’d have plenty of walls for cover against lasers. Until then, these long sightlines were a problem. Her shoulder was still injured, and her whole body ached, but she couldn’t do much about that. A roar sounded throughout the sky, from multiple jets.

She thought about Asim again and smirked. With one secret phone call, he might have already sabotaged this whole plan for all she knew. But Damien had said he trusted him to stick to the mission and would monitor him for signs of subterfuge. She figured that if it came down to Asim turning on them, then it was never meant to be. Without him, whatever she managed here wouldn’t amount to much anyway.

Approaching one of the building’s employee side doors, she thought of Clare to steel herself. This wasn’t a numbers game anymore. She couldn’t quantify the vast threat Damien feared, nor could she know what the future should look like, but she at least knew the world had to see what went on here. And her friends had to be free. Sometimes wars weren’t about numbers, but about principles. When she first left this place, she’d made a promise to herself that she’d come back for Clare and Marcus and others, one way or another.

Well, here she was. Another jet roared overhead.

Two guards were stationed at the door, both with lasers. The scanner beeped and it opened as she reached it, thanks to her ID badge. One door guard seemed more curious than the other, staring a bit too closely, but it was hard to say if she was imagining it or not. She feigned confidence and kept marching forward. Just through the door, no lingering, no second-guessing. She readied herself to crush their heads if they were to so much as twitch, but neither did.

She turned left. The sterile scent and white-lined corridor brought a familiar sense of unease, but she just had to remain visibly confident. Finding Clare was her first objective, so that she couldn’t be used against her. Then Sara could initiate the other two parts of the plan.

“Hey!” shouted some other guard from behind. One of the relatively few women.

Sara waved her hand and kept walking. She couldn’t risk speaking back to someone who likely knew Jessica’s voice.

“Jess?” the woman said, more insistently. Sara ignored her, pretending she didn’t hear. The character she was playing listened to music now. That was why she wore earbuds. Jessica’s formal duty didn’t start until the top of the hour. Normally at this time she’d be walking to the armory to get her rifle.

She strode toward the cafeteria, continuing to project confidence and belonging past two patrolling guards with laser rifles. A lot of the new guards don’t know each other, she reminded herself. But then there was a security drone, monitoring the busy corridor. Her disguise wouldn’t fool it. As she approached, she looked down and pretended to cough, covering her mouth and nose with her hands. Her sunglasses still covered her eyes as well. The drone pivoted toward her, and she tensed, but then it pivoted back. It must’ve scanned the RF chip in her ID badge and found it to be genuine, and Jessica had been right: the drones were tuned not to overreact after a missed facial scan. She took a deep breath of relief.

At the cafeteria, several subjects and guards were eating breakfast, but not Clare. Of course. That would’ve been too easy. She turned back, walked down another corridor toward the facility’s eastern stairwell, went in, and ascended.

A door opened above, followed by the sound of footsteps. She paused to listen; it seemed casual, neither running nor sneaking. A moment later, Carter and his imposing frame rounded the corner of the next flight of stairs. He had a holstered pistol on his hip but otherwise seemed to be off duty. No armor. No rifle.

He looked at her and stopped. Sara slowed and eyed him for a moment, pretending to be casual, but yes, he knew. Shit. She’d hoped to avoid close run-ins with other subjects like this. His right hand inched toward his pistol, and she sighed.

With one focus she crushed the pistol, then the ceiling camera, and with her other focus she grabbed him by the throat, choking him before he could shout. Not too hard; she didn’t want to crush it yet.

But Carter broke out from her grip and lunged. She had gotten used to manipulating normal people, but Carter was strong, and she’d held back too much. In response, she re-gripped him harder, just before he reached her. It was easy enough, but she fought not to overdo it. She squeezed his neck, making sure to press on both of his carotid arteries. Seconds went by, and his thrashing subsided as she laid his unconscious body on the steps.

Now what?

If she left him like this, he’d wake up within minutes and become a problem. Logically, she should kill him—there was no reason to give this place any potential edge. Yet, she hesitated. Her pulse quickened, tension rising from her indecision.

She swallowed, steadied herself, and instead used one of her foci to bash his thigh in, breaking his femur with an awful crack, like a branch snapping. It would keep him sidelined for the day, but with his enhanced healing he’d recover after all this was done.
