She kept a wary eye on him as she slipped past and continued up the stairs, leaving his broken body behind. One of these mercies would come back to get her killed, she knew.

She had to move quickly. People rarely stayed unconscious for long. Carter would wake up and get help, and a camera had now been disabled, which would be flagged almost immediately in the facility’s heightened state. The Jessica disguise would start wearing thin as word spread.

Sara stepped out of the stairwell doorway onto the second floor and strode past the Class B dormitories toward the Class C wing. Three guards with lasers patrolled the corridor, and she prepared to strike if they so much as flinched. But none of them showed any inkling of recognition or concern, and she proceeded straight to Clare’s room.

This variable was a big unknown. Although Sara had already checked off the cafeteria as a likely spot during breakfast hours, Clare might be in her room, in a restroom, or somewhere else in the facility, like the pool. Still, she had to start somewhere.

She knocked lightly and casually opened the door, careful not to draw the guards’ attention. And inside was . . . Jolce sitting at Clare’s desk alone, in armored combat attire, reading manga. Jolce turned around to look. Why—

“Sara? Is that you?” Jolce asked, then smiled as she stood up and dropped what she was reading on the desk. “I can’t believe you’re this stupid. I thought Fallon was wasting my time, but she was right. How’d you even get in?”

“What are you . . .” The hair on Sara’s neck rose as she looked around for traps, and noticed a camera attached to the room’s ceiling. Normally the subjects’ rooms didn’t have cameras. She mentally crushed it.

The facility’s building-wide emergency alarm started blaring.

“Too late. Everyone will know you’re here now,” Jolce said, shrugging. “I’m supposed to tell you that if you leave this room or harm me, Clare dies. Stay here and surrender.”







Chapter 44



Sara’s mind raced. She stepped fully into the room and locked the door. Staying in the corridor for even a second longer would be suicide, now that the alarm had been triggered and laser rifles were everywhere. She avoided the room’s east-facing window too, since drones and laser-wielding guards patrolled the grounds. This room was now a beacon, drawing forces in.

“You’re in on this plan to hurt Clare?”

“Only if you refuse to surrender,” Jolce said with a grin.

“If Clare dies, so do you,” Sara said.

Jolce’s eyes narrowed. “I’ll be the least of your worries in a moment.”

“Target confirmed in Clare’s room,” Santiago’s voice said over both Jolce’s and Jessica’s radios. “Red-brown hair instead of black or blond. Team en route.”

“I’m getting into position, package en route,” Fallon’s voice added, but only through Jolce’s radio, not Jessica’s. That had to be the leaders’ frequency.

“Roger,” Santiago said, only through Jolce’s radio.

Sara’s pulse hammered, and options spun through her mind. She could burst out the window, but the facility grounds were blanketed by laser coverage, and Fallon might go through with her threat to kill Clare. From outside the door came a growing commotion. The guards in the corridor could have kicked it in by now, but they knew the threat she posed from behind it and were clearly planning something more deliberate.

A phone rang. It sat on the bed.

“That’ll be for you. Answer it,” Jolce said, shaking her head. “I still can’t believe Fallon was right.”

Sara paused, unwilling to take her eyes off Jolce. After Fallon, Jolce was the strongest telekineticist left, and an experienced assassin. Cautiously, Sara picked up the phone and angled it so that both the screen and Jolce stayed in her line of sight. It was a video call. She answered.

“Sara?” Fallon’s smiling face appeared. She wore her armored combat attire and held Clare in front of her, one arm wrapped loosely around her neck. “Nice costume. But you didn’t follow my instructions. Tell her, Clare.”

“Protect yourself, Sara!” Clare shouted.

Fallon scowled and choked Clare hard, glancing down at her. “That’s not what you agreed to say. Why is everyone so unreliable?”

“Stop!” Sara shouted.

“I will, as long as you listen,” Fallon said, her eyes back on the camera, and looming a few inches taller behind Clare. She eased her arm a bit, but Clare was still partially choking with Fallon’s arm semi-tight around her neck. Fallon was probably using one of her foci to immobilize Clare too, since Clare wasn’t reaching for the arm. “There will be a knock at your door by a lab dork. You’ll open it and let him give you an injection. That’s all. No reason to fight. Nobody has to get hurt, especially Clare here.” She kissed Clare’s temple and stared at Sara through the camera.

Sara’s heart pounded in her chest. What could she do? Should she just surrender? Let the entire mission end in failure, just like that? A loud knock came at the door.

She glanced toward it, then back to the phone, trying to study Fallon’s background. Where is she?

“He’s here. Open it,” Jolce said, loudly enough for Fallon to hear through the phone as well.

Fallon appeared to be on the second floor like they were, judging by the same carpet style. The morning sun slanted in through a window at her side. Facing eastward, then, like the room Sara stood in. A long row of Class C bedrooms faced east along the corridor she’d come in from.

“I’ll count to three, Sara,” Fallon said. “Then I’ll start ripping body parts off Clare if you haven’t taken the injection. I’m not bluffing. Let’s avoid that.” She tightened her arm around Clare’s throat again, turning her face red and forcing her to gasp.

Sara clenched her fists. They were definitely in another bedroom. She caught a nightstand at the edge of Fallon’s video.

“One.”

Was it Fallon’s bedroom? Would they be there? If so, that was only three bedrooms over to the left—her prized corner suite. Sara instinctively turned and looked in that direction. Someone knocked on the door again.

“Two.”

No. Sara turned back. A hair tie rested on the nightstand next to Fallon and Clare. Fallon never wore them. Her chin-length cut couldn’t gather into a tie; she only wore clips, if anything. Sara glanced at Jolce. The tie was just like the one she wore for her long braid. On the screen, Clare sagged, falling unconscious from Fallon’s choke, her struggle ceasing.

“Three.”

Jolce’s room was . . . five rooms down in the opposite direction, to the right. Jolce and Clare had likely been switched after Fallon’s threat. That was part of Fallon’s trap, in case Sara tried something like she had today. And she’d fallen right into it.

“Time’s up,” Fallon said. “I’ll start with an ear, then.”

Now or never. Hopefully the rooms in between were unoccupied, given the circumstances.

She planted her bracers and blasted straight at the wall with her right focus, aimed toward Jolce’s room. A wide and energy-inefficient directional blast, harder than any other telekineticist besides Fallon could do. The air turned frigid, frost settling on the carpet around her feet.

The kinetic blast tore through five walls, five bedrooms, straight to where she hoped Fallon was, and parallel to the long corridor that Sara had come in from. At the fifth room, it slammed into a strong resistance, and Fallon’s video call cut out. Dust rose into the air from the rubble in the series of shattered rooms ahead.

Jolce attacked. Both of her foci surged toward Sara from the left, with lethal force. The air grew colder still, but Sara was ready. She mentally grabbed both of Jolce’s foci with her left focus. Jolce pulled her foci back, splayed her fingers and split her foci into several sharp points each like the spiked wings of some demonic angel, then relaunched them. Sara split her left focus into just as many parts to immobilize each one. Ironically, it was Clare who’d trained her in this.

Jolce’s nostrils flared. Her strength surged as she pushed with everything she had, trying to break through and reach Sara’s body. But it wasn’t enough. Not even close. Sara held firm with just her left focus.

With both her foci firmly blocked, Jolce reached for the pistol at her hip. She was only a few feet away, so Sara lunged. With her right hand, she grabbed the weapon, and with her left, she shoved Jolce back hard, tearing the gun from her grip in the process.

Jolce stumbled backward. Disarmed and snarling as she recovered, she looked as though she might physically rush back in, but stopped herself. They both knew how that would end; she was small and had never taken martial arts training seriously. Sara held Jolce’s pistol down at her side, with Jessica’s still holstered on her hip.

Jolce’s foci had already weakened from the distraction. Instead of coming closer, she refocused and tried to break both of her foci through Sara’s left focus, but she failed to gain any ground.

Sara’s instinct was to end Jolce right there, but she hesitated. If anyone deserved it, it was her. There probably was no other choice . . .

“Idiot!” Fallon shouted, her voice distant.

Both Sara and Jolce looked through the line of busted walls and rubble as some of the dust settled. Fallon stood about forty yards away in the fifth room, Jolce’s room, facing them with her forearms in front of her in the shape of an X. Both of Fallon’s ethereal foci crisscrossed out in front of her, matching the shape, forming a shield.

Clare lay slumped at Fallon’s feet, seemingly unconscious. Likely from the choke. For Clare’s sake, Sara had purposely blasted no harder than she knew Fallon could block, hoping she would do so in time, and of course she had.

“Fallon! Status?” Santiago shouted over the main frequency, his voice coming out of both Jolce’s and Jessica’s radios. The whole facility would’ve heard the blast.

“Plan B. Engaging target now,” Fallon said in a low voice over the same frequency. “Let’s go.”

Fallon’s eyes flared with visible rage, and her hands turned to fists as she dropped them down to her sides. Thick frost spread all around her on the floor, and both of her foci surged forward toward Sara, forming an even stronger combined kinetic counterblast back through the five rooms, and equally as wide.

Sara had no time to dodge. She could block it, but likely not with only one focus. And letting go of Jolce’s foci to block Fallon with both of her own would mean death from Jolce. It was two versus one.

Sara mentally grabbed both of Fallon’s blasting foci with just her right focus, trying to halt their momentum like she had with Jolce’s. But damn, they were strong. As she suspected, her one focus wasn’t enough to stop both of Fallon’s. So, she pivoted and used the full might of her right focus to push Fallon’s dual blasting foci toward Jolce’s side of the room, and simultaneously took a swift step away from Jolce. Slightly redirecting was more doable than outright stopping.

Jolce widened her eyes with last-second realization and was liquefied by the hit, splattering into guts and bone shards as Fallon’s dual-foci blast ripped that whole side of the room apart. The wall behind Jolce disintegrated with a thunderous crash, and the east-facing windows next to her shattered outward into the cool autumn air, with drops of blood mixed among the glass.

Both of Fallon’s foci whipped back toward Sara. With Jolce’s foci now gone, Sara used each of her foci to grab and hold each of Fallon’s. They became locked in a full telekinetic grapple, with Fallon trying to ram both of her foci straight through her chest like ethereal spears, and Sara holding them back.

Fallon screamed, a rising guttural roar, her voice echoing through the ruined rooms as well as out of Jessica’s radio, as she somehow pushed harder and harder. Sara gritted her teeth and held firm. It took a tremendous amount of energy, more than she’d ever expended at once before, and her head throbbed. The air turned arctic, and a massive circle of frost widened across the floor all the way to the walls.

A heavy slam shook the door a few feet away. Not good. Both of her foci were preoccupied protecting herself from Fallon, so she took a step back and readied the pistol she’d taken from Jolce. She couldn’t aim properly when concentrating so much on telekinesis, but these shots would be up close. She prepared herself.

The door burst open with a second slam, and Sara shot at it from the side, dropping the first guard to come in, then the second and third, all with headshots from a few feet away, before they could get a shot off.

She had the advantage of a chokepoint, knowing where they’d come from, while they had to turn left and spot her in the room before getting a fix on her. But there would be countless more out there now, and her foci weakened briefly whenever she concentrated on taking a shot, even up close. Still locked in a telekinetic grapple with Fallon across the rooms, she waited for a fourth and fifth to come through the doorway, but they paused for a moment.

Fallon’s scream subsided, but her eyes still stared daggers down through the rooms toward Sara, and her foci kept pushing insanely hard. Through Jessica’s radio, Sara heard Fallon speak again, sounding hoarse. “Go in, Santiago. I have her pinned but can’t hold much longer.”

No! Her pistol would be useless against Santiago in his full head-to-toe, heavy armor. Or any armored Class B member.

But . . . Fallon’s push was diminishing. She was strained. Tiring faster than Sara. Using dynamic inclusion, Sara split her left focus to grab both of Fallon’s foci, then took the risk of releasing her right focus from the grapple.

With everything she had, she held back both of Fallon’s weakening foci with only her left, just in time to crush Santiago’s armored head with her right focus as he burst through the doorway. But he moved fast; a laser blast that he managed to get off at the same time struck her left side, straight through her armored vest, sending a shower of golden sparks into the room and a surge of agony back through her body.

As Santiago’s headless body crashed to the floor with a wet slam, splattering some of its blood onto her, she screamed and fell to one knee, dropping her pistol to the frozen carpet. Fallon’s two foci were suddenly inches away from spearing through her chest, and she frantically re-concentrated on holding them back. The split-second distraction had almost been enough for them to fatally close the distance.

Another guard came through the open doorway behind Santiago. There were legions out there. Sara strained to keep both of Fallon’s foci at bay with her left focus, while with her right focus she crushed that guard. Not just his head, but the top half of his body as well, since it was so hard to even aim her mental grip in this state. He splattered into bloody chunks across the room.

Three drones flew in, straight through the spray of blood before it could even settle, but Sara crushed those, too. Then with her right focus, she picked up Clare’s bed and desk and slammed them against the open doorway as a temporary barricade, rattling the concrete wall on impact. Her recording sunglasses had fallen off somewhere.

So. Much. Pain. She squeezed her wet eyes shut and concentrated all her might on holding back both of Fallon’s encroaching foci with her left focus, while also holding the barricade against the doorway with her right as someone pounded on it.

Is this it? The end? There were too many of them, and the pain was unbearable. Had this whole thing been doomed from the start? Like her and Damien’s escape had been?

“Just let go,” Fallon’s hoarse voice said through Jessica’s radio, “and I’ll make it quick.”

Sara’s head throbbed. Her side burned. She laughed out loud to distract herself from the agony as she tried but slowly failed to hold back both of Fallon’s foci, injured as she was now, as they continually pushed toward her, closing the remaining gap inch by inch. With her eyes still closed, she heard a shotgun blast burst through the makeshift doorway barricade. That wouldn’t hold much longer either. It would be so easy to just . . .

No. Not yet. That inhuman expression on Marcus’s face flashed in her mind, with cities in ruin. Damien’s concerned eyes, telling her of what would come. These unchecked assassinations, and Asim ready to go all-in against them if she could just give him an opening. If there was a time to be stubborn, it was now.

She opened her wet eyes, still on one knee, pulled Jessica’s pistol from the holster on her hip, and leveled it at Fallon across the five rooms.

The mental strain made wielding foci and pistols at the same time nearly impossible, especially aiming from forty yards away. But she had no choice.

Fallon’s eyes went wide. She yanked her own pistol from its holster like a Western-style fast draw, frantically firing first. The bullet buzzed inches past Sara’s temple, and Fallon’s foci weakened briefly from her fractured concentration.

Sara exhaled and took a second to aim amid the chaos, remembering Bronn’s training and her years of daily practice. Marksmanship was all she had back then. She squeezed the trigger an instant before Fallon could fire again—and scored a hit straight through Fallon’s neck.

Fallon gasped, collapsing backward against the wall, and her foci vanished inches from Sara’s chest, freeing her from their oppressive force.

Sara still had her room’s door barricaded with her right focus, but two guards came through the doorway of the adjacent room in front of her and looked left toward her through the giant hole in the wall. She crushed their heads with her left focus, now that it was free from Fallon’s grapple.

Finally, she looked down at her laser burn.

The blast had seared her left side, straight through armor and flesh, but a glancing enough hit through the skin and muscle on her side to miss her organs. Still, every twist of her torso sent a fresh burst of agony from the area. It hurt even more than when Asim had shot her through the shoulder, since it was impossible to isolate the abdomen’s movements.

Another shotgun blast came through the makeshift barricade, which she still held against the room’s doorway with her right focus. Her breath turned ragged, and she shivered from shock, but it was time to move. She used her left focus to painfully pick herself up and flew over to Fallon and Clare, through the five broken walls of the five broken rooms.







Chapter 45



Sara watched as Clare stirred, her eyes opening. Fallon’s were squeezed shut, but she was conscious, slumped over and clutching her neck, coughing and bleeding out. With that much blood, the shot must have struck an artery.

After checking her surroundings, Sara spent a few seconds with both her foci barricading the door and blocking part of the hole in the wall with furniture.

Fallon looked up, bared her teeth, and weakly lashed out with both foci again. Sara caught them with her left focus, releasing part of the barricade briefly, then pistol-whipped Fallon across the face with her right hand, stunning her and making her foci vanish for the second time. Fresh blood came from Fallon’s mouth on the impact.

“Clare, come on. We have to go,” Sara said, trying to get her up faster. Someone pounded on the door, and Sara used her right focus to hold the room’s desk tightly against it as a barricade.

“You’ll nev . . . get out,” Fallon said, then spit out blood. Her voice was little more than a gurgle. “Should’ve . . . listened to me.”

Sara knelt, grabbed Fallon by the hair, and looked into her eyes. “Where’s Stallard? Tell me, or I’ll rip pieces of you off one at a time like you threatened Clare.”

Fallon smiled, eyes barely open, with blood smeared across her lower face. “Such a . . . sharp blade.”

Sara used her left focus to bash Fallon’s thigh, snapping her femur with a sick crunch like she had with Carter earlier. Fallon arched her back and gasped with her bloody mouth, a silent scream. The barricaded door was still being pounded on, and now someone started to shoot through it. Sara stayed low to the floor. She couldn’t hold this room much longer against so many people. Eventually, it would be breached. Her head was splitting in pain; she had used too much energy in this fight. Fallon closed her eyes and leaned her head back against the wall.

“Fine. I’m done with this,” Sara said, reaching out to crush Fallon’s head with her left focus. She didn’t like killing downed combatants, but Fallon was too dangerous to leave alive, and she was bleeding out anyway. This wasn’t a time for mercy.

“Stop!” Clare shouted, awake now. Her two foci grabbed Sara’s left focus. “She’s done!”

Sara turned. “Don’t you know what she was going to do to you?”

“She was trying to keep others safe,” Clare said, sitting up and pressing her palm over Fallon’s bleeding neck. “She apologized when she brought me here, and wanted me to convince you to surrender during the call. She really thought you would. I know that she’s . . .” Clare trailed off and just looked back at Sara, her eyes pleading, seemingly not knowing what else to say.

Sara could have effortlessly pushed through Clare’s two foci to finish Fallon off, but she couldn’t bring herself to do it, not with Clare looking at her like that. She let the tension go in her left focus and locked eyes with her friend as more shots blasted through the nearby door.

“Do you know where Stallard is?” she asked.

Clare shook her head.

Sara grabbed Fallon’s radio. “Fallon has fallen,” she said into the radio’s main frequency, trying to sound as vicious as possible. “So have Santiago and Jolce. For anyone hearing this, leave the building if you value your life. I’m not your enemy.”

“Is that C17?” some guard asked, sounding alarmed. “Is Fallon really down?”

“It’s coming from Fallon’s radio,” another said, voice grim.

“Both class commanders?” That was Quinn’s voice. C8.

“Hold your stations,” Raphael said, loud and firm.

More chaotic chatter followed. Morale was breaking, both among subjects and guards. The pounding and shooting on the barricaded door ceased as they reassessed their next steps with a fractured leadership structure. Still, Sara knew dozens must be out there, with hundreds on the broader grounds and countless more security drones. Clare kept working to suppress Fallon’s bleeding, using her telekinesis on the blood itself in addition to her hands on the wound.

“Now what?” Quinn asked. She was the oldest remaining member of Class C who was still active somewhere. “Both of our class commanders are down.” Fallon’s radio had a secondary frequency for leaders like Jolce’s did, and Quinn seemed to be speaking on that.

“You’re the new Class C commander, then,” Raphael said on the leaders’ frequency. “And Bronn, you have Class B. Hades fallback plan initiated. Hold your stations in the meantime.”

“Acknowledged,” Bronn said. “Careful what you say here.”

What did that mean? Hades fallback plan? Underground?

If she understood correctly, the basement seemed a rather risky place to fall back to. It was more protected due to narrow chokepoints, but there were also fewer exit paths if those chokepoints were breached. And was it the basement or the sub-basement? Who would be there? Or maybe she was misunderstanding what he meant entirely.

“Clare,” Sara said, breathing heavily, “my mission’s messed up now. I can’t do both of my remaining objectives. I need you to do something.”

“What’s all this for?” Clare shouted, looking back toward Sara as she tended to Fallon, her hands covered in blood. “Why are you doing this?” There were tears in her eyes, and as she glanced down at Sara’s laser burn, they watered further.

“I want to free the rest of you, and I have to stop what Stallard is going to do with Marcus. Damien discovered something so dangerous before he died, Clare. I’m doing this with him. But with Fallon’s trap, this setback, I need your help.”

“You’ve killed so many,” Clare said. “And you’re hurt.”

Sara nodded, out of breath, pain coming from everywhere, and reached into her pocket. Hopefully it wasn’t broken from the fight. “Please, just listen. Your part is peaceful. Go to the server room upstairs on the third floor and connect this memory drive to server rack seven. Quickly. This will transmit data from this facility to our allies on the outside. It might help them shut this place down and set you all free. Damien wrote the code himself. He already has a transmitting program running here, and he gave me directions on where to insert this to bring down the facility’s firewall and let the data out. Server rack seven, specifically.” She held out the memory drive to Clare and looked into her eyes. “Please, Clare. It’s me. If I somehow get through this, I’ll tell you everything. I know it looks awful.”

“How can I get up to the server room through so many people?” Clare asked.

“They’re not after you. It was only Fallon and Stallard’s plan to use you against me, since it would hurt morale if too many knew. Jolce and Santiago were in on it too, I guess. I have to go downstairs. They’ll come after me. I know you can find a way upstairs. You’re on their team, after all.” Sara smiled, pretending to look confident even though she was anything but.

Sara looked around the rubble of Jolce’s room. Those basement chokepoints would be well protected, and by people who knew what they were doing, like Raphael and Bronn, who were still around somewhere. Seeing a piece of broken mirror on the floor, originally from Jolce’s bedroom wall, Sara brought it over to herself with her left focus and grabbed it with her hand. It could come in handy.

Clutching the memory drive in one hand and keeping her other on Fallon’s neck, Clare furrowed her brow in uncertainty. Fallon was limp, lying against the wall with her eyes closed, barely breathing. She would’ve almost looked peaceful if not for all the blood.

Sara brought the radio to her mouth. “Only Clare and Fallon are left in Jolce’s room. Don’t fire at it. Fallon needs emergency care.”

“Sara . . .” Clare said.

“I trust you.” Sara looked down and blasted a narrow hole in the floor. “Trust me?” She glanced back up and smiled, then dropped through the hole, using one of her foci to slow her descent.







Chapter 46



Sara landed in a men’s restroom on the first floor. A guard stepping out of a stall turned to face her, gasped, and reached for his pistol. Sara crushed his weapon and mentally shoved him hard against the wall.

As more jets thundered outside, their sound vibrating through the building’s walls, she tried to get her bearings straight. If she was going underground, the central stairwell was the best option, since it descended to both the basement and the sub-basement, unlike the other stairwells that stopped at the basement level. The industrial elevator went down there too, but using it now was too risky, and it was located in the same central shaft anyway.

From the hole in the ceiling above came shouting and the sounds of her makeshift barricades being torn apart, along with Clare’s sweet voice amid the chaos. Hopefully Clare would be safe—and would trust her enough to do her part. She couldn’t help but smirk to herself at the thought. This must have looked so insane to Clare. Sara wouldn’t blame her if she refused to act. She didn’t even trust herself. Not truly. Why should Clare? And yet Clare’s actions were just as important right now as Sara’s final objective.

Another jet roared. Was it her imagination, or were they getting more frequent? They’d probably been alerted to the infiltration by this point and were tightening airspace control.

“Target went through the floor, somewhere on level one now,” Quinn’s voice said over the main frequency. “Fallon’s dying. Med team to level two, Jolce’s room.” Sara still had Fallon’s radio with her, since it gave access to their communications, including the leaders’ frequency.

The guard in the restroom stirred. Sara slammed him once more with her right focus, then picked him up with it. She pushed him through the doorway, using his body as a levitating shield, and stepped through after him.

A laser blast came at her from a female guard, but Sara’s makeshift shield took the hit. She crushed the female guard’s laser rifle with her left focus, hurled the injured guard toward her, and sprinted down the hall in the other direction despite the searing in her side. Two more guards wielding standard assault rifles with pistols at their hips stood ahead of her, along with a levitating security drone. With one focus, she crushed both their heads and the security drone’s shell, and with a second focus she blocked the bullet that the drone had been able to fire before being crushed.

She slipped around a corner, down a smaller corridor, through a doorway, and into the central stairwell. Gasping in pain, she mentally crushed the ceiling camera and paused to gather more resolve, taking deep breaths. So much for being a ninja. It was the Pentagon all over again, just a monster on a rampage. But some of this blood was on Fallon’s hands; if not for her trap in Clare’s room, Jessica’s disguise would have lasted longer.

It didn’t matter; there was no time to dwell. Now that she was away from major sightlines, she could try stealth again. Sara mentally twisted off the nearest portion of the stairs’ metal railing to jam the steel door she had just come through, buying herself a little time against the next wave. After eyeing her work, she headed down the stairs, on alert for guards.

Like in other stairwells in the facility, each flight of stairs doubled back in the opposite direction of the prior one, with a series of small landings in between. As she reached the basement level, she crushed the camera there and crouched near the door to listen. It didn’t sound like anyone was in the corridor outside of it. She inched the door open and levitated her mirror shard out to see down the corridor to the left, using the open door as cover on her right side. From what the mirror showed, there were plenty of closed doors but no people around. She sent the shard farther out, past the slightly open door, and flipped it to look down the corridor to the right. Empty. Voices drifted from that direction, though. From the pool area.

She grabbed the mirror shard out of the air and snuck down the hall toward the pool, listening to doors along the way, until a familiar voice sounded from behind.

“Freeze, Sara,” Bronn whispered. “Keep looking forward. I’ve got a laser on your spine, so don’t try anything sudden.”

She froze in place, her shoulders tightening. How had he been so silent, even to her ears? She considered lethally blasting back behind herself without looking right away, but he was so fast that he’d probably get his shot off too. They’d both die. And this was Bronn of all people.

“Where’d you come from?” she asked.

“It’s my job, Sara. It’s all I do. What are your goals?” Even when he was speaking softly, his voice had a resonance behind it. Like the sound of distant, rumbling thunder.

“To find Stallard. No one else,” she said.

“He isn’t on this level. This is where the children and their caretakers were evacuated to. There can be no fighting here.”

“Did he go deeper, down to the sub-basement?” she asked.

He remained silent.

“Bronn. It’s me. If you tell me where he is, I can minimize casualties.”

“Stopping you here would end casualties now, Sara.”

She sighed. “Yes, but it would lead to more down the line from a much greater threat than me. Do you know what Stallard was doing with Damien? What he’s still doing with Marcus?”

He didn’t respond.

“Those children you’re protecting,” she said. “Do you want them to grow up like us? Forced to kill? Or would you rather they be free?” She wished she could see his face, and that in return he could see the tears welling up in her eyes. “It’s still me, Bronn, I swear. I have allies on the outside. This wasn’t meant to be so bloody.”

After a few tense seconds, he spoke. “Go downstairs. I’ll try to delay them, but no promises.”

Her tight shoulders eased. Despite his prior instructions, she turned around to face him. He tensed, trigger finger ready, but she smiled and showed her palms. “I missed you,” she said. His heavy armor covered his face and body, so she couldn’t see his expression. “I have to go back the way I came,” she added.

He treaded backward, still pointing his laser rifle at her as she walked forward, but after a few steps, he lowered it. Now that she saw him, whether he pointed it or not, she could use one focus to block his trigger and another to crush his head, and he surely knew that. He had let her turn around, after all.

“In case I don’t see you again, thank you,” she said.

He nodded, and she slipped through the door, back into the stairwell. Clare should have reached the server room by now. Or so she hoped.



“It’s starting,” Damien said. “She brought the firewall down. I’m receiving terabytes of data from their core database, and it seems my programs are working as expected.”

Asim released the bridge of his nose, which he’d been pinching so hard that it’d gone numb. Both he and Damien had been holding their metaphorical breaths for the past several minutes, fearing that Sara had been killed when her recording sunglasses stopped transmitting. The last thing they’d seen was Santiago’s laser shot, and the last thing they’d heard was Sara’s awful scream. Yet, minutes later, the database transmission started. How had she managed that?

“Holy shit,” Asim said. “That means I actually have to go through with my part of the plan. I almost hoped for my sake she’d fuck this up.” He looked over at Damien and smiled.

Damien nodded, but he remained expressionless, saying nothing.

“What’s wrong? This means your girlfriend’s still alive. She made it to the server room somehow.” His words were as much for his own sake as they were for Damien.

“You heard that scream,” he said. “That she got to the server room is promising, but we don’t know how, and she’s still in danger. That’s the part I hated from the start—her potential exit strategies are so limited. And by now, Colonel Torbeth is probably sending reinforcements as well. It’ll be inescapable.”

He was right of course. Sara’s part in this was practically a suicide mission, but she’d been adamant about doing it anyway. Asim found himself wanting to comfort Damien and had to remind himself that he was only a mimic.

“I’m sure she’ll find a way. I shot her before, but it still worked out somehow. And don’t forget to send me the message when the download is finished,” Asim said with a false smile.

“Mimics don’t forget,” Damien said. “That’s my problem.”







Chapter 47



“Update on target’s location?” Raphael asked on the main frequency.

“Multiple cameras just went offline in the central stairwell,” replied a woman who sounded like a coordinator.

Well, there goes that. Sara crept down the central stairwell one flight at a time toward the sub-basement as quietly as possible, not that it mattered much now. At each landing, before she turned the corner to go down the next flight in the opposite direction, she levitated out her mirror shard to check for threats first.

At the fifth landing, as she floated it out, she caught a glimpse of Raphael, Romulus, and several guards with laser rifles at the bottom of the final flight. Six people total, all with lasers, along with maybe eight security drones and a thick steel barricade to use for cover. Romulus shot the shard into pieces before she could pull it back. Damn his reaction time.

His laser blast also drilled several inches deep into the concrete wall of the stairwell landing. Just the sight of those sparks made Sara’s burnt side flare in pain again. She’d been doing her best to ignore it, but each step and every movement sent another scorching sensation through her body.

She exhaled. Deep down, she’d known it would come to this. Despite all the planning, this felt like the Pentagon. No room for error. No unnecessary risks. She could blast diagonally down through the second-to-last flight of stairs that she was using for cover with lethal force and end them. Too much was on the line, she was this close to finishing her mission, and her pain-induced rage brought her to the brink of doing exactly that. They’d all be ready to shoot lasers the second she rounded the corner to try to grip any of their weapons, so she had to blindside them.

But she was trying to be better, and Raphael had likely saved her life from Fallon two years earlier. Romulus was a narcissist but nothing worse, and with her luck, those other four guards probably all had big families or tragic backstories.

She clenched her fists. “Put down your guns and leave! Please don’t make me kill anymore. My fight isn’t with any of you.”

“You’re fucking insane!” Romulus shouted.

“Sara,” Raphael said in a more measured tone. “Just turn back and surrender to the team above.”

“You know I can’t do that. One more chance,” Sara said, almost pleading. “I won’t hurt anyone who walks up the stairs unarmed, right now. Ten seconds.”

There were whispers and footsteps, then a laser shot and a thud.

“No quarter for deserters. Hold the line,” Raphael said, voice low. Had he killed one of those who’d tried to leave like she offered?

“What happened?” she asked.

Silence.

“What happened!”

“Target in central stairwell, sub-basement level,” Raphael said over the main frequency. “Send major reinforcements down to flank now.”

“Acknowledged,” someone said in response. Probably a guard subcommander.

Sara gritted her teeth as fury washed over her. There was nothing more to say. She blasted diagonally through the edge of the second-to-last flight of stairs with lethal force, down toward where she knew the group was stationed. She’d been delusional to think that Stallard and Raphael’s core chokepoint would be soft, and they’d likewise been delusional to underestimate her capacity for violence. Sometimes it takes a monster.

She heard their screams, and the rumbling moan of the stairwell as it shifted under her feet, its structural integrity impaired. She couldn’t be sure she’d hit them all, but from the sheer force of the blast, she knew most or all must be dead. She burst around the corner onto the last flight of stairs to look, ready to crush anything that still seemed like a threat.

There was nothing but ruined bodies, shattered drones, and rubble. Only one of them coughed and squirmed.

Raphael was dead. Four other guards were dead. Romulus was down and gasping amid the rubble, partially protected by his ruined heavy armor.

Sara stepped down to the sub-basement where the bodies were, crushed the ceiling camera, then looked back up the stairs as a commotion echoed from a floor or two above. The reinforcements.

Using her foci, she ripped down the bottom flight of concrete and steel stairs that she’d just come down, as well as the flight above them, collapsing them with a grinding roar into a rubble-filled blockage. That would block whatever team was coming, but not for long.

Ignoring the sound of settling chunks of concrete, she toggled the radio mic and spoke over the main frequency. “Raphael’s dead. I have his chokepoint now. Whoever comes down dies next.” It didn’t take any effort to sound savage this time.

“Bronn?” Quinn said over the leaders’ frequency, panicked.

“Colonel Torbeth and his forces are en route,” Bronn said over the main frequency. “I’m taking over Raphael’s security command in the meantime. Hold off on breaching until we organize a concentrated force. Maintain positions, and stop using these frequencies. They’re compromised. I’ll reach out to some of you individually to establish a secure line.”

“But what about Dr. Stallard?” Quinn asked over the leaders’ frequency.

“What did I say about comms?” Bronn responded, raising his voice. “That’s an order. Stand by.”

By organizing everyone, Bronn was both slowing them down for Sara’s sake and saving their lives. It wouldn’t last, though. The Stolguard facility team, especially once backed by Colonel Torbeth and his forces from the nearby Air Force base, could perform an unstoppable push down here with explosives, Class B and C subjects, and sheer numbers of drones and soldiers. And her threat over the radio was partially a bluff; her fight against Fallon and her team had already drained most of her energy.

She looked down at Romulus. One of his legs had been shredded apart, and other major injuries covered his body through his broken armor. With this much damage, he’d probably bleed to death before he could be stabilized. She crouched down next to him, feeling nauseous at how much pain he must be in, and pulled off his helmet. “Do you want to try to live, or should I make it quick?” she whispered. “I’m sorry, Rom.”

“Pl . . . please . . . live,” he gasped. His face was smeared with blood.

Sara nodded and set the helmet down beside him. It seemed like the wrong choice to her, but at least she’d asked. She stood back up and looked around. Never in her life had she been down here, and her splitting headache and side pain made her disoriented.

There was the stairwell, the industrial elevator, a door that read—hell, it was hard to even focus on reading the words—Maintenance, another marked Restrooms, and a large set of double doors labeled Cold Storage. Rubble from the stairwell lay strewn across the cracked concrete floor.

Sara reached out with a focus to grab a piece of metal railing from the stairwell rubble, twisted it into a U with her other focus, and rammed it into the elevator doors to lock them together. None of this would hold against a real push, but it would prevent stragglers from easily coming down in the meantime.

She listened to the two single doors, then peeked into them one at a time to make sure nobody was there. She set her sights on the double doors next. They were button-operated and would make some noise, but there was no other way.

She pressed and entered, ready to shield herself.

This was a mortuary of some sort, chilly, smelling of formaldehyde and antiseptics. Emmett stood with his hands already up. A younger female lab assistant next to him did the same. They must have heard the fight with Raphael’s team and knew she was coming. Next to them lay Zarina’s body, naked and half-covered by a sheet, cut open on a wheeled metal table. Emmett seemed to be overseeing the assistant performing Zarina’s autopsy. A woman Sara herself had killed just days ago.

“Emmett,” Sara said, nodding. She was trying, despite everything, to sound peaceful. A monster pretending to be human. Dusty, bloody, burnt, and practically staggering at this point, she wondered what she must look like to them. She glanced up at the ceiling camera and crushed it.

Emmett winced at the sound and nodded back. “Sara.” His voice was tense. Nervous. He glanced down at the burnt side of her vest and tightened his jaw.

She scanned the room. “Open your lab coats. Do either of you have weapons?”

“Of course not,” Emmett said. With slow and deliberate movements, he held his lab coat wide open, and so did his assistant. No signs of concealed guns on their hips or inner pockets.

“Did Stallard come through here?” Sara asked, still breathing hard.

Emmett hesitated, then gave a conflicted shake of his head. Sara held his gaze for several seconds, but he said nothing more.

“He did,” the assistant said, breaking the tension.

Emmett looked down and exhaled.

Sara looked at the assistant. A storage closet stood behind her. “Open that,” Sara said, pointing.

The assistant glanced at Emmett, who nodded, and she turned and pulled open the door. It was nothing, filled only with equipment.

“Anything else I should know?” Sara asked. She eyed Emmett, trying and failing to sound casual. “Just tell me. Please.”

Emmett studied her for a long moment. “Sara . . . I can’t,” he said eventually.

“You’re a doctor,” Sara said. “Romulus is dying outside that door. Bleeding out fast. Tell me who else came through here. Then I’ll let you out there to help him. I’m not your enemy.”

Emmett sighed, looked back up at the broken camera, then met her gaze again. “It was Thane and Marcus,” he said. “But it’s cold in there, very cold, so you’ll be weakened.”

He put his arms down and reached for medical supplies before she even said he could. He’d always been able to read her well; he had known her all her life. His lab assistant hesitated, taking in Emmett’s actions, and then looked back at Sara. Sara nodded, and the assistant put her arms down and set to work with him.

Fallon and some other subjects viewed Stallard as their father for all practical purposes. Sara had never felt any such bond. But she was young enough that people like Emmett and Bronn were almost like uncles—older role models she’d known since her earliest memories, and who’d always shown kindness.

After half a minute of preparation, Emmett and his assistant walked past her toward where Romulus lay dying. A dark thought crossed her mind as they did.

Emmett ranked so highly here, basically Stallard’s number two, and she imagined him of all people being the one whom showing mercy to would come back to haunt her. What if he did have a gun, or some concentrated poison? It wasn’t like she’d checked that thoroughly. And what if Bronn, despite what he said on the radio, was secretly sending everyone down here right now, rather than waiting for Colonel Torbeth? What if Fallon woke up and stopped Clare from getting to the server room? What if Carter got back up and was the one to shoot her on the way out?

One of these people she’d let live somewhere in the building would probably surprise her with her death, directly or indirectly. If that was the case, well, she couldn’t help it.

She could, however, hedge her bets.

“Emmett,” she said, and he paused in the doorway. “When this is over, can you reach out to a colonel named Asim Rahal and tell him some of what happened here today? Off the record, at least. He’s at Army Counterintelligence. And . . . thank you. For all those times you treated me well.”

Emmett furrowed his brow, then nodded and let the door close behind him. A heavy weight settled in her chest at the thought that this might be the last time she’d see him, though she’d always known her affection for him was mostly one-sided. He was the closest thing she had to a parent, but he had a whole life and family outside this place, and she was one of many subjects he showed kindness to. It wasn’t like they’d ever talked much.

She sighed and looked around the room. Aside from the storage closet that they’d already proven to be empty, there was a set of double doors labeled Cold Storage 1. An empty coat rack stood beside them. Why had Stallard and Marcus come this way? It would clearly lead to a dead end.

When she pressed the button, the double doors opened into a small insulation room. Then, as she pressed the button on the wall inside that area, the doors closed behind her, and the next set of double doors opened into a cold, large warehouse, with seven aisles of storage extending into the room.

At the far side through the middle aisle, another set of double doors was closing, which meant someone had just gone through. She looked to her right and left, then trudged down the middle aisle toward the doors, crushing the cameras on the ceiling along the way.

These doors had Cold Storage 2 written on them. She glanced through the window. Stallard or whoever had gone through had already gotten past the next insulation room that she could see. She pressed the button to open the doors, then pressed the button in the insulation room to open the next set. Once again, the doors behind her closed. But as the new ones opened, she was blasted by cold so intense that it almost burned. She stepped back, shocked.

Involuntary shivers ran through her body as the insulation room grew colder and colder, far deeper than any winter she’d ever known.

Would she even be able to use her telekinesis here?

She unholstered her pistol and held it to her side. That’s why Stallard came down here, she realized.

“Stallard!” she shouted. “Let Marcus go. It’s over.”

“Sara?” Marcus’s voice came from deep inside the room, from somewhere behind the shelves of storage. “Are you here to kill me too? I don’t want to die.”

“I’d never hurt you, Marcus. I want to help you.”

She listened, growing colder, trying to hear a response through the constant refrigerator hum. Like the previous warehouse, this one was vast and had seven aisles of storage. From the entrance, she was looking straight down the middle aisle. Dressed as she was, she couldn’t linger too much longer. Her arms were bare, and the temperature felt like death. Hushed speaking came from deep inside and slightly to the right, as far as she could tell.

“What lies have you told him, Stallard?”

“Only the truth, C17,” Stallard said back. “That you killed your fellow subjects, including Damien. He has seen some of the clips, and they speak for themselves.”

Wrath surged through her. “Marcus, I didn’t kill Damien! I came to free you from those painful tests Stallard makes you do. Can you come out to me, or is he stopping you?”

Silence.

“Stallard, final warning. The tests you do with Class D are more dangerous than you realize. Don’t make me do this. Surrender yourself and let him go for his own good. For everyone’s good.”

More silence.

Well, there went the last of her possible exit strategies—using Stallard as a live hostage to get out of here. There was no way she’d be able to fight through whatever forces were up in the facility now, preparing to breach down here. Especially in her injured, drained state. There were so many lasers and so little cover around the grounds of the facility, and they’d use the chokepoint of the central stairwell and elevator shaft to prevent her from even getting back up to the surface.

Her shivers grew more violent. It was now or never. She’d come this far and wasn’t about to turn coward now.

Holding her pistol out with both hands, she stepped into the vast room and turned right. As she walked, she glanced to her left down each of the three aisles on that side, surveilling the area before heading deeper in. She reached the last aisle without having seen Stallard or the boy; they were probably hiding behind one of the shelf-ends on the deep side of the room.

As a test, she tried to mentally crush one of the ceiling cameras, but she couldn’t manage it. She could mentally tear its power cord, though, and did the same for the three others she saw.

The ridiculous temperature of this place made her as weak as she used to be; it was nearly impossible to pull energy out of the air. She wouldn’t be able to stop bullets or crush weapons here, and Stallard was certainly armed. With this extreme cold, and tired and hurt as she was, she could feel her life draining away by the second. Her fingers had already gone numb on the pistol.

She walked back toward the middle aisle near the entrance where she’d started, again looking down each aisle on this side of the room as she went.

She wanted to keep sight of the double doors in case Stallard tried to sneak himself and Marcus around to them while she headed deeper in. So, she crept down the middle aisle toward the deep side of the room, pistol up, frequently looking back over her shoulder at the doors.

There were gaps on some of the shelves on either side of her that someone could hide in or slip through from an adjacent aisle, so she peeked into them as she passed by to make sure Stallard wasn’t waiting for her with a surprise shot. She’d never set foot in here before, while he probably knew every square inch of it by heart.

When she neared the end of the aisle, she stayed close to the shelf to the right, angling to see more and more of the area on the left shelf-end, around the corner. Nobody was there. She burst around the shelf corner to the right, ready to fire.

Marcus stood alone in a heavy coat, hiding behind the right shelf-end, and flinched back at the sight of her. He was so small for a thirteen-year-old, and the adult-sized parka he wore draped down nearly to the floor.

“Where is he?” she asked, voice hollow.

Marcus’s eyes widened, and he looked up at something behind her right shoulder. She glanced back, breath catching in her throat, but it was already too late.

“Goodbye, C17,” Stallard said from behind as he raised an assault rifle straight at her head. He must have slipped through one of the shelf gaps and snuck up behind her from the same aisle she’d come down, like she’d worried might happen. He pulled the trigger.

For a long time, she’d looked forward to death—the end of a frustrating existence. Damien’s escape plan had given her a brief week of optimism, but then his death had finished her off inside. Deep down, when she’d decided to return to this place, she knew she’d die here.

But now, face-to-face with it, she wanted to live.

Somewhere along the way, whether it was Jitters’s and Aisha’s care, playing with Scorpio, arguing with Asim, sipping tea with Ava, falling asleep with Damien’s mimic, or seeing Jessica’s love for her son, something had woken back up inside of her.

It was hope, maybe. She’d finally seen the outside world.

Yet, she knew what she had to do. It didn’t feel sad; it felt right. All was well, even though she wouldn’t be.

A dozen of the rifle’s bullets came out with a deafening bang, but they stopped midair between Stallard and herself.

Stallard’s eyes went wide. He staggered back, nearly stumbled over, and dropped the rifle. For the first time in her life, Sara saw real fear in him. Filled with adrenaline, these seconds stretched out for her, and probably for him, too. She couldn’t help but enjoy his expression.

Since the air was too cold, she had extracted her own body heat for energy. Right from the blood in her veins. A final energy source, but one that would kill her to use. With it, she’d shielded herself from his shots using her left focus.

With her right focus, she grabbed the bullets and held them aloft as she stared at Stallard’s face. Using the last of her blood’s heat, she mentally thrust them back at him, faster than they’d come out of his gun. Back through his head and chest, a dozen holes. He was dead before his ruined body hit the floor, his heavy coat sprawling around him.

Sara dropped to her hands and knees, then fell onto her side, clutching her arms to her chest, frigid down to her core. Her heart was failing. Her legs lost feeling, and then her whole body went numb. As her still-open eyes lost vision, a tiredness that felt different from sleep washed over her.

“I love you, Marcus. I’m sorry I scared you,” she whispered, hearing the boy come over.

She smiled and closed her eyes. It was better to die wanting more than to die feeling bitter about what had been. As her consciousness faded away, she felt at peace.







Chapter 48



Asim received the message he’d been waiting for Damien to send. Time to hold up his end of this shit show.

It would take a while to comb through the data, but from Damien’s analysis, it looked like they had the relevant part of the Stolguard facility’s database, including detailed records of tests, missions, and scientific details. Even Stallard’s personal logs. They separately had footage from Sara’s perspective for the early part of her attack, including recordings of Fallon’s threats about Clare.

If Asim released this to the public or admitted that he had foreknowledge of Sara’s attack on the facility, he’d be charged with treason. So, he’d lie and see if he could get away with it. A man needed to take risks when he thought it was the right thing to do.

No news outlets had reported anything about the attack on the Stolguard facility, and no official word had come down through the military. Suppressed, of course. It’d been over two hours since Sara began her infiltration, which should’ve lasted half an hour if successful, depending on how long it took her to find Clare first. Sara was either dead or captured; if she’d gotten out somehow, he would’ve likely heard from her by now. Damien himself still hadn’t heard anything either, which said everything there was to know.

Asim felt bad for the woman, but she had chosen this for herself. At Damien’s insistence, she’d promised during their planning session that she would try to get out if she could, but they all knew it wasn’t likely. Asim would make sure to find out the details of her fate, one way or another. First, though, it was time to make sure it wasn’t all for nothing.

He picked up the phone and made a call.

“Major General Scholl’s office,” her secretary answered. “Colonel Rahal?”

“The one and only,” he said. “I need to speak to the general in person immediately. Absolute highest priority. National scale. I don’t mean to go around Davis, but I’m already here at INSCOM for some meetings and he’s over at the Pentagon. I need to report this to a superior sooner than I can get over there.”

“One moment,” she said. Seconds later, she came back. “The general can see you in five.”

Asim was already on his way to the elevator. He cracked his neck in both directions as he waited for the doors to open. Riding up, he rehearsed his lies. He strode past the secretary as she nodded to him, then knocked on the general’s door.

“Come in,” Scholl said from behind the heavy wood and decorative trim.

Asim entered and saluted. “Ma’am.”

“At ease. This better be good, Colonel. I delayed an important call for this.”

“Well, it’s not good, but it’s critical, ma’am.”

“Tell me.”

“I believe there’s been another attack by Jade, this time right at the heart of the Stolguard facility.”

Scholl nodded. “I was notified by General Rodriguez an hour ago, but his team is still crafting the narrative. This time they got her. Jade’s dead. She did damage, and Thane Stallard himself was killed, but it’s over.”

Asim wasn’t surprised, but it still felt like a gut punch to hear it out loud. “Unfortunately ma’am, I have additional news on it that they might not have. Most of their data was leaked.”

“What?” Scholl’s voice sharpened. He’d never seen her eyes go wide like that before.

“I received this message from what I believe is a mimic of a deceased subject from that facility. Look, ma’am.” He held out his phone and played the message. It was a video of Damien’s mimic, in VR, which Asim had secretly preplanned with him.

“Colonel Rahal. My name was Damien,” the video began. “I was a test subject at the Stolguard facility. Sara, or Jade as you might know her, recorded part of her infiltration today. She also sent me petabytes of core data from the servers. Lists of missions. Full subject genomes. And more. I haven’t released it publicly yet, but I will if my reasonable demands aren’t met. I’ll be in contact soon with more details. Here’s a sample, with provable metadata.”

The video cut to footage from Sara’s augmented reality sunglasses, including the part where Fallon held Clare hostage, followed by a fight breaking out between Sara, Fallon, and Jolce, with Jolce gruesomely splattering apart from what looked like an invisible shockwave. The video ended as Santiago broke through a door and shot toward the camera while his armored head imploded in a spray of blood. Sara’s scream was the last thing on the audio as the sunglasses hit the floor and went offline.

It sure looked like Sara died there, but she must’ve gotten at least a little farther before they took her out, since the facility’s firewall had gone down several minutes later and the servers had begun transmitting then. Tough as nails, she was.

“This . . . this is catastrophic,” Scholl said, staring at the phone. “We have to alert the Army Chief immediately. Why did the mimic send this to you?”

“I made contact with Jade twice in recent weeks during my investigation. She was using one of her captives’ identity keys and VR avatar. I couldn’t prove it, and for security purposes I kept that detail close to the chest. So, I guess this mimic decided to reach out to me. His virtual features match one of the subjects’ bodies we found at the initial rest stop attack, ma’am.”

“You had contact with her and didn’t disclose it? You might get skewered for that, Colonel. There’ll be investigations.”

“I expected that, ma’am. But I wanted to make sure you had this mimic’s threat immediately.”



Two days later, Asim found himself repeating the story in the Pentagon to an assembly of top military officers, including General Rodriguez, who had flown in. Asim was under preliminary investigation by the Army’s Criminal Investigation Division, CID, for potential negligence or conspiracy, and they made a note of the whistleblower reports he’d filed as well. SOCOM was also applying a ton of pressure. He certainly looked complicit.

“Did you have any knowledge of the attack ahead of time?” asked Rodriguez’s investigator. A man named Major Duwain. He spearheaded the process for his general. Some other corners of the military seemed more sympathetic to Asim’s side of the matter. Before deciding who to blame, most of the top brass just wanted to understand what the hell had even happened.

“No, I did not,” Asim lied. “If anything, we suspected she might strike MacDill. We’ve had to split our resources across multiple regions.”

“Why did you withhold the fact that you had established virtual contact with the suspect in your intel-sharing agreement with the Stolguard facility?”

“Because the nature of the conversations with the suspect led me to potentially distrust the facility’s director, Thane Stallard, from a counterintelligence perspective. I wanted to keep the line of communication with the suspect open. However, I used intel learned from those conversations to issue warnings. I sent alerts for major facilities to acquire laser rifles after first speaking with her. And I had my team collect public social media posts that matched the types of language that the suspect used in our conversations, and made them known to the Stolguard facility, so they’d have the intel without me revealing my source, sir. She was concerned about a specific threat involving the facility’s Class D subjects, and I made that known to them. I also included the suspect’s warnings about Class D in my report to the Joint Chiefs after she murdered General Price, from the brief conversation I overheard between them.”

“Did anyone else on your team know you made contact with the suspect?”

“Not that I know of. I met her alone in VR. My team only knows that I have some clandestine sources.” Another lie. Ava, Flanagan, and Brooks would be kept clean from this mess if possible. The rest of his team had been truly in the dark about that part. “And I would remind the assembly here that I was the one that arrested her in the first place. Not other agencies. It was partly because of the second meeting with the suspect that I directed more resources back to Brooklyn, where we found her.”

“Do you still stand by your whistleblower case?”

“I do. And the initial footage the mimic sent me further confirms it. The video’s metadata shows that it came from a pair of augmented reality sunglasses that belonged to a woman named Martha Twill. She and her husband reported false imprisonment and theft a few days ago from their yacht, by someone matching the suspect’s description. That metadata would be extremely hard to fake, especially on such short notice. It shows major ethical breaches at the facility, including one subject holding another subject hostage and threatening her with a violent death, even though they were on the same team, sir.”

“That’s rather minimal relative to everything else, isn’t it, Colonel?”

“Designating human beings born on US soil as noncitizens, then treating them inhumanely,” Asim said. “Threats of torture, death. I wouldn’t call that minimal, sir, but there’s more. This morning, the mimic sent me highlights of some of the broader data, which I’ve shared with my superiors. It confirms with extensive evidence that in addition to their foreign operations, several Class C subjects were sent on domestic assassinations, including against certain government whistleblowers, protest organizers, corporate targets, two members of Congress, multiple district judges, and even a Supreme Court justice. I believe the rabbit hole here needs to be ripped open and examined, sir. Multiple generals could be complicit. Maybe higher.”

“That is . . . alarming, Colonel. But if this investigation finds credible evidence that you collaborated with the suspect or had foreknowledge of the Stolguard facility attack—which resulted in seventeen fatalities, including the suspect—you’ll be court-martialed and face potential life imprisonment for treason. If you wish to make a confession before evidence is found to substantiate charges along those lines, that would be factored into sentencing. Is there anything you wish to say, Colonel?”

You only killed sixteen? Not bad, Sara. That was downright restraint compared to the number he’d feared to hear. “I stand by the truth of my statements, sir. I love my country. I did what I thought was right, purely to keep a communication line open and make sure I took all potential threats seriously. Not just the obvious threat from her, but also the threats she warned about. I had no foreknowledge of her attack on the facility.”

“From your knowledge of the case, what do you recommend we do regarding the mimic’s terrorist threat to release sensitive data?”

“That seems to be a mimic of a deceased Class D subject. An extension of a victim, in other words. I wouldn’t quite classify it as a terrorist threat. More like an aggressive whistleblower. Even though I cannot condone the mimic’s threat to release the data publicly, I see why it’s taking that approach. Given the highlights I’ve already received and shared with you, I recommend negotiating with it. I do believe there are severe ethical breaches at the facility and at SOCOM that potentially extend to the highest levels of government. That’s why I filed my whistleblower report in the first place, before this attack even happened.”

Major Duwain leaned to his side and whispered to General Rodriguez, probably deciding what course of questioning to take next. They likely hadn’t expected Asim to call out their command so directly.

He looked around the room of high-ranking officers and their various support staff. It was time to make this abundantly clear in case not all of them were getting it yet. Bad cop, good cop.

“One more thing, if I may,” Asim said.

Duwain turned back toward him. “Yes, Colonel?”

“I intend to keep pursuing my whistleblower case through formal, legal channels. About everything. The inhumane treatment of subjects, the treasonous domestic assassinations, and the potential Class D cybersecurity threat that nearly went haywire. If I’m imprisoned, my colleagues will be prepared to carry the whistleblower case forward while I contest the charges. Given the mimic’s data leak threat, and based on the wording of its demands so far, I believe it will be satisfied as long as we thoroughly pursue the evidence wherever it leads and prosecute accordingly. Which, I trust, is what all those present want to do anyway.”

Asim took a deep breath and met the eyes of various top brass, one by one. After all, a man should stand by his principles, even when it drew uncomfortable attention. Someone had to spearhead this mess. Might as well be him.



When Ava strolled into the Stolguard facility’s main building, her first thought was that it wasn’t as creepy as she expected. And that was a bummer.

The forested grounds were nothing special, and the main structure, while enormous, was little more than a research building the size of a shopping mall. She already knew that of course, from aerial photos, but even the inside was . . . kind of boring. Just white and sterile.

She was one of three people who’d arrived as agency representatives: herself for ACI, Colonel Bright for General Rodriguez’s command, and Ms. Mageth for the CIA. Colonel Rahal couldn’t come himself; he was stuck at the Pentagon, performing his part of the plan. But he’d made her promise not to say anything weird about aliens here, and she was trying her best.

“The facility was damaged from the attack two days ago, but we already ran safety checks and will of course avoid the areas that are considered unstable,” said their escort. She was a middle-aged woman named Dr. Michelle Verdant, the facility’s head of subject well-being.

“I was told Ackerman would see us directly,” Colonel Bright said. He was referring to Dr. Emmett Ackerman, the facility’s acting director for the past two days, following Dr. Stallard’s death. Rodriguez’s office and the CIA had both demanded to come and see the aftermath of the incident, and for some reason Dr. Ackerman had personally reached out to Colonel Rahal for an invitation to come as well.

The woman paused, then smiled. “Of course. I’m here to take you to him. Right this way.” She brought them through a series of corridors toward a large industrial elevator and ushered everyone in, then followed. “Dr. Ackerman is ready to meet you in our mortuary, to verify some of your questions in person.”

The doors closed, and after a longer-than-expected ride down, they opened onto a heavily damaged sub-basement area. Even the elevator doors had two holes in them. The concrete floor was practically shattered, and six construction workers were shoveling rubble aside. It was only when Ava stepped out and looked to the side that she could see the full scope of the damage—the stairwell here had completely collapsed, and that had been the source of most of the rubble. A woman in her twenties with those cat-like green eyes and brown hair tied back into a loose bun leaned against the wall, watching them as they exited the elevator.

“This is the VIP tour,” Dr. Verdant said to the green-eyed woman.

The woman nodded and knocked on the set of double doors labeled Cold Storage. “The tour’s here, Emmett!” she shouted, then turned back to the group and smiled.

A moment later, the doors opened. A man with graying brown hair and blue eyes stood in the doorway wearing a lab coat, with a female assistant about Ava’s age beside him. Both of them had bags under their eyes.

“Welcome,” he said with a tired smile, glancing around the group. “I’m Dr. Emmett Ackerman. You can just call me Emmett. Colonel Bright, is it?” He held out a hand, and the colonel shook it.

“Ms. Mageth, welcome.” He shook her hand.

“And you’re Special Agent Zhou, of Army Counterintelligence? I’m sorry Colonel Rahal couldn’t make it, but I’m glad he was able to send someone on his behalf. He spoke very highly of you.” He reached out, and Ava shook his hand.

She glanced past him. Now this room was starting to look sufficiently creepy for her taste. The sort of place where aliens might be kept. And this was the type of man who would know about them. It was always the soft-spoken ones who knew the creepiest stuff. She could almost feel the secrets within him, right under the surface. He was hiding something.

“This is one of my lab assistants, Rachel, and I see you’ve met my acting bodyguard, Clare,” Emmett said, gesturing them inside. He put on a more somber expression as they walked in. “This is our subject mortuary. I understand you wanted to see the deceased before they undergo dissection or are put into deep storage. Of course, the non-subject deceased personnel have been taken care of at external mortuaries, and so this is only for the three subjects who died in the attack, since they are classified as our facility’s property, as ill-advised as that term might be.” He shrugged apologetically. “I must warn you; their deaths were quite graphic.”

“Yes, yes,” Colonel Bright said.

When no objections came, Emmett walked up and put his hand on one of the handles on the mortuary wall. “This is Santiago, or B8 officially, who died from head trauma,” he said, and pulled out a sliding table from the wall. He drew away part of the sheet. Ava covered her mouth at the sight, while Colonel Bright remained stoic. It was the massive olive-skinned man whom she’d seen at Fort Hamilton, his head now reduced to a pile of meat and bone. Emmett slid the table back in.

“Oh my,” Ms. Mageth said.

Emmett nodded. “This next one is Jolce, or C6, who died from blunt-force trauma to, well, everywhere. Friendly fire, unfortunately.” He pulled out a table holding an absolute mess: a bloody partial rib cage, several red-spotted bone pieces of various sizes, two fully intact feet and shins of a light-skinned woman with a toe tag on one of them, and several large jars of red gore.

“What the hell?” Bright asked.

“One of our own subject commanders was a bit overeager to take out the attacker and missed, it seems,” Emmett said, shaking his head. “Tragic.”

He slid that table back in, then tightened his jaw. “And last, the attacker who caused all this,” he said. “She was officially known as C17, but she called herself Sara. You likely know her as Jade. She died of hypothermia, as well as shock from an abdominal laser blast. The late Dr. Stallard bravely led her into a trap in our deep cold storage warehouse, which impaired her abilities. I’ll be dissecting her brain this week to better understand how she could do the things she did.”

As Emmett pulled out the table and moved aside the sheet, Ava’s heart sank. There in front of her rested Sara’s body. The reddish-brown hair dye and side-swept bangs made her look different, but from her face, scars, and emaciated figure, it was indeed Sara. She had several new injuries as well, including a gory burn on her left side and a host of smaller cuts and bruises. Her right shoulder wound still looked somewhat fresh from her torture, and she was missing some fingernails on her right hand.

She looked so young now, lying there without her armor, eyes closed, peaceful. Ava thought about how her own mother would frame it, even if she didn’t really believe it herself. She’d say that Sara would wake up from this life, as if from a bad dream, and realize all was as it should be.

Ava looked up at Clare. Her eyes seemed tense. From things Sara had said, the two of them had been best friends. She had to be heartbroken over this. Although she tried to hold it back, Ava’s own eyes welled at the thought. Clare inclined her head slightly, a sense of curiosity in her expression.

“Good riddance,” Colonel Bright said. “What a mess.”

Emmett nodded and sighed as he draped the sheet over the body, then slid the table back into the wall. Clare shifted her gaze to Bright with a more piercing stare, those dangerous eyes out of place in such a kind face.

“Now,” Emmett said, “Ms. Verdant can show you upstairs, where most of the damage occurred, and can take you to the infirmary if you wish to see or speak with our injured subjects. I assure you they’re being well taken care of. I’ll finish here and meet you up in my office shortly thereafter, where I’ll be happy to answer any of your remaining questions.”

Oh, Ava would put that offer to the test. And regardless of what Colonel Rahal had said, there would indeed be a question about aliens. Sorry, sir.



Minutes later, after the tour left, Sara’s table was pulled out from the wall again.

“You played that nicely,” Emmett said. “This one made me nervous as hell, so hopefully that’s the last time. Let’s get that side bandaged up again.”

Sara opened her eyes. “I’m . . . freezing,” she whispered. Talking was still hard.

Emmett’s assistant, Rachel, came over and wrapped her back up in an electric heated blanket, careful to avoid touching her side, while Clare stepped up, grinning with relief, and gripped her hand.

Sara met her eyes and smiled as best as she could. She was still too weak to move much at all. Between the heavy painkillers and the heartbeat-slowing serum Emmett had injected her with, it didn’t take much effort to play dead other than holding her breath. Her body felt pleasantly numb, with a buzzing, almost floating sensation. Strangers seeing her half-naked didn’t even matter at this point; details like that felt so trivial after everything else.

When she had collapsed in the cold two days earlier, her blood itself frigid to the core, Marcus had been unable to carry her. Instead, he ran for help and found Emmett, who was still in the sub-basement near the broken stairwell, stabilizing Romulus.

According to Emmett, he followed Marcus and found her pulseless body, carried her out to this mortuary, wrapped her in an electric blanket, and administered CPR. Her pulse came back, weakly, though she remained unconscious. Using Fallon’s radio, which Sara still had with her, Emmett reported that both she and Stallard had died in battle, and requested assistance to clear the stairwell rubble so they could evacuate Romulus to the medical bay.

Under command of the Air Force’s Colonel Torbeth, the forces breached down to the sub-basement ten minutes later. Emmett had made use of that window. He displayed Sara’s “corpse” in the mortuary next to Zarina’s and Stallard’s, as if she were one of the dead. And in the two days since, after she had woken and with Clare keeping watch for him, Emmett made Sara play dead for other staff who came through, whether to bring Santiago’s body and Jolce’s guts, or just to check on things.

It turned out, Sara realized, that one of her acts of mercy had come back to save her.







Epilogue





Six Months Later


Asim relaxed on his favorite virtual beach, sipping a can of flavored sparkling water. The salty breeze from the crystalline sea and the sound of gulls amid its waves blended nicely to ease his mind.

He came here less often now, not even once a month. But for some reason, he needed it this evening. It’d been a particularly stressful week, capping a particularly stressful series of months.

Because of his whistleblowing and secret coordination with Damien’s mimic to threaten a public release of the Stolguard facility’s data, there had been countless hearings requiring Asim’s participation, and the facility had undergone major reforms.

All subjects could refuse to participate in tests if they wished, and at age eighteen they could choose to leave the facility entirely. Several, including Clare, had already stopped their missions. Others, such as Fallon, had chosen to stay in the US special forces. The newest classes would have all those choices from the start as they grew up, and the creation of any new classes beyond those was paused for now.

Stallard’s permanent replacement, Dr. Emmett Ackerman, supported the reforms, which made the process far smoother than it otherwise would have been. One less headache, at least. He hadn’t fought every step of the way like his predecessor had, and higher-ups like General Rodriguez could no longer shield the program from scrutiny.

Especially not Rodriguez himself: he had been arrested on charges of conspiracy, tied to several of the domestic assassination missions, along with two officers on his staff and three senior CIA members. Asim’s team at ACI—along with the FBI, CID, and others—were still working through the web of connections there, and probably would be for years.

The science behind Class D had been distributed to several other scientific bodies within the country under top-secret agreements, for further safety reviews. Damien’s mimic even worked with some of them, elaborating on the dangers of his experience. That compromise was considered the best of both worlds by the specialists; it hadn’t released the method of creation to the public yet, but it allowed more sets of eyes to examine it and run various game theory analyses on it.
